**GILLEY**
Stacey Dawson.  The one nobody gets to brag about. Yet.

He stretches, cocky as hell, running a hand through his hair. This isn’t loneliness. It’s *sport*.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
It wasn’t about Stacey. It wasn’t even about Jeremy Dawson.  It was about winning. About always, always being the story everyone tells the next day.

He dials, grinning, voice velvet.

**GILLEY** (into phone, low and playful)
Stacey?

Yeah, it’s Gilley.

I know.

You too.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
Fire’s still burning.  I don’t miss the girl. I miss the thrill.

(beat)
Let’s see how high this can go.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S LIVING ROOM – NIGHT**

The fan hums. Old carpet smells faintly of cigarettes. On the coffee table: sleeves, dice, two worn decks.

**STACEY DAWSON** sits cross-legged on the couch, black nails drumming her cards, lipstick like a dare. **GILLEY** leans against the couch on the floor, barefoot, shirtless, soda glass sweating in his hand.

**STACEY** (laying down a Swamp, sly)
You gonna make me beg?

**GILLEY** (grinning)
Only if you want me to.

**STACEY**
Not my style.

She summons a wraith. He counters instantly, too smug by half. She only smiles wider.

**STACEY**
You always do that.  Cut things short. Stop them before they matter.

**GILLEY** (shrugs)
I call it taste.

**STACEY**
I call it fear.

The game tightens — her patience against his interruptions, a duel in slow motion. Every move is less about cards than about *them.*  Finally, she takes it. By inches, by hours. He shrugs like he expected it. He didn’t.  She gathers her deck, rises, finds her keys. He reaches to collect the dice. For a moment—her fingers brush his, light as smoke, gone as soon as it lands.

**STACEY**
Tell the band I said hi.  And tell Kathy she looked on fire the other night.

**GILLEY** (measured)
She gives a lot of looks.

**STACEY** (a beat, then)
None like that.

She leaves. Quiet, deliberate. The room exhales with her absence.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
She played black. I played blue.  Neither of us played red.

(beat)
Maybe that’s why it never burns.  Not yet.

---

## **INT. PRE-OP ROOM – DAY – 8:06 A.M.**

**JEFF** lies in the hospital bed, gown gaping, IV taped to the crook of his arm. His hair is pressed down by a blue surgical cap. Only one sock—nobody knows where the other’s gone. The pre-op world hums: cart wheels, sliding glass, nurses moving like a well-oiled pit crew.

The anesthesiologist checks the last syringe—clear, labeled. **DR. GOLDBERG**, the ENT, reads **JEFF**’s chart, unhurried and perfectly bored.

**JEFF** turns, half-fogged from Versed but stubbornly lucid.

**JEFF**
Hey, uh…before I go under, I got a question.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
Of course.

**JEFF**
Is it true you use skin from behind the knee to rebuild an eardrum?

**DR. GOLDBERG** (smiling)
Actually? Good question.

(beat)
Yeah. Sometimes. Sometimes behind the ear, sometimes behind the knee. Depends how much we need. It’s fascia—thin connective tissue—not skin, but yeah.

**JEFF**
So I’ll be hearing through my knee.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
Not quite, but that’s the spirit.

**JEFF**
Weird.

(beat)
Any, uh, phantom knee sounds?

**DR. GOLDBERG** (chuckling)
You’ll be the first to know.

**JEFF**
Great.

(pause)
Knock me out.

He glances at the ceiling, trying to sound casual.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
Tell **KATHY** I didn’t cry or say anything weird.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
You’ll be legendary.

**JEFF**
Tell her I was cool.

The anesthesia hits. His eyes stutter, breathing slows.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Knee in the ear. Wild what a body borrows from itself.

(beat)
Like a band. Like a garage. Scraps and stitches. Somehow—it works.

---

## **INT. HOSPITAL WAITING ROOM – 8:22 A.M.**

Lights are cruel. The vending machine glows like a portal to hell. TV on mute—weather, traffic, whatever.

**MRS. EVANS** knits with relentless determination, needles clicking. She glances up as **GILLEY** ambles in—hoodie, sunglasses, coffee stolen from some other floor. He lands in a chair like he owns the lease.

**MRS. EVANS** (eyebrows raised)
Well. That’s a surprise.

**GILLEY** (shrugging, grinning)
Morning, ma’am. Not selling anything, promise.

He slides down in the seat, legs sprawled.

**MRS. EVANS**
Didn’t expect you here. Practice is cancelled. **JEFF** told everyone.

**GILLEY**
I know. I’m not here for the band.

(beat)
I’m here ‘cause I owe the guy.

**MRS. EVANS**
Owe him?

**GILLEY**
Last summer. I had this eye thing—bad, like, crawling-in-the-dark bad. Couldn’t look at light, couldn’t do shit. Only place I could stand was the hall closet.

(beat)
**JEFF** found out, came over, crawled in with me. Brought a flashlight that barely worked and a deck of cards. We played made-up games. Barely talked. Just…sat there.

He sips coffee, eyes on the floor.

**GILLEY (CONT’D)**
Since then, guy’s got a seat in the back of my heart. Whether I like it or not.

(beat)
So. I’m here. Paying it forward. Sitting. Waiting.

**MRS. EVANS**
Well.

(beat)
This is the nicest thing I’ve ever seen you do, **JEREMY GILLEY**.

**GILLEY**
Don’t tell anyone. I got a reputation.

**MRS. EVANS**
Too late.

(beat)
But for what it’s worth…you did good.

**GILLEY**
I’m decent when no one’s looking.

**MRS. EVANS**
Just don’t tell **KATHY ESPICH**. She’ll think you’re evolving.

**GILLEY**
If I ever evolve, shoot me on sight.

They sit in silence. The kind that’s earned, not given.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
Everybody needs a guy who’ll sit with you in the dark.  Some debts you don’t pay with money.

---

## **INT. RECOVERY ROOM – 11:15 A.M.**

Muted tones. Soft beeping. A partition curtain. The smell of antiseptic and grape-scented anesthesia masks.

**JEFF** blinks awake slowly. Eyes dry. Mouth dry. Brain still rebooting like a Commodore 128. His body, though, is sending a single, clear message: *feed me.*

**JEFF** (low, raspy)
…m’sandwich?

A **NURSE** appears, calm and competent.

**NURSE**
Hey there, welcome back. Everything went fine. Surgery was smooth. You’re in recovery now.

**JEFF** (grumpy)
Yeah okay. Great.

(beat)
Am I allowed to be hungry or is that illegal?

**NURSE**
We’ll get you something in just a second. Let’s check vitals first.

**JEFF**
Vitals are fine. Vitals want toast.

She laughs as she checks his BP.

**NURSE**
Pain?

**JEFF**
Mild.

(beat)
But my thirst is a medical emergency.

**NURSE**
We’ll start with water. Ice chips first.

**JEFF**
Jesus Christ. It’s like a spa run by prison guards.

**NURSE**
Your mom’s still in the waiting room. And a…Jeremy?

**JEFF** (nods, eyes shut)
Yeah. **GILLEY**. Probably strutting like he owns the hospital.

**NURSE**
Want them to come in?

**JEFF**
Only if one of them brought a sandwich.

She smiles and walks off.

**JEFF** slumps back. His hearing already feels different—cleaner, quieter, like static scraped away.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
They cut me open. Rebuilt a piece of me. Now I’m here.

(beat)
Still hungry. Still me.  Maybe…just a little more tuned in.

---

## **INT. RECOVERY ROOM – 1:23 P.M.**

**JEFF** sits upright, wrapped in white gauze like a mummy, bandage over his ear looping over the crown of his head and under the jaw. He looks like a helmeted squirrel—and not thrilled about it.

**DR. GOLDBERG** stands at the foot of the bed, clipboard in hand.

**GILLEY** and **MRS. EVANS** enter. **MRS. EVANS** gasps. **GILLEY** freezes.

**MRS. EVANS**
Oh honey…

**JEFF** (deadpan)
Hi Mom.

**GILLEY**
Dude.

(beat)
You look like you lost a fight with a roll of paper towels.

**JEFF**
Thanks for coming.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
The procedure went well—textbook. But so you all understand what we did…

(gestures to the bandage)
We made a small incision behind the ear, partially detached the outer ear, and temporarily attached it to the side of his face with surgical adhesive.

**GILLEY**
Wait. You sliced his ear off?

**DR. GOLDBERG**
Partially. Then we harvested a fascia graft from behind the knee, replaced one of the ossicles—the middle ear bones—with surgical wire, rebuilt the eardrum, stitched up the canal, and packed the inner ear.

**MRS. EVANS** (to JEFF, straight-faced)
You have an ear cheek.

**GILLEY**
That’s metal as hell.

**JEFF**
I feel like a ham sandwich somebody tried to reassemble.

**DR. GOLDBERG**
He can’t lift anything over ten pounds, avoid all exertion for a week, and absolutely no water in the ear.

**GILLEY**
No cannonballs. Got it.

**MRS. EVANS**
And you’re staying at my house. No argument. Guest bed is made. Pillows fluffed. Twice.

**JEFF**
Of course you did.

(beat)
What about music?

**DR. GOLDBERG**
No headphones. No loud noise. And definitely no garage practice.

**GILLEY**
What if we just play really soft, like acoustic blues?

**DR. GOLDBERG**
He can listen from another zip code.

**JEFF** (nods, resigned)
Cool.

**GILLEY**
For a guy who just had a piece of knee installed in his head, you’re holding up pretty well.

**JEFF**
It’s the hospital Jell-O. Gave me powers.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
They sliced my ear. Wired my bones. Stitched me together with glue and luck.  But I’m still here. Still grouchy. Still me.

(beat)
Just a little more patched up than yesterday.

---

# **CHAPTER SIX: THE SOUND BARRIER**
## **EXT. FRONT STREET WAREHOUSE – 4:02 A.M. – SATURDAY**

The street is dark, thick, sticky. Sodium lights buzz. The warehouse squats, silent, like a Korean War relic with metal roll-up doors shuddering in the breeze.

A single truck idles, headlights accusing the night.

**KATHY**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** drift in separately—but only by seconds.
Three zombies, same funeral.

**KATHY** (muttering)
I hate everything.

**JEREMY**
I hate you for being on time.

**BILL**
I haven’t seen the number four this early since I failed my AP Chem final.

**KATHY**
Shut up, **BILL**.

**BILL**
Respectfully.

They cluster at the dock. Nearby: a guy in jorts with a boiled egg, another kid chewing on the end of a Red Bull can.

**JEREMY**
Where’s my dad?

**KATHY**
Hopefully still asleep. Like a human.

**JEREMY**
Nope. He’s probably already halfway to the flight line, driving a golf cart full of Michelob.

**BILL**
What are we even doing?

**KATHY**
Beer. Kegs. Napkins. Loading up chalets so old men can drink overpriced vodka and watch F-16s pretend it’s patriotism.

**BILL**
That’s so bleak.

**JEREMY**
So’s my bank account. Two extra concert tickets don’t materialize out of guilt.

**KATHY**
I’d kill for a hashbrown and five hours of sleep.

**JEREMY**
You already sold your soul. This is just collections.

A forklift coughs to life. **FOREMAN** emerges, clipboard, five o’clock shadow, pure diesel.

**FOREMAN**
Let’s move, crew! You want that ticket, you earn it!

**JEREMY** (under breath)
Indentured servitude, but with more parking.

**KATHY**
Let’s go commit war crimes in the name of Miller Lite.

They trudge inside, three silhouettes against jaundiced light.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
While I was healing, they were hauling. While I was doped up, they were sweating in the dawn.  We all had our own ways of paying for the music.

---

## **INT. FRONT STREET WAREHOUSE – MANAGER’S OFFICE – MOMENTS LATER**

A door bangs open at the top of the steps.  **MR. EVANS** appears: tall, tucked polo, double-pager, and a grin so wide it could power a sump pump.

**MR. EVANS**
Morning, team!

Everyone groans in one exhausted chorus.

**MR. EVANS (CONT’D)**
Come on! It’s a beautiful day in the Miami Valley. Sun’s not even up, and we’re already winning!

**KATHY** (low, to **BILL**)
Why is he like this?

**BILL**
He bathes in black coffee and motivational posters.

**MR. EVANS**
Ready for the airport?

**JEREMY**
Dad. It’s four-oh-freaking-seven.

**MR. EVANS**
Exactly! Time waits for no keg! And guess what?

(beat, that salesman sparkle)
I’m driving.

They all freeze. There’s only one thing worse than being up at four…

**MR. EVANS (CONT’D)**
That’s right. Silver Bullet One.

**KATHY**
No!

**BILL**
You mean the rolling coffin with the wolf mural?

**JEREMY**
The one with the CB radio and captain’s chairs from the Nixon administration?

**MR. EVANS**
That’s the one. Tires rotated, tank full, spirit untouchable.

**KATHY**
Does the passenger door still fall off?

**MR. EVANS**
Only if you disrespect it.

**JEREMY**
Are you actually driving us onto Wright-Patt in that?

**MR. EVANS**
Hell yes I am.

(beat)
We’re bringing class, style, and a faint aroma of menthol to the Dayton Air Show.

They shuffle out, battered, blinking, half-awed.  There are worse ways to earn a ticket to the music. But not many.

---

## **EXT. LOADING DOCK – MOMENTS LATER**

There it is. **SILVER BULLET ONE**. Chrome trim. Rear axle sagging. CB antenna waving in the humid wind. The faded wolf mural howls at a dented moon. Side door chained and padlocked for “safety.” Engine idles like a Vietnam vet with PTSD.

**MR. EVANS**
Everybody in!

**JEFF (V.O.)**
While I was eating Jell-O and wondering if my face still worked…They were climbing into the Econoline of legend.

---

## **EXT. LOADING DOCK – 4:17 A.M. – MOMENTS LATER**

The crew stares at the van like it’s about to demand a blood sacrifice.  **MR. EVANS** stands proud, laminated badge swinging from his belt like it’s a VIP lanyard at the world’s worst music festival.

**MR. EVANS**
Oh—and just to clarify—Did you mean Dayton International Airport and not Wright-Patt?
Because we can’t get on base. Not without clearance, a background check, and a damn convincing story about hauling ice cream.

(beat)
BUT!

(holds up badge, triumphant)
I’ve got an Access All Areas pass. For the van. And for y’all!

**KATHY**
What does that even mean?

**MR. EVANS**
It means—once we drop off those pallets, hook up the taps, and roll out the trash bins—you are *unleashed* upon Dayton International Airport grounds.

**JEREMY**
Unleashed like dogs?

**BILL**
Unleashed like interns?

**MR. EVANS**
Unleashed like legends. Unlimited meal cards. Staff access. Hangars, chalets, beer tents, break areas, even the tarmac if you don’t cross the Thunderbirds.

**KATHY**
Do we get a map?

**MR. EVANS**
Improvise.

**JEREMY**
Oh my God.

**MR. EVANS**
It’s a bargain.  Two hours hauling. All day perks. Hot dogs. Sodas. Shady spots behind hangars. You wanna stand under a C-5 and feel spiritual? Boom—you’re in.

**KATHY**
If this is a scam, it’s the most charming one I’ve ever seen.

**MR. EVANS**
Scams don’t come with nachos and a folding chair near the flight line.

(beat)
Now get in the van before somebody else steals our fuel truck route.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
While I was recovering from having metal hammered into my head…My friends were about to work harder than ever—In exchange for nachos and freedom.

---

## **INT. SILVER BULLET ONE – 4:26 A.M. – MOVING**

Dashboard glow, cracked dome light, CB radio flickers blue.  Everyone is half-asleep, rattling in captain’s chairs bolted at suspect angles.  The windshield frames nothing but Ohio darkness.

**JEREMY** (squinting at the road)
Hey Dad?

**MR. EVANS**
Yeah, buddy?

**JEREMY**
Just a thought.  Why haven’t you turned the headlights on?

**MR. EVANS** (calm, glancing at dash)
Oh, they haven’t worked since Memorial Day.

**KATHY**
Excuse me what? I’m sorry—what?

**BILL**
Are we stealthing our way to the airport?

**MR. EVANS**
It’s fine. There’s enough streetlight to keep her between the lines.  Plus, those reflective stripes on the hood let folks know we’re coming.

**KATHY**
Reflective stripes?

**JEREMY**
You mean the duct tape you slapped on in June?

**MR. EVANS**
Exactly. That stuff’s rated for construction zones.

(beat)
We’re good.

**BILL**
We’re gonna die in this van. This is how the band ends.

**MR. EVANS** (cheerful)
If we die, we die legends. With access all areas!

**JEREMY**
You’re insane.

**MR. EVANS**
You say “insane,” I say “efficient underfunded logistics.”

**JEFF (V.O.)**
While I was sipping broth and pretending not to feel stitches in my skull…The band was careening across Dayton in a ghost van, no headlights, no shame—Led by a man powered by pure optimism and expired inspection stickers.

---

## **INT. SILVER BULLET ONE – STILL RUMBLING DOWN THE HIGHWAY – 4:31 A.M.**

The van rattles like a trash can in a hurricane. Windows fogged. CB mic sticky with spilled coffee. The engine hums, a chorus of loose bolts and half-remembered maintenance.

**JEREMY** white-knuckles the passenger seat, eyes locked ahead as **MR. EVANS** swings the van left, no headlights, no signal, just pure gut and *Ohio intuition*.

**MR. EVANS** (O.S.)
You just gotta feel the road, son. It’s like jazz. Tires tell you where to go.

**KATHY**, slouched in the back, arms crossed, leans toward **JEREMY**, voice so low it barely stirs the stale van air.

**KATHY** (quiet, dry)
Sometimes I can really tell that **JEFF** is your father’s son.

**JEREMY** (still staring forward)
What’s that supposed to mean?

**KATHY**
Means he’s calm in chaos. Doesn’t panic. Gets hurt and never says a word.

(beat)
Doesn’t know when to bail.

**JEREMY**
That’s not fair.

**KATHY**
It’s not mean, **JEREMY**.

(beat)
It’s just…true.

**MR. EVANS** (O.S.)
Hey! I found the high beams! Wait—nope, that’s the horn.

**HONK!**

The van blares into the empty dark.

**BILL**
This is a slow-motion hostage situation.

**KATHY** (smiling, almost fond)
Yup. And **JEFF** would never complain. He’d just sit through it. Same way he sits through **GILLEY**. And me.

(beat)
It’s kind of brave. Maybe a little sad.

**JEREMY**
He’s not sad.

**KATHY**
No. He’s not.

(beat, soft)
But sometimes, I wonder if he gets tired of being quiet just to keep the rest of us okay.

The van rolls on, wheels humming, silence growing.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
They say we inherit our parents’ bones.  But maybe we also inherit their silences.

---

## **INT. SILVER BULLET ONE – 4:44 A.M. – APPROACHING THE AIRPORT PERIMETER**

Black sky. Horizon just beginning to bruise pink. The Dayton International Air Show service gate glows under harsh floodlights, guarded by two airport cops in folding chairs beside a barricade.

Inside the van: tension tightens.

**MR. EVANS**
Alright, team. Time to get tactical and practical.

**KATHY**
Tactical?

**BILL**
Practical?

**MR. EVANS**
**KATHY**, hand me the bag of donuts. Top of the cooler. White bag. That’s my cop currency.

**BILL**
You’re bribing the police?

**MR. EVANS**
I’m incentivizing community relations.

(beat)
The access passes get us through the gate. But they don’t explain why a wolf-painted van with no headlights is idling on the tarmac at 4:45 in the morning.

**KATHY**
Jesus Christ.

**MR. EVANS**
When in doubt—donuts.
And also—(serious, teacher voice)

Try to stay out of sight.

**JEREMY**
Are you smuggling us into the airport?

**MR. EVANS**
Technically, you’re “vendor support specialists.” The cops don’t need to know you’re the entourage.  Omissions are just…efficient.

**KATHY**
So you lied.

**MR. EVANS**
I curated the facts for the audience at hand.

(beat)
Now crouch, and don’t breathe too loud. Cops hate that.

The van creaks as everyone ducks behind seats, under tarps. **KATHY** snags the donut bag. **JEREMY** hisses:

**JEREMY**
This is felonious.

**MR. EVANS**
This is entrepreneurial logistics.

**BILL**
This is how a bad movie starts.

**MR. EVANS**
This is how *legends* start.

The van slows for the checkpoint. Donuts in hand.  The vibe is pure *Mad, Mad, Mad, Mad World*—if filmed in Dayton at sunrise.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
They weren’t just sneaking into the airport.  They were sneaking into the memory of a lifetime.  One coffee-soaked donut at a time.

---

## **EXT. AIRPORT SERVICE GATE – 4:48 A.M.**

**SILVER BULLET ONE** rolls to a stop, engine grumbling like a bear with a migraine.

**OFFICER NANCE** and **OFFICER WELLS**—mid-40s, all Midwestern pragmatism—stand by, coffee steaming in one hand, folding barricade in the other.

**MR. EVANS** hops out, badge and donut bag raised: the world’s friendliest criminal.

**MR. EVANS**
Morning, officers!

**OFFICER NANCE**
Morning, Evans. You’re early.

**MR. EVANS**
Early is the new on-time. And I brought sugar diplomacy.

He hands over the bag. **NANCE** peeks in—maple bars, jelly, a single cruller. The smile blooms.

**OFFICER WELLS**
Same van as last year?

**MR. EVANS**
Silver Bullet One. Still running. She rattles, but she’s got heart.

**OFFICER NANCE**
Still no headlights?

**MR. EVANS**
Don’t need ’em. I’ve got God and duct tape.

**OFFICER WELLS** (grinning)
Same thing, this hour.

They wave him through.

**OFFICER NANCE**
You know the drill. Load at Chalet 3, check in at Red Zone tent, don’t block the loop like last year.

**MR. EVANS**
Wouldn’t dream of it.

He hops back in, salutes the cops. The gate swings wide.  The van rolls in—slow, easy, legend status unlocked.

---

## **INT. SILVER BULLET ONE – MOVING THROUGH AIRPORT – MOMENTS LATER**

**JEREMY**, **KATHY**, and **BILL** rise from their hiding spots like raccoons peeking out after a thunderstorm.  Their hair’s messed, their hearts pounding, but the van just glides—no sirens, no lights, just early-morning victory.

**JEREMY**
We’re in?

**MR. EVANS**
Like Flynn.

**BILL**
I didn’t even hear you lie.

**KATHY**
He didn’t have to. That was all…vibe.

**MR. EVANS**
Son, I’ve been sweet-talking local law enforcement since before you were a thought in your mama’s day planner.

(beat, catching their eyes in the rearview)
Lesson one: Sometimes it’s not what you say. It’s what you bring for breakfast.

(beat)
Now let’s go move some beer.

They look out the windows—fields of parked trucks, hangars lit gold, the first rays of sun picking out streaks of dew on a thousand folding chairs.  For a second, it feels like they’ve leveled up. Maybe they have.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Some people break rules.  Some people bend them.  Dad just winks at the rules— and the rules let him through.

---

## **“THE COORS CREW COMETH” (FULL GONZO)**

---

### **EXT. AIR SHOW GROUNDS – 5:21 A.M. – SUNRISE IS A LIE**

**SHOT:** **KATHY** screeches the Coors golf cart sideways around a hangar, one-handed, other hand shoving an *industrial-sized soft pretzel* into her mouth.  A keg flies out, nearly decapitating a garden gnome made of empty Bud cans.  **JEREMY** clings to the seat, praying in broken French.

**JEREMY** (screaming)
WE’RE ALL GONNA DIE IN A GLORIFIED FISH COOLER!

**KATHY** (howling)
BUT AT LEAST IT’S NOT BUD!

---

**SHOT:** **BILL** faces down a Bud delivery guy—a doughy, haunted man in a red cap, loading a cart with suspiciously lukewarm cans.  They circle each other, Mad Max style, between the beer tents.  **BILL** pulls a Coors keg from the cart like he’s drawing a sword.

**BILL**
I baptize this airshow in the only beer that isn’t *technically* a hate crime.

**BUD GUY**
You wanna go, Blondie?

**BILL**
You wanna taste the Rockies or suck the Mississippi?

They stare. Then, without warning, **BILL** lobs a single Bud can back into the Bud truck. It explodes in a blue-white geyser. The crowd gasps.  The Air Force gives him a slow clap.

---

**SHOT:** **JEREMY** discovers a Bud-branded tent staffed by teenagers with the dead eyes of corporate conscripts.

He strides in, grabs the PA mic, and preaches:

**JEREMY** (into mic)
This is your taste bud intervention.  Friends don’t let friends drink beer that tastes like the backwash of a tire fire!

A child in a Bud Light visor weeps.  The crowd turns on the Bud tent like a 1980s anti-drug PSA.  A security guard, sipping Coors, just gives him a thumbs up.

---

**SHOT:** **KATHY**—now fully feral, bandana on, war paint (ketchup from a cold hot dog) streaked across her cheeks—delivers three kegs to the VIP chalet.
A Bud guy tries to intercept.

**BUD GUY #2**
Hey! This is Bud country!

**KATHY** (deadly, gleeful)
Not today, St. Louis.

She tosses him a can of Coors.  He drops it.  It bounces once—hisses open.  A rainbow forms in the morning mist.

**A child in a Wright State sweatshirt gasps:**  *“I want to be her when I grow up.”*

---

**SHOT:** **BILL** at the staff tent, sitting on a crate, devouring a pretzel and washing it down with a Coors.  Someone offers him a Bud-branded water bottle.  He screams, throws it in the trash, and douses his own face with the Coors.

**BILL**
Baptize me, Silver God!

---

**SHOT:** **MR. EVANS** does paperwork in the shade. Notices the Coors crew and the Bud crew staring each other down across the tarmac.  He stands up, blows a whistle, and yells:

**MR. EVANS**
You want to move product, you do it with pride!  If you want to sell shame, try Budweiser!

The Coors Crew cheers. The Bud Crew hangs their heads.  A single hawk circles overhead, watching the carnage.

---

**FINAL SHOT:** The whole crew, sweat-soaked, half-mad, reclining beneath the massive wing of a C-141, sharing a couple of bottles of water, lusting after a six-pack of Coors like soldiers after the battle, angry that the drinking age got hiked while they were still in school.  They look out at the sun coming up over a wasteland of crushed Bud cans.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
While I healed, the band went to war.  Their only armor: a Coors logo.  Their only code: Don’t let Bud Light touch your soul.

(beat)
If there’s a heaven for rock and roll, it smells like pretzels, jet fuel, and a cold can of beer you actually believe in.

---

## **EXT. BEHIND CHALET 3 – 7:16 A.M.**

**KATHY** slams down a gallon bottle of water, missing her mouth and soaking her shirt, but not giving a damn.  **BILL** sprawls in the grass, sunglasses askew, Coors-branded towel over his face like a death shroud.  **JEREMY** is just pacing, shoes squelching, eyes half-wild, inhaling hot asphalt and cold beer fumes.

**MR. EVANS**
That, my friends, is what we call “crushing it.”

**KATHY**
That’s what I call OSHA violation number forty-six.

**BILL**
If I die, just bury me in a Coors case and don’t bother with the eulogy.

**MR. EVANS** (smiling, hands on hips, the vision of a man who *loves* a loophole)
You kids did good. I mean it.  Now listen close—this is the stuff you don’t get from textbooks:

(leans in, mock-conspiratorial, but his eyes are sharp)
It ain’t a crime if no one drops a dime.

**KATHY**
Christ, that’s bleak.

**BILL**
You should print that on a bar napkin and call it your memoir.

**JEREMY**
He told me that before I knew what a dime was.

**MR. EVANS**
And you’re still here, aren’t you?  The real trick—move quick, move quiet, keep the beer cold, and always have a donut for the right guy.  That’s management, kids.

**KATHY** (with a dead smile)
And how many donuts to get out of freezer duty?

**MR. EVANS** (innocent as a saint)
Oh, freezer duty is a barter situation.  Welcome to the real world.

---

## **EXT. BACKSIDE OF MAIN CHALETS – 11:02 A.M.**

The sun is *apocalyptic*.  The tarmac is shimmering with heat.  **KATHY**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** are so sweaty they can barely move, the *tang* of stale beer and grass in their nostrils.

They watch **MR. EVANS** lock eyes with a man in airport-issue aviators and a power stance—Clipboard Guy.  It’s a language of dads: shrugs, grins, a little “what can you do,” and the fateful handshake.

**JEREMY** (eyes narrowing)
Is that…Is that the handshake?

**KATHY**
That’s the handshake.

**BILL**
I can see my breath and it’s ninety-eight degrees out. That’s how cold this deal feels.

**KATHY**
We’re not people, we’re favor tokens.  Barter chips.

**MR. EVANS** turns, gives the world’s most damning thumbs-up. You can *hear* the sound of the freezer truck’s cooling unit kick on. Like a *guillotine* for hope.

**JEREMY**
He just volunteered us for something.

**KATHY**
That’s not a volunteer. That’s a transfer of liability.

**BILL**
We should’ve just kept running. I’d have lived under a parked C-5 and eaten hot dog buns for a week.

**KATHY**
You think they’ll even *let* us have gloves?

**BILL**
I’d settle for a cup of coffee that doesn’t taste like despair.

**They watch as Mr. Evans and Clipboard Guy part ways, both looking smug and victorious—like foxes after a henhouse raid.**

**JEREMY**
If this is about organizing ice cream sandwiches, I’m walking back to Bethel.

**KATHY**
You can’t. He’s got the keys.

**BILL**
And the only air conditioning.

**KATHY**
Goddamn it. We’re going into the box.

**They exchange a look—the look of the truly powerless, the looked-after, the bartered, the used.**

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Mr. Evans ran on charm, donuts, and the barter economy of the desperate.  And in the real world?  A favor was never free.

(beat)
The cold shift wasn’t about freezer burns.  It was about learning the price of being useful—and the cost of letting someone else hold the keys.

---

## **EXT. BACKSIDE OF THE MAIN CHALETS – 11:05 A.M.**

**KATHY**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** aren’t just tired. They’re spiritually *taxed*.  The ground is hot enough to fry a bologna sandwich. Their souls are cold enough to make an icicle sweat.

**MR. EVANS** (strolling up, Olympic-winner energy, clipboard at his side)
Now before you yell at me—hear me out.

**KATHY**
Oh, we’re way past yelling.

**JEREMY**
Dad, did you just sell our bodies to the frozen meat gods?

**MR. EVANS** (waves a dismissive hand, all charm and salesmanship)
I just struck the best deal since I got your sister those Elton John tickets in ‘87.

**BILL** (weak, haunted)
That was a felony, wasn’t it?

**MR. EVANS** (ignoring the question, eyes sparkling)
Focus up.

(He pauses—*this* is the sales pitch of his life, the reason middle managers are born.)

How would you guys like…SIX tickets. To see DEF LEPPARD. At Riverfront Coliseum. September.

(beat—lets it land)

**KATHY**
You’re fucking with us.

**MR. EVANS**
And because I am, in fact, the *greatest* negotiator on the goddamn tarmac—Backstage passes.

**BILL** (his soul leaves his body)
Back…stage?

**MR. EVANS**
Meet and greet. Green room access. You might even smell the drummer.

**JEREMY**
You bartered us for Def Leppard?

**MR. EVANS**
I bartered you for *rock immortality*.

**KATHY**
What’s the catch?

**MR. EVANS**
Just a few hours of freezer truck work.  Help the catering crew with cold storage logistics.  Maybe break down a pallet or two.  Light lifting. Minimal frostbite.

**BILL**
You said no more lifting.

**MR. EVANS**
I said no more *keg* lifting. Now it’s just…Crates of frozen pretzels. Maybe some bulk corn dogs. You’ll be fine.

**KATHY**
You’re a monster.

**BILL**
I would strip for those passes.

**MR. EVANS**
That’s the spirit!  You kids are on the front line of music history. The Def Leppard line.

He’s already walking toward the freezer truck, clipboard swinging like a sword.

---

## **EXT. FREEZER TRUCK – 11:09 A.M.**

The sun is merciless. The side of the truck is so white, so bright, it’s like staring at God’s knuckles.

**MR. EVANS** stands at the back, grinning, rolling up the metal door. Fog spills out—cold, blue, the breath of Hades.

**MR. EVANS**
Alright, crew. Good news. This one’s simple.

**JEREMY**
There’s never good news.

**MR. EVANS**
You’re just moving a small pile of ice.

**KATHY**
Define “small.”

**MR. EVANS**
Fifteen—

**KATHY**
—hundred?

**MR. EVANS**
Thousand. Fifteen thousand pounds.

**BILL** (deadpan)
Are we bagging glaciers now?

**KATHY**
Do you even know what 15,000 pounds of ice *is*?

**MR. EVANS**
Of course! That’s like…1,875 eight-pound bags.

**JEREMY** (hollow)
Like we’re ice gnomes in some capitalist fairy tale.

**MR. EVANS**
You want to see Def Leppard, don’t you?

**KATHY**
Do I have to die to see them?

**MR. EVANS**
It’s a simple exchange. Work fast, get done fast. Gloves are in the van. They might be a little damp. Maybe some holes.

**BILL**
We’re gonna be cold. We’re gonna be wet. We’re gonna be traumatized.

**MR. EVANS**
And when you’re done? All-access passes. Unlimited hot dogs. Backstage. With *Def Leppard.*

He says it like he’s Moses handing out commandments.

They stare into the freezer. The ice is stacked in blue bags, like a glacier’s guts. The air bites, even from five feet away.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Fifteen thousand pounds of ice.  Trapped in a meat locker on wheels.  In exchange for music and nachos.  Somewhere between bravery and madness, they said yes.

Because that’s what friends do.  Even when it’s freezing.

---

## **INT. FREEZER TRUCK – HELL O’CLOCK – SAME DAY**

It’s 36 degrees Fahrenheit and dropping. Breath comes in visible puffs. Every inhale burns. The walls are coated in a thin film of ice, as if the truck has ambitions to be a glacier. A single overhead light buzzes, casting sickly, flickering blue light.

And the ice. God, the ice.

**KATHY**, **JEREMY**, and **BILL** are buried in it, shivering, dragging bags from the deepest, darkest corners of the truck toward the yawning, uncaring daylight.

**KATHY** (teeth chattering)
This is war.

**JEREMY** (ice in his lashes)
This is how people die climbing Mount Everest.

**BILL**
This is how I die in Ohio. For Def Leppard.

**KATHY**
My whole ass is on ice. My soul is on ice.

**JEREMY**
I can’t feel my knees. I think I left them on the last pallet.

**BILL**
There’s crushed ice in my shoes, Kathy. In my *shoes*.  There are entire civilizations of frost in my socks.  This is…this is the end.

**KATHY**
My face is stuck. Rage and resignation. I may never smile again.

**BILL**
Why did we do this? Why did we say yes?

**JEREMY**
Because my dad said “backstage Def Leppard,” and we’re all morons with no self-preservation instinct.

They pass another bag. Then another. Each one is heavier, wetter, and colder than the last. Every movement echoes like a curse in a deep, cold tomb.

---

### **CUT TO: EXT. NEAR THE VIP CHALET – SAME TIME**

**MR. EVANS** is living his best life:  Sunglasses on. Folding chair. Walking taco in one hand, barbecue sandwich in the other.  A Coors Light-branded cup sweats by his feet. He surveys the airfield with the air of a man who’s just conquered Rome with nothing but paperwork and adolescent labor.

**MR. EVANS** (to himself, mouth full)
God bless America.

(beat, nodding at the distant jets)
Cold beer. Hot food. Air superiority.  And highly motivated youth!

---

### **INT. FREEZER TRUCK – 54 MINUTES IN**

**KATHY**
My soul is wet.

**BILL**
My lungs are wet.

**JEREMY**
My hope is wet.

The *shhhhkkk* of another bag of ice sliding across the truck. Numb fingers. Soaked gloves. Despair.

**KATHY** (bleak)
If we die, make sure my tombstone says, “Killed by your Dad’s ambition and Def Leppard.”

---

## **EXT. AIR SHOW LOADING ZONE – 12:23 P.M.**

The freezer truck door creaks open.  **KATHY**, **JEREMY**, and **BILL** stumble out like extras from “Titanic: The Ohio Cut.”  They’re sodden, shivering, and hunched—shadows of their former selves. Their shirts stick to their backs. Their socks squish. Their hands are claws of ruined felt.

**KATHY** (hoarse)
If I die today…put Mr. Evans in the casket with me.

**JEREMY**
He’s your ride home.

**KATHY**
Then we’re all going in together.

**BILL**
I think I just peed a bag of ice. Not on purpose.

**MR. EVANS** (beaming, approaching like a coach greeting his championship team)
There they are! The Champions of Chill!

**KATHY**
We are damp. We are broken. We are legally no longer people.

**MR. EVANS**
Come on—it wasn’t that bad! Builds character! And check this out—

He yanks a plastic shopping bag off a table, waving it like a war banner.

**MR. EVANS (CONT’D)**
Ta-da! Commemorative Dayton Air Show T-shirts!

He flings them out, one by one. They’re stiff, boxy, aggressively patriotic, and as comforting as sandpaper.

**KATHY**
You think this will keep me from testifying?

**JEREMY**
I’m going to burn this.

**BILL**
I’m going to *frame* mine. As a warning to others.

**MR. EVANS**
You kids were incredible. You did the work. You showed grit. And now you’re legends.

(beat)
Go find somewhere dry and think about what you’re going to wear to meet Def Leppard.

**KATHY** (sotto, dead-eyed)
A towel. A towel and vengeance.

They stagger away, holding their shirts like cursed trophies.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
While I napped and healed, They faced frost and humiliation.  They earned t-shirts, trauma, and backstage passes.  And somehow…They’d do it all again.

(beat)
Because we were all a little stupid for the right reasons.

---

## **EXT. DAYTON INTERNATIONAL AIRPORT – SHOW CENTER – 1:15 P.M.**

The sun is a white hammer in the sky. The air tastes like hot asphalt, jet exhaust, and scorched funnel cake. **KATHY**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** sprawl on the trampled grass behind the VIP tent, still sticky from freezer-truck hell, shirts limp, skin buzzing.

And then—

A distant *growl*. Like the earth has indigestion.

**JEREMY**
You hear that?

**KATHY** (squinting)
No. But I feel it in my teeth.

**BILL** (voice trembling)
That’s not a truck. That’s…that’s doom approaching.

And then: **F-15 EAGLE**. A streak of gray death, slicing through the air like an accusation. Five hundred knots. Wings knife-edge. **Screaming** over show center, barely above the tents, the nose yanking vertical—physics be damned.

The sound follows— A wall of thunder, violence, and awe.  It *hits* them. Like being drop-kicked by the voice of God.

Every rib vibrates. Every cavity shakes. Grass flattens. Heads duck by instinct.

**KATHY** (eyes wide, hand on chest)
That just erased my entire childhood trauma.

**BILL** (genuinely, stunned)
I can taste colors.

(beat, awed)
I’m going to devote my life to this noise.

**JEREMY** (shouting, like a sermon)
God is so, so LOUD!

The F-15 hangs at the edge of the sky, teasing the sound barrier—flirting with the impossible. Then disappears, leaving silence so absolute it’s almost divine.  Mr. Evans appears, lemonade in one hand, churro in the other. His sunglasses catch the last glint of jet-wash.

**MR. EVANS**
That, my friends, is the sound of *American air superiority*.

(beat)
And that’s why we sell beer, not Budweiser. We’ve got standards.

The kids are silent, still vibrating, souls reset.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
While I was trapped in gauze and hydrocodone,  They got baptized by jet fire and thunder.  It wasn’t subtle. It wasn’t gentle.  But for one long moment, It was perfect.

---

## **EXT. DAYTON AIR SHOW GROUNDS – 1:30 P.M. TO 4:00 P.M. – TIME LAPSE MONTAGE**

The sun is brutal. The field is packed—kids on shoulders, granddads in old squadron hats, sunburnt families half-napping on military-issue wool blankets. **KATHY**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** are flat on their backs in a patch of grass behind a VIP tent, hands aching, faces up, still tasting cold and salt on their lips.

**SHOT: TORA! TORA! TORA!**
Pyro erupts along the tarmac—a line of fake napalm, black smoke roiling, Zeros buzzing overhead.  **KATHY** flinches, her hand squeezing **BILL’s** arm without thinking.

**KATHY**
This is the loudest history lesson I’ve ever survived.

**JEREMY**
I just learned that fear smells like lighter fluid and hot dogs.

**BILL**
I’m patriotic, nauseous, and deeply impressed.

**SHOT: RF-4C PHANTOM**
A huge shadow sweeps over them as the Phantom passes, camera windows glinting.

**ANNOUNCER (V.O.)**
Ladies and gentlemen, your *United States Air Force* RF-4C Phantom II, taking a picture of every single one of you right now!

**KATHY**
Smile for government scrapbooks.

**JEREMY**
I blinked.

**BILL**
They know.

**SHOT: F-14 TOMCAT**
A rolling barrel of thunder. Gear down, wings swept, the Tomcat floats past, waggles, then lights the burners and climbs, twin trails of smoke painting the sky.  A Navy vet near them stands and salutes, tears in his eyes.

**BILL**
That’s the sexiest thing I’ve ever seen that wasn’t Joan Jett on MTV.

**KATHY**
You’re in public.

**JEREMY**
Let him have this.

**SHOT: KIDS WITH EAR MUFFS, DADS WITH BEERS, OLD MEN FILMING, TEENS MAKING OUT UNDER THE BLEACHERS.**
Life. Heat. Sweat. Laughter.

**TIME: 3:58 P.M.**
A hush sweeps the crowd, restless and electric. People surge forward to the fence, cameras up, hearts beating fast.

**KATHY**
This is it.

**BILL**
We survived frostbite for this.

**JEREMY**
We get to feel this.

They don’t even realize they’re holding hands.

---

## **EXT. SHOW CENTER – 4:00 P.M.**

Stillness. A thousand faces tipped skyward, squinting in the sun. Every sound seems to hush—birds, radios, the low hum of anticipation.

**ANNOUNCER (V.O.)**
Ladies and gentlemen…your ***United States Air Force Thunderbirds.***

SFX: The *world* explodes.

SIX F-16 FIGHTING FALCONS burst from behind the hangars, slicing the sky in perfect delta formation, contrails streaming like cosmic chalk lines.

The trio is frozen. Breathless.

**KATHY** (barely audible)
Jesus fucking Christ.

**BILL**
That’s not flying. That’s something else.

**JEREMY**
That’s the speed of god.

**MANEUVER #1: BOMB BURST**
At show center, the six jets split wide, fanning out in a starburst. The shockwave hits a split-second later, a slap to the chest and the soul.

**BILL** (eyes wide, voice cracking)
How…How do they do that?

**KATHY**
Shut up and look. Just…look.

**MANEUVER #2: DIAMOND 360**
Four jets sweep back in, diamond tight, wingtips almost touching, carving a perfect circle at 400 knots.

**JEREMY**
I can’t even parallel park, and they’re doing *that.*

**BILL**
I think this is better than sex.

**KATHY**
Hmph! It’s definitely louder.

**MANEUVER #3: OPPOSING SOLO PASS**
Two jets approach from opposite ends, crossing center at 1,000 mph—one inverted, one knife-edge. They pass so close it’s a miracle of math. The crowd *gasps* in unison. A baby wails. A drunk uncle cheers.

**KATHY** (laughing, disbelieving)
That’s actually illegal.

**JEREMY**
We’re all accessories.

**BILL**
America, please never change.

**MANEUVER #4: VERTICAL ROLL CLIMB**
Solo #5 claws straight up, spiraling into the blue, disappearing into the glare. For a second—he’s just gone. Then he tumbles down, rolling, and pulls out inches above the tarmac. The crowd loses its mind.

**ANNOUNCER (V.O.)**
Give it up for your ***United States Air Force Thunderbirds!***

All six jets return, banking low in the sun, rolling wings in salute before vanishing into the sky.

**KATHY** (blinking, dazed)
I mean…it’s a good day.

**BILL** (voice cracking, quietly)
I think it’s the best day.

**JEREMY** (soft, smiling)
Totally worth it.

They’re quiet, for once. Just three friends, shoulders pressed, hearts pounding in their chests, eyes wide and shining.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
You never know the best days while you’re living them.  But sometimes—if you’re lucky?  You get a glimpse.  Just for a second.  Sunburned, ringing, hearts full of noise and sky.  And you know— It’s a good day to be alive.

---

## **EXT. PARKING LOT – DAYLIGHT – 7:14 P.M.**

The sky is still blazing blue, not a hint of dusk yet. No golden hour for another hour. No relief. More hours of full-force sun, bouncing off windshields and heating the pavement until it smells like rubber and hot dogs.

**KATHY**, **JEREMY**, and **BILL** are trudging across the parking lot toward Coors Force One, sweat reactivating with every step, but grinning all the same—sunburned, stiff, and stupidly proud.

The van, with its peeling wolf mural and duct-taped CB antenna, gleams in the afternoon sun like a holy relic of poor decisions.

**JEREMY**
I’m gonna sleep in the shower.

**BILL**
I’m gonna write a will before I go unconscious.

**KATHY**
You both better live long enough to brag, because I’m not letting the others off the hook.

(beat)
They missed it.

**JEREMY**
Big time.

**BILL**
Like, they’ll never understand missed it.

**KATHY**
I want Jeff to hear everything. All of it.  Every jet. Every ice bag. Every bag of regret.

**JEREMY**
They sat at home. We got a goddamn aerobatics baptism.

**BILL**
We made memories. We earned t-shirts. We saw God and He drives an Eagle!

They reach the van. Mr. Evans is already in the driver’s seat, sipping something out of a red Solo cup and humming “*Rock of Ages*” to himself.

**MR. EVANS**
Coors Force One is wheels-up in five, folks. If you didn’t bleed for beer and burn fo JP-4 today, I don’t want you in this van.

They collapse inside. Doors slam. The van rumbles to life.

**KATHY** (Softly, to no one)
We won.

**BILL**
And Def Leppard is just the victory lap.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
I didn’t see the Thunderbirds. Didn’t feel the shockwave. Didn’t taste the sweat or the cold or the nacho cheese dust on Bill’s chin.  But when they came home, glowing and broken, I understood something deep: Sometimes the best part of the band…Is when they come back with stories. And save one just for you.

---

## **EXT. I-70 WESTBOUND ON-RAMP – 7:41 P.M.**

**Coors Force One** crawls forward, surrounded by a river of tail lights. The air outside is thick with after-sun and the dull ache of too much living. Every car is a little island of exhaustion.

**KATHY** (leans back, staring at the ceiling)
We survived frostbite, jet engines, and fifteen thousand pounds of ice…for a parking lot.

**JEREMY**
At least we’re not still cold. My feet feel like soup.

**BILL**
I think I left part of my soul on the grass.

**MR. EVANS** (cheery, running on pure dad-juice)
Traffic, baby! Builds patience, builds character, builds stories.

**KATHY**
Everything’s a story with you. I want a nap, not a narrative.

**MR. EVANS**
You’ll sleep when you’re dead!

She doesn’t even bother to reply. Instead, she rolls down the window and lets the muggy Ohio evening slap her in the face.

---

## **EXT. I-70 – 8:05 P.M.**

The van finally breaks free. Wind whips through the cabin, Def Leppard fuzzes through the speakers. The highway opens up—a promise, a threat, a dare.

**“Photograph”** comes on, wild and raw.

**BILL**
Crank it! Let’s hear the cones die!

**KATHY** (half-laughing, half-feral)
I want the wind so loud I can’t think.

**JEREMY**
God, you’re not tired *at all*, are you?

She grins at him, eyes wild and alive. Sunburned, battered, glowing with something that refuses to die down.

**KATHY**
Are you kidding? Days like this—I want to drive straight through to California. Just keep going.

The van barrels west, the mural wolf howling at the sun. The song rides the static. For one perfect moment, none of them want to be anywhere else.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
They were half-melted, half-drunk on noise and cheap glory. But with the sun setting behind them and the music loud, nothing hurt for a little while. They belonged to the road, to the moment, to each other.

---

## **EXT. FRONT ST. PARKING LOT – 8:27 P.M.**

The day is ending, but Kathy’s not ready. She drags her feet getting out of the van, t-shirt clinging, face still sun-dazed.

**BILL** (yawning, packing up)
Alright, I gotta crash. Reality calls. I have to pretend to care about a job at dawn.

**JEREMY** (wiping his face, sheepish)
Same. I’m fried. Jeff’ll be fine, he’s made of spare parts now.

**KATHY** (soft, restless)
Yeah. See you.

She watches them go, shoulders tight, eyes following the highway, not the parking lot. For her, the night isn’t over. She wants more—music, noise, anything but silence.

---

# **CHAPTER SEVEN: ONE TO SPEAK, ONE TO HEAR**

---

## **EXT. THE EVANS HOUSE – 8:56 P.M.**

Kathy stands on the Evans porch, McDonald’s bag in hand, nerves jangling under her skin. The world is too quiet after jet engines and a thousand strangers’ cheers.

She knocks. Twice. No hesitation.

**INT. EVANS HOME – CONTINUOUS**

The door opens on **JEFF**—bandaged, weary, but smiling at the sight of her.

**JEFF**
Let me guess. McRib season?

**KATHY**
It’s always McRib season when you’re healing.

She holds up the bag, a peace offering, a favor.

**JEFF**
You want to tell me about the Thunderbirds or the trauma first?

**KATHY**
I want both. But mostly, I want to not be alone when the day finally stops ringing in my ears.

He steps aside, lets her in.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Sometimes, after the best days, you chase the noise for as long as you can—just to keep it from fading. Sometimes you show up with cheap food and sunburn and stories no one else will believe. Sometimes, that’s what keeps the world spinning.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 9:06 P.M.**

The TV is on but muted—Bob Barker, eternally smiling, gestures at a silent Showcase Showdown. The room is dim, soft lamplight filling the corners. There’s a hint of fries and sweet barbecue sauce in the air.

**KATHY** is curled up at the edge of the couch, cross-legged, half-wrapped in an old throw blanket that once covered **JEFF**’s childhood bed. She looks smaller in this light—sunburned, hair frizzed from the day, but unwound.

**JEFF** sits nearby, ear bandaged, pajama pants, a single sock, holding half a McRib like it’s the last artifact of civilization.

**JEFF** (taking a bite, chewing)
Okay. You’re gonna have to explain “freezer trauma.” Because I don’t get it.

**KATHY** (smiling, weary)
You ever move fifteen thousand pounds of ice?

**JEFF**
In what universe would I ever do that?

**KATHY**
Exactly.

(beat)
We were in a freezer truck. All three of us. No breaks. No gloves that worked. **JEREMY** was delirious, **BILL** swore he saw his ancestors. I couldn’t feel my femurs.

**JEFF**
That sounds awful.

**KATHY**
It was. Your dad called it “a favor.” Which is code for “you’ll suffer, and I’ll eat a sloppy joe while you do.”

**JEFF**
Jesus.

**KATHY**
We were soaked. Frozen. Hauling bags out for hours while it hit triple digits outside. My fingers went full popsicle. I haven’t been warm since noon.

**JEFF**
And I missed all of it?

**KATHY**
You missed everything.

**JEFF** (soft, wry)
My ear was kind of…preoccupied.

(taps the bandage)
Being stapled back on.

**KATHY** (nods, gentle)
Fair.

She leans her head back against the couch. Closes her eyes for a moment, letting the day fall off her shoulders.

**KATHY** (CONT’D)
Still wish you were there.

**JEFF**
Yeah. Me too.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Sometimes you miss the best day of someone’s life. And they bring you a sandwich anyway.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – LATER**

The TV flickers blue in the background, barely lighting the room. The McDonald’s bag is crumpled on the table, fries long gone. The last bites of McRib hang between them.

**KATHY** sits back, brushing sauce from her thumb, studying him with a softness she tries to keep hidden.

**KATHY**
You know…you look okay.

**JEFF** (raising an eyebrow)
For someone with his ear duct-taped to his skull?

**KATHY**
Exactly. You look better than I expected.

**JEFF**
You smell like smoke and jet fuel and…barbecue sauce.

**KATHY**
Not the worst combination.

**JEFF**
It works.

She smiles, small and crooked. Looks down at her knees, then back at him.

**KATHY**
You’re smarter than people think.

**JEFF**
You’re tougher than people realize.

A beat. It hangs there, longer than it should. They sit in the hush, side by side, warm and a little raw from the day.  Finally, **KATHY** tugs the blanket up and settles into the couch, pulling her legs in. **JEFF** puts his empty sandwich wrapper on the table, leaning back, suddenly aware of how close they are, but not quite sure what to do with it.

Nothing more needs to be said.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Sometimes the best nights don’t say much. Just enough to let you know you’re seen. That you’re wanted. Even if neither of you can say it yet.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 9:24 P.M.**

Empty wrappers sit balled on the table. The TV glows quietly in the background. **KATHY** is tucked into one corner of the couch, arms around her knees, blanket trailing. **JEFF** shifts in his seat, clearly circling something in his head.

**JEFF**
So, uh…Doctor says no heavy lifting.

**KATHY** (grinning)
I’d hope so. Your ear’s held together with dental floss and hope.

**JEFF**
Yeah. He said bass guitar probably counts as “heavy lifting.”

**KATHY**
Definitely. That thing’s half a redwood.

**JEFF** (fidgeting)
Anyway…I was thinking, maybe Monday night, if you’re free…we could, I dunno, try writing together? Lyrics, chords—stuff I can’t pick up right now.

**KATHY** (surprised, studying him)
You asking me to babysit the invalid?

**JEFF**
No. I’m asking you to show up.

She looks at him for a second, all jokes dropped.

**KATHY** (soft, sincere)
Yeah. Okay. Monday night. We’ll write.

**JEFF**
Cool.

**KATHY**
You’ll owe me fries.

**JEFF**
You already owe me a new eardrum.

She actually laughs—quiet, genuine. The silence that follows is comfortable, full of things neither needs to say.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
No big confessions. No lines in the sand. Just an idea, and someone who didn’t hesitate.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 9:31 P.M.**

**JEFF** sits angled toward **KATHY**, silent but not distant. His wrapped ear makes him look a little softer, somehow—vulnerable in a way she rarely sees. But his face? Still unreadable.

**KATHY** steals little glances, measuring the silence between them. She thinks:

**KATHY (V.O.)**
*Okay.* He asked me to come over. Brought up Monday night. Invited me to write. That’s not nothing. That’s…something.

*But* he never says why.  Not “I missed you.” Not “Stay.”  Just sitting there, bandaged up, post-op, eating a McRib like it’s holy.

*So,* what do I do?  Reach out? Touch his hand?  Ask a real question?

*Or go nuclear*, just unzip his fly and solve it with my mouth, not my heart?  Would he even stop me? Would he stop me?  Or worse—would he say “thanks”?

**If** he says thanks, I’m walking straight into traffic.

Maybe he’s waiting for me. Maybe he’s scared.  Maybe he just doesn’t want to push.  Maybe I’m the same.

She looks up—catches his eyes. Just for a heartbeat.  He gives her that small, safe, easy smile.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This would be so much easier if he were a jerk. Or cocky. Or just…obvious.  But he’s Jeff.  And that’s the problem.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 9:36 P.M.**

**JEFF** leans back, half under a blanket, eyes on the TV but aware of **KATHY** in his periphery.

She’s twitchy tonight—not in a bad way. Just…on edge, like she’s buzzing with static. He can’t read it, but he likes having her here.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
She’s acting different. Not bad-different. Just…jumpy. Tense.  I don’t think it’s *me.*

I mean, I’m glad she came. I’m glad she’s still here. This is one of the best nights I’ve had in weeks.  She brought food. She sat on my couch.  She roasted my ear bandage, but made me laugh.

So why does it feel like she’s ready to bolt? Or…jump me? Or *both?*

(beat)
Maybe she’s tired. Or maybe she’s overthinking. She does that—goes quiet in a way that fills the room.

Maybe I should say something.  But *what?*

He glances at her, then offers a gentle smile.

**JEFF**
Hey. Reds are on at ten-oh-five. Out in San Francisco.  Wanna stick around and watch?

He says it like it’s casual. But it’s not.  He wants her to stay. Just a little longer.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Don’t go yet. Please don’t go yet.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 9:37 P.M.**

**JEFF** looks over from the couch—voice casual, face open.

> **JEFF**
> Reds are on at ten-oh-five. In San Francisco. Wanna stick around and watch with me?

**KATHY** doesn’t move. But inside, she’s buzzing.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Is…is that the best he can do?

**Yeah.**

Yeah, it is. That’s his way of asking me to stay.  No hint. No pressure. Just baseball. Just company.

God, it’s so *soft* it hurts.

I’ve been listening to **JEREMY** more lately—not just hearing him, but *listening*.  The way he talks about **JEFF**—it’s different. He doesn’t say “weird.” He doesn’t say “off.”  He says, “He’s just wired another way.”

And yeah. He is. **JEFF** doesn’t flirt. He doesn’t chase.  He just…opens a door. If I want in, I have to walk through it.

So *maybe* I stop waiting for a sign.  Maybe I stop playing like it’s a game.
Maybe I just say—

**KATHY**
Yeah. I’ll stay.

**JEFF** (quietly pleased)
Cool.

She settles deeper into the couch. Not closer. Not further. Just there.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
One game. One night. One more chance to learn how he works.  Because maybe that’s what love looks like with someone like **JEFF**.

Not lightning. Not explosions.  Just a couch. A quiet TV. And a really, really good night.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 10:36 P.M.**

The Reds are down by two in the third. TV light flickers across the room.

**KATHY** and **JEFF** sit side by side—not touching, but the distance between them isn’t empty anymore.

She hasn’t said much in the last inning.

Finally, quietly:

**KATHY**
Can I ask you something?

**JEFF**
Always.

**KATHY**
How do you do it?

**JEFF**
Do what?

**KATHY**
Write lyrics like that.  Like you *feel* everything.  Like you’ve lived everything. Like your chest is a cathedral and all the doors are open.  And then…in real life…you barely say a word. You don’t show it. You barely hint at it. You just…fold in on yourself.  How does that make sense?

**JEFF** doesn’t answer right away. He shifts—like the question itself weighs something.

**JEFF**
Writing’s different. There’s time. There’s space. No one’s looking at you.  I can think it through. Rewrite it.  Cut the parts that don’t make sense, or feel too loud, or come out wrong.

It’s like…It’s like building a bridge out of wood you’re still growing.   In real life, there’s no draft. No second take. Just people looking at you, waiting for you to say something, and you don’t even know what you’re supposed to say.  So you say nothing.  Because nothing feels safer than the wrong thing.

He keeps his eyes on the TV—a batter fouls one off into the stands.

**KATHY** just watches him.

**KATHY**
So the lyrics…they’re the right thing?

**JEFF**
They’re the only thing that comes out right.   They’re the parts of me I wish I could just…walk around with.   But I can’t. Not yet.

The TV drones on. The Reds load the bases.  She doesn’t answer right away. Then—

**KATHY**
Thanks for telling me that.

**JEFF**
Thanks for asking.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Some people speak in poems.  Some people speak in silence.  And sometimes, if you’re lucky— They meet in the middle.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 10:52 P.M.**

A commercial break. The room is lit by the soft glow of the muted TV and the faint whir of the fan.

**KATHY** shifts, glancing over at **JEFF**.

**KATHY**
Hey—did you hear about Tim?

**JEFF**
Class of '87, 88' and '89 Tim?

**KATHY**
Hah! He finally got a ship assignment.

**JEFF**
Wait—really?

**KATHY**
Yeah. He finished corpsman training. He’s getting deployed to the *USS Iwo Jima.*

**JEFF**
No shit.

(beat)
I ran into him earlier this summer, just randomly. He was back in town.

**KATHY**
Yeah?

**JEFF**
I didn’t even recognize him. Swear to God, I thought he was someone’s older brother.

**KATHY**
I heard he dropped a ton of weight.

**JEFF**
Eighty pounds. Eighty. He’s not even the same human. He was the soft, doughy guy who used to fail gym just for existing.
Now?

(beat)
He looks like he could break ribs on purpose.

**KATHY**
That’s what happens when you let the Navy own your ass for a year and a half.

**JEFF**
Yeah, well—he cleaned up. Still weird, though. Like seeing a childhood stuffed animal come back with a six-pack and naval discipline.

**KATHY**
Tim, the plush bear turned war medic.

**JEFF**
Exactly.

The game flickers back. Bases cleared. Reds down by one. They watch, but the conversation has changed something. The world has crept in. It feels like a different night now.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Time doesn’t just change people. It redraws them.  Sometimes you see it. Sometimes you feel it.  And sometimes…you sit beside someone and realize it’s happening to you, too.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 11:08 P.M.**

The Reds are rallying, barely. **KATHY** isn’t watching anymore. She’s watching **JEFF**. His profile is calm, focused, a little battered but steady.

One sock. Blanket. Head still bandaged. He looks both fragile and impossible to break.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
If anything’s going to happen, it has to be me. That’s the truth.  He’s not going to make the move—not tonight, not Monday, maybe not ever.  He needs space. He needs time. He needs to be sure.

But me? I don’t want to wait. I’ve been waiting since before the McRib.

So I have three options:  I do it now, tonight, in the quiet, when we’re close enough to breathe in sync.

Or I wait until Monday, when we’re writing—when it’s safe, when I can hide behind lyrics and deflection.

Or…I *don’t.* I let it stay sweet and distant. And I go home. And I lie awake, screaming into my pillow about what could have happened.

But if I do it now—What is it?

A kiss? A touch? A blunt “do you want me?” Or just curling closer on the couch and letting that be enough?

God, why can’t he *just make* a move?

No. That’s not fair. This is the move. This night. This couch. This version of him.  It’s the best he can do. And I either meet him halfway—

Or I *don’t.*

She studies him again. He shifts slightly, eyes still on the game, but his body angled just a little toward her—like he’s waiting, without knowing he’s waiting.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Now or Monday or never. That’s the choice.  And whatever I pick…it’s on me.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 11:12 P.M.**

**JEFF** is chuckling softly at a missed double play. The TV glows. The couch cushions sink between them. The night hums.

But **KATHY** isn’t watching the game.  She’s watching memory.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
That F-15. That Moment. Right after lunch. The sky was calm, the air was heavy, and then—

**WHAM.**

Screaming across the runway. Nose up. Engines full throttle. A hole ripped into the blue. The sound hit us a second later—like getting punched in the lungs by God. It was beautiful. Terrifying.  And no one saw it coming.

Even **BILL**—mouth open, nacho cheese on his shirt—just said, “That’s better than sex.”

And you know what? He wasn’t wrong.  Because surprise can be shocking, and shock can be intimate.

And **JEFF**? He needs that. He’s quiet. Careful. Internal. You don’t hint your way into **JEFF**.  You build a bonfire.

*So* now I’m thinking—do I do it? Right here, right now? Just…shock him?

Kiss him? Grab his hand? Say it all? Pull the nose up and fly straight through him, no warning, no prep? Would he press? Would he freeze? Or would he finally—finally—open up?

Because I swear to God—

(beat)
I want to be the jet in his life. Not the white noise.

She glances at him again. Still smiling. Still **JEFF**.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
It’d be so easy. Just lean over. Just press the Moment against his lips. One second of thunder.  And then? Let the smoke clear.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 11:19 P.M.**

The Reds are still losing. A pitcher change crawls across the screen.  **JEFF** leans forward, tossing back the last of his drink—unaware that the temperature in the room is about to change forever.  **KATHY** shifts closer. Just slightly. Close enough that he can feel the warmth of her. She leans in—not aggressive, not dramatic, just quiet. Like someone sharing a secret. Like someone offering lightning wrapped in velvet.

She tilts toward his good ear. Her breath brushes his neck. And in the softest, most deliberate whisper—

**KATHY**
After the game…

(beat)
I’d like to give you a blowjob.

(beat)
If that’s okay.

(beat)
I would…really, truly love the chance.

She pulls back. She doesn’t smile. She doesn’t break eye contact. She just lets the words settle into him like heat. Like a sonic boom, half a second behind the jet.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
It didn’t come like a kiss.  It came like the sky splitting open.  And for once—I didn’t have to guess.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S LIVING ROOM – 11:20 P.M.**

Silence.

On TV, the pitcher is warming up.  **JEFF** just stares. Mouth slightly open. Processing. Failing to process.  **KATHY** sits calmly beside him, watching. Waiting. Patient and daring.

**JEFF**
I…uh—

(He clears his throat, blinking rapidly)
That…That’s…wow.

(beat)
I mean, I think the Reds are making a—

(he glances at the TV, desperate for footing)
—a pitching change? Left-hander coming in. Maybe. I don’t—

Jesus.

(He catches himself. Hears it: the spiral, the dodge. He doesn’t want to ruin it. Not this time.)

He exhales. Hands tremble slightly. He reaches down, unzips his fly—a simple gesture, a quiet permission. He can’t look at her when he says it. But he says it anyway.

**JEFF**
Well…after the bottom of the ninth…

(beat)
You can…yeah. If you still want to. Well…

(after a breath, just barely above a whisper)
Yeah. After the bottom of the ninth.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
I didn’t know how to say yes. But I knew how not to say no.  And maybe…for tonight…that was enough.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 11:41 P.M.**

**KATHY**’s legs are tucked under her, eyes half-lidded, watching the TV out of the corner of her eye.  **JEFF**? Fully locked in.  He’s leaning forward, mouth open—not at her, but at the sudden, improbable offensive rally happening on screen.

**MARTY BRENNAMAN (TV)**
That’s eight unanswered runs for the Reds here in the top of the ninth!   Can you believe it? *Can you believe it?* They are absolutely demolishing the Giants’ bullpen tonight!

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Are you fucking kidding me? This is happening? Right now?  I whisper the boldest, most open offer I’ve ever made in my sexual history…And now the Reds decide to become the 1927 Yankees?

**KATHY** watches **JEFF** fist-pump softly as a line drive cracks down the third-base line.

**JEFF**
That’s three RBIs—Jesus. Where the hell was this offense last week?

**KATHY**
They’re doing this just to test me, you know.

**JEFF**
What?

**KATHY**
The Reds.

**JEFF** (laughs, a little nervously)
Oh, c’mon, it’s just…I mean, this is wild, right? Look at that scoreboard.

**KATHY**
I am. It’s mocking me.

She leans back into the couch, arms crossed—half in jest, half in actual frustration. She’s flushed, restless, biting the inside of her cheek, holding on to her patience by a thread.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
You were literally unzipped thirty minutes ago. What the hell is happening?  Cincinnati’s cuckolding me.

**JEFF** (still oblivious)
Okay, that’s nine! That’s nine runs! This is insane.

**KATHY** (under her breath)
So is my self-control.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
I didn’t notice her shifting. Didn’t notice the arms crossing.  Because the Reds were on fire.  And I forgot—for a second—what was waiting beside me.

---

## **INT. JEFF’S BEDROOM – 11:58 P.M.**

The Reds are up by nine. The Rosie Reds are their feet in San Francisco.  But the crowd in this room is just two people, and one of them is losing her patience.  **KATHY** sits rigid now, arms folded, one eyebrow twitching. She glances over—sees **JEFF** looking at her.

Hard.
