Mm-hmm.

There’s a pause, two women working side by side, slicing and stirring, letting the moment stretch.

Then:

**JO ANN** (CONT’D)
He a good one?

**KATHY** freezes, hand half-extended for the garlic powder. Doesn’t look up. No blush. But her lips curve, small and completely unguarded.

**KATHY**
He’s a weird one. But yeah. I think he might be.

**JO ANN** doesn’t press. She just pats her daughter’s shoulder as she passes for the oven mitts.

**JO ANN**
Good. Weird lasts longer than handsome.

They go back to cooking, kitchen bright and easy as a summer Sunday, the whole world feeling lighter than it did the week before.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
She knew. Of course she knew. Moms never need the play-by-play—just a clean head of hair and a real smile on a Sunday afternoon.

---

## **INT. KITCHEN – KATHY’S MOM’S HOUSE – SUNDAY, 12:26 P.M.**

**KATHY** pours salad into a bowl. **JO ANN** is sliding the green bean casserole into a baking dish, the kitchen blooming with comfort food and sly intent. There’s jazz, there’s clatter, there’s an ease—until her mother tilts the world, just a notch.

**JO ANN**
By the way, just so it’s on record—I’m not ready to be a grandmother. Ten years, minimum. Maybe twelve.

**KATHY** freezes, salad spoon mid-air, brow cocked.

**KATHY**
Did you just bring up grandkids while I’m still trying to figure out if he knows how to use a calendar?

**JO ANN**
Timing is everything. Also—

(passive as the weather)
Please pass the ranch.

**KATHY** sighs, digging the bottle out of the fridge.

**KATHY**
This is why I don’t bring men home.

**JO ANN**
I didn’t ask to meet him. I asked for dressing.

She takes the ranch, gives a little nod of Midwest satisfaction.

**JO ANN** (CONT’D)
This is the Midwest, Katherine. Ranch goes on everything. Salads. Pizza. Questionable life choices.

**KATHY** laughs, shaking her head as she tosses the salad.

**KATHY**
You terrify me sometimes.

**JO ANN**
That’s how you know I’m good at this.

They clink forks and keep prepping, no sermon, no heat—just casual, layered advice: ranch, warnings, love. Safety talks and sex ed, all laced with humor.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
She said it like a joke. But she meant it. And somehow, that made me feel safe. Even if I have no idea where this is going. Yet.

---

## **EXT. PUTT-PUTT COURSE – LATE SUNDAY AFTERNOON – 5:12 P.M.**

The sun’s dropped low, stretching shadows across cheap astroturf and the battered volcano hole. **JIM**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** are on hole 12. One ball floats in a pirate-ship water trap, bees circle Mountain Dew, and every third word is profanity.

**JIM**
That’s bullshit. I didn’t even hit it that hard.

**BILL**
You bounced it off the clown’s uvula, **JIM**.

**JIM**
That clown’s got a vendetta.

**JEREMY** lines up his shot like a monk preparing tea—sinks it in two. He barely reacts.

**JEREMY**
Precision. Not power.

They gather their clubs, head inside—air-conditioning and arcade haze, the promise of ticket stubs and old nachos.

---

## **INT. ARCADE – 5:32 P.M.**

The NBA Jam cabinet glows with holy purpose. The announcer’s voice slings 90s basketball like prophecy.

**NBA JAM ANNOUNCER** (CABINET)
MIKE IUZZOLINO!
CAN’T BUY A BUCKET!
FROM DOWNTOWN!
HE’S ON FIRE!

**BILL**
Did anyone ever figure out who Mike Iuzzolino was?

**JIM**
That man has haunted my dreams.

**JEREMY**
He’s the reason I fear Italians.

They button-mash, cackle, shove—timing their trash talk to every buzzer and pixelated slam dunk.  After a brutal jam, **JIM** narrows his eyes.

**JIM**
Alright. How bad was the airshow?

**JEREMY**
You mean the labor camp?

**BILL**
You ever been waterboarded with crushed ice?

**JIM**
That bad?

**JEREMY**
We were in a freezer truck for over an hour. **KATHY** nearly punched a colonel. We got T-shirts.

**BILL**
It was hell. But then the Thunderbirds flew.

**JIM**
So I missed everything.

**NBA JAM CABINET**
MIKE IUZZOLINO!
BOOMSHAKALAKA!

**JEREMY**
You missed the pain. The glory. The meat sweats. Next year you’re on airshow crew.

**JIM**
Let me finish dunking on this pixelated fucker, then we’ll talk.

Laughter, flashing lights, the background wail of a jammed skee-ball machine. Boys in orbit. Everything as it should be.

**JIM (V.O.)**
They survived something. Now I gotta catch up—preferably without frostbite.

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – MALL FOOD COURT – SUNDAY EVENING – 6:41 P.M.**

The fluorescent lights hum with the threat of migraines. Everything smells like reconstituted beef and industrial-grade citrus. **JIM**, **BILL**, and **JEREMY** sprawl in the corner booth—dead center between the mall’s dwindling Sunday crowd and the stained-glass glare of the Baptist church’s parking lot signs. Empty Mountain Dew cups, stray nacho chips, and the last remains of Crunchwraps scatter between them.

**JIM** (leaning back, eyeing **JEREMY**)
I still don’t get how your dad conjures tickets out of thin air. Def Leppard? Backstage? That’s made up.

**JEREMY**
It’s never thin air. It’s quid pro quo.

**BILL**
Latin at Taco Bell. Christ, we’re doomed.

**JEREMY**
Some sales guy gets comped arena seats—pavilion, whatever—but can’t fill ‘em. So he trades. Maybe he needs a 6 A.M. keg drop-off. Maybe he wants a surprise shipment of Zima. Maybe he needs Wednesday’s order swapped to Thursday because he’s got a tee time. That’s the trick. We get the tickets.

**JIM**
That’s…depressingly rational.

**JEREMY**
That’s the family business. I got comped tickets before I got braces. Didn’t know people actually paid for concerts until sophomore year.

**BILL**
My dad paid for Huey Lewis in ’87.

**JEREMY**
And that was his first mistake.

Their laughter is half-delirious from salt, sugar, and the psychic fatigue of living in southwest Ohio. **JEREMY** crunches his taco, points toward the Baptist church with solemn mockery.

**JEREMY** (CONT’D)
That’s the Baptist Quadrant. No booze. No cards. No dancing. Definitely no fucking.

**JIM**
No fun.

**BILL**
No grace.

**JEREMY**
And yet, 300 yards west, behold: tacos and the barter economy of Dayton’s entire liquor black market.

**JIM**
Alcohol: the universal solvent.

**JEREMY**
Barter: the universal currency.

They lift their cups in a benediction—plastic clunk, all ice and sticky regret.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
The economy’s not cash. It’s favors. It’s knowing who needs what, and what you’ve got to swap. Even if it’s just Zima and a Ford van with no brakes.

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – MALL FOOD COURT – SUNDAY EVENING – 6:53 P.M.**

Fourth round of Mountain Dew, trash talk at fever pitch, the sun slipping behind the Baptist church across the parking lot. Then the doors swing open and the gravitational field in the food court shifts.

**JEFF CREMEANS** enters, decked out in full Sunday Best: pressed khakis, white shirt, tie still buttoned up, hair parted with the precision of a man raised on hymns and hardware stores. He beelines for the soda fountain, a prophet in a land of melted cheese.

The booth goes quiet. Watching him is like watching a high-wire act.

**JIM**
Is that…?

**BILL**
**CREMEANS**.

**JEREMY**
Something’s about to happen.

They watch as **CREMEANS** grabs a cup. He stands in front of the machine. Instead of the sacred Mountain Dew, he fills it—slowly, methodically—with sweet iced tea.

**JIM** (quiet, panicked)
No. No, he wouldn’t.

**BILL**
Don’t look at him. That’s not our Cremeans.

**JEREMY** (dead serious)
If he drinks that, we run.

Cremeans turns, holding the cup of tea. He surveys them—makes direct eye contact. The table is dead silent, half-expecting to see his skin peel back and reveal a Soviet android.

Then, without breaking gaze, **CREMEANS** cracks a grin, grabs a second cup—and crucially—fills the cup to the brim with Mountain Dew. The booth erupts in relieved, nervous laughter. Balance restored. Universe untwisted.

**JIM**
You fucker. I almost had a heart attack.

**BILL**
I was gonna call your mom.

**JEREMY**
Never do that again, man. That’s how timelines split.

**CREMEANS** just grins, lifts the Dew in salute, and slides into the booth—right as Marcy enters, sundress, wee too much cleavage, and a kiss on the cheek, the whole package.

**JIM** (V.O.)
Some people cause chaos on purpose. **CREMEANS** *is* chaos on purpose. If he ever actually drinks tea, that’s when we get the shotguns.

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – MALL FOOD COURT – SUNDAY EVENING – 6:56 P.M.**

They’re frozen, hands half-raised, tacos suspended like weapons in a standoff. **CREMEANS**, stone-faced, holds out the iced tea to Marcy, who takes it with both hands—ceremonial, like the passing of the Holy Grail at Vacation Bible School. He turns back, fills his own cup with Mountain Dew. The order of the universe reestablished.

He turns, catches their gaze, and winks—a flash of secret knowledge, then slides in beside Marcy, who’s already laughing at something only he would dare say in public.

**BILL**
Okay, false alarm. Tea was never his.

**JIM**
Which means he’s still **CREMEANS**.

**JEREMY**
Yeah, but I need a minute. That was almost a paradigm shift.

They try not to stare, but Marcy’s magnetic—Sunday best, confidence for days, sharp as a youth pastor’s side-eye. Not just pretty: calculated. Present. Every bit a match for his chaos.

**CREMEANS** is the calm in the center of the swirl, eating like he’s just won a bet against God.

**JIM**
You think he’s ever tapped that?

A glance between them, silent, instant consensus.

**ALL THREE**
No.

**BILL**
Not unless there’s a ring, a contract, and a parental blessing.

**JIM**
Church wedding. Full choir. Handwritten vows.

**JEREMY**
And only then. Once. Probably on a Wednesday.

**BILL**
Lights off, shoes on, missionary, with a notarized affidavit and a morning-after testimony at youth group.

**JIM**
He’s not just waiting for marriage. He’s waiting for the offertory hymn after communion.

They nearly lose it, stifling laughter so hard their eyes water. Nobody wants to risk **CREMEANS** picking up the wavelength—because if anyone can hear irreverence from across space and time, it’s him.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
There’s everyday weird. Then there’s **CREMEANS** weird. Somewhere between Mountain Dew, the choir girl, and that wink…you realize: whatever’s happening, you’ll never know the whole story—unless you’re rolling nat 20s on Perception.

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – MALL FOOD COURT – SUNDAY EVENING – 7:11 P.M.**

**CREMEANS** and Marcy are off in their own little orbit, two booths away, deep in theological flirtation or whatever passes for a date in their strange, parallel universe. Meanwhile, the rest of the band leans in, elbows on fake woodgrain, wrappers pushed aside, the moment stretching between them.

**JIM** finally breaks the silence, no preamble, just the raw question:

**JIM**
Hey. How well do you guys really know **CREMEANS**?

**BILL**
Better than we want to. Why?

**JIM**
I’m in two classes with him this summer at Wright State. Business electives. Intro to Finance and Organizational Theory. The guy is…

(pauses, searching)
Otherworldly.

**JEREMY**
As in, actually good?

**JIM**
As in, untouchable. Doesn’t argue, doesn’t grandstand. The professors start a topic—he’s already past it. He fixes case studies one-handed, eating Egg McMuffins. He’s bored, you can tell. It’s like he’s running four classes in his head just to keep from falling asleep.

That sinks in. Each of them glances at **CREMEANS**, who seems oblivious, and yet somehow you know he heard every word.

**JIM** (CONT’D)
Made me think, you know? What am I doing? Sitting in classes I don’t care about, keeping to a path I never even chose. But then there’s the band. There’s the garage. There’s you idiots. What if we got out of **GILLEY**’s garage? What if we went for it—really went for it? On the road, out of Dayton, chasing something bigger?

He looks them both in the eye now. There’s no punchline coming.

**JIM** (CONT’D)
I’d be a real musician. Not just a kid screwing around—living the dream for once.

There’s a long, honest silence. Just the sound of soda machines and the sun crawling down the glass.  **JEREMY** breaks it:

**JEREMY**
You think we can get there?

**JIM**
I don’t know. But I keep thinking about not going back.

**BILL**
Because of **CREMEANS**?

**JIM**
Because of us. Because this doesn’t feel like a joke anymore.

Three guys, the remains of dinner, and an idea that feels dangerous because it just might be true.

**JIM (V.O.)**
**CREMEANS** could build an empire. Me? I just want a van, a gig, a setlist that means something. I want one shot to be more than the guy who never tried.

---

## **INT. TACO BELL – SUNDAY EVENING – 7:18 P.M.**

The lights above buzz and flicker—judging, maybe, or bearing witness. **JIM** has just dropped the “maybe I don’t go back” bomb. The air is heavy. Then **JEREMY** sits up, serious for once.

**JEREMY**
Alright. Real talk.

**BILL**
That’s not usually your brand.

**JEREMY**
I’ve gamed with **CREMEANS** for years. Hundreds of hours. Tabletop, basement RPGs, running campaigns so weird even the vice principal banned us from study hall for a week.  He’s weird—but honest. He never flakes. Not once.

He glances over—**CREMEANS** and Marcy are sharing a cinnamon twist, like it’s their first communion.

**JEREMY** (CONT’D)
What if he managed us?

**BILL**
Managed—like a real band?

**JIM**
Set lists. Promo. Phone calls. Booking.

**BILL**
How do we even pay him? If it’s trucker rules—ass, grass, or gas—we’re gonna have to get creative. What do you buy for a guy who’s half accountant, half paladin?

**JIM**
We made sixty bucks at W.O. Wright’s. I blew mine on drumsticks and tacos. Not exactly flush.

**JEREMY**
He doesn’t need the money. He needs a puzzle. Give him our chaos, he’ll color-code the whole tour, with bonus points for side quests and emotional damage mitigation.

**BILL**
Dungeon Manager.

**JIM**
Dungeon Master *and* band manager. It fits. He’d follow us straight into the abyss and book a return ticket.

They look over at **CREMEANS**, who raises his Mountain Dew, like he’s been summoned by prophecy.

**JIM (V.O.)**
Bands don’t start with glory. They start with a dumb idea at Taco Bell, and the impossible hope that maybe, just maybe, you’re not a punchline after all.

---

# **CHAPTER EIGHT: LIVING UNDER UV LIGHT**

---

## **EXT. BETHEL TOWNSHIP FARMLAND – DAY – MID-OCTOBER 1990**

Corn stands ready for the combine. Trees are a riot of red and gold. Cold, dry wind, a combine chewing through a field, distant crickets. You can almost hear the sun snap as it sets.

**EXT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – DAY**

Garage door flung wide. Band gear littering the floor. A mess of extension cords, pedals, empty Coke cans. The air is cold enough to see their breath, and every sound is sharper for it.

**JEFF** is mid-speech, arms moving, earnest and—let’s be honest—completely out of touch.

**JEFF**
I was never the devious type. My wildest act freshman year at Wright State was working the typing lab. Really. Three hours of homework and, sometimes, *actual conversation.* One May afternoon, me and a coworker started talking about—well—sex.

**GILLEY**
Whoa, whoa. Typing lab scandal? Did you rearrange the keys, rebel?

**BILL**
What next, Jeff, swapping out typewriter ribbons? Hardcore.

**JEFF** (unfazed)
I told her, flat out—I’d never had sex. I was a virgin.

**GILLEY** (mock horror)
You told her? Like, with words?

**BILL**
Damn, Jeff, you just handed her the playbook!

**JEFF**
And then, right as we’re closing up, she looks at me and goes, “We shall have to remedy that.” Like it’s a prescription or something.

**GILLEY**
She *said* that? No way. Did she wink? Was there tongue action?

**BILL**
Did her glasses fog up, man?

**JEFF**
I don’t remember. I was preoccupied. Honestly, I wasn’t sure she meant it. I went home and did nothing. That seemed…safe.

(Cut: Gilley and Bill share a look—this is peak Jeff.)

Just then, **KATHY** appears in the doorway. She catches only the tail end, missing the “virginity lost” reveal. She’s curious, but the tone already puts her on guard.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS**

**JEFF**
Next day, first thing out of her mouth: “Are you prepared?” No context. I’m staring at her like she’s assigned me a group project.

**GILLEY**
Prepared for *what,* man? Is this a health class skit?

**BILL**
Yeah, you bring your number two pencil?

**JEFF**
I say I need to get condoms. I mean, what else do you say? So I hit every vending machine in Millet Hall. Sodas, erasers, mechanical pencils—no condoms. Greek tragedy.

**GILLEY** (doubled over)
Jeff’s sexual awakening, derailed by vending inventory!

**BILL**
You’re the Odysseus of campus contraceptives.

**GILLEY** (doubled over, crying with laughter)
Jeff’s sexual awakening—derailed by vending inventory!

The guys howl, the garage echoing with mock-heroic praise.

**JEFF** doesn’t laugh with them. His eyes drift to the rafters, voice flat and private.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
The world never looks the same twice. For most people, it’s daylight and shadow. For me, it’s something harsher—like living under a blacklight. Every flaw glows.

He blinks, snaps back, and shrugs off the silence.

**JEFF**
Anyway, so then I’m sprinting across campus to the Geo—Speedway, third stop. Wall of condoms. And I’m just…frozen. Like I’m picking a lock to my own execution.

**GILLEY** (wheezing)
Speedway? What the ever lovin' hell, Jeff!

**BILL**
Grab a Slim Jim while you’re at it, Romeo!

Across the garage, **KATHY** folds her arms tighter, jaw set.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Why her? Why not me?

The guys, meanwhile, are egging Jeff on, loving every cringe.

**GILLEY**
Did you ever get the damn condoms, or did you just turn into a monk?

**JEFF**
Slow down, G-man.  Let me remember this properly.

**BILL**
Legend. Jeff Evans, sex hero.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He’s so goddamn clueless.

She turns her gaze away, hiding a flush that is equal parts frustration, embarrassment, and a tiny charge of desire. Gilley catches her expression, gives a sly smile.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Maybe I need a new story of my own.

She doesn’t let herself finish the thought. Not yet.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – DAY**

The garage is cold and echoing. **JEFF** is mid-monologue, his voice gone half-brag, half-confessional. **GILLEY** and **BILL** are losing it, egging him on with every dumb detail.

**JEFF**
I remember from orientation there was this self-service station by the dorms—supposed to have everything. So, you know, another quarter-mile hike. For science.

**GILLEY** (wiping his eyes)
A quarter-mile trek for Trojans. You’re a pioneer, Jeff.

**BILL**
That’s dedication. The Wright Brothers had it easier.

**JEFF**
I get there—nothing. Nada. It’s like fate is against me.

He lets the silence hang.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
So now I’m desperate. There’s a woman who wants me—like, actually wants to do it—and I am running out of time, and condoms, and apparently basic dignity.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Tick-tock. The universe had started the countdown, and I was fumbling the clock.

**GILLEY**
You sweating yet, big guy?

**BILL**
You must’ve looked like a hostage on TV.

Across the garage, **KATHY** flinches. Sympathy, for half a second—then irritation, then something hotter and meaner.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
God, he’s so…helpless. And kind of—adorable? But why do I feel…jealous?

She can feel her face burn, arms crossed tight. Why is she angry? Why is she *turned on*? She clamps her jaw, determined not to show it.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He’s making this into a quest for another girl. Not me. Why not me?

Her pulse is thumping—equal parts anger and the reckless thrill of a dare.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Screw it. I’m getting laid tonight.

She makes the decision, hard and bright as glass.

**JEFF**
So I haul ass all the way across campus to my Geo Metro. One more hike, one more test. Speedway, Col. Glenn Highway—the Promised Land. Wall of condoms. The anxiety of too much choice. Do I go cheap? Do I go brand name? Colors? Ribs? Flavors? Who the hell are these even for?

He mimics the struggle, voice pitching up in faux-panic.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I just grab whatever I can reach and pay. Nearly died at the register, but I survived. I lived to tell the tale.

**GILLEY** (V.O.)
I’m watching Kathy out of the corner of my eye. She’s not just mad. She’s lit up. That’s not anger—that’s a challenge. I can work with that.

**BILL (V.O.)**
Best. Story. Ever. We should sell tickets.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – DAY**

**JEFF** is in full saga mode now—part comedy, part confession, his voice riding the edge of self-mockery and triumph. **GILLEY** and **BILL** are barely holding it together, howling at every twist.

**JEFF**
So now I’m driving back, parking, hiking across campus, sweating like I’m in a hostage video. Forty-five minutes later, I’m a mile from where I ought to be, no way to call her, convinced she’s left or called campus police.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
I’m the knight on a quest, except the dragon is a vending machine and the princess is probably grading midterms by now. My horse is a Geo Metro, and I’m late for my own coronation.

**JEFF**
I was sure I’d blown it. My moment, my story—done before it started.

**GILLEY** (howling)
You were about to blow your shot, man!

**BILL**
Friend-zoned by fate and the condom gods!

**JEFF**
But I go back. Quad, third floor, typing lab. I’m shaking like I’ve just cheated death. No memory of that walk—just tunnel vision.

**(QUICK CUTS:)**
Jeff’s sweaty hands. His foot tapping. The clock on the wall, hands spinning, time out of sync.

**JEFF**
I open the door. She says, “What took you so long?”

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Like I’d just gone to get a Dew, not cross the goddamn Rubicon.

**JEFF**
I tell her, “I had to go to Speedway.”

**GILLEY** (gasping)
Speedway! The pilgrimage for love!

**BILL**
Yeah, next time pick up a Slim Jim, Romeo!

**JEFF**
Then she says, “Oh. I made a spot and a sign. Lock the door.”

**JEFF (V.O.)**
That’s when I knew—this wasn’t a quiz. This was the real thing.

He glances—*directly at the camera, breaking the fourth wall.*

**JEFF**
Her name was Diane. Senior, tiny, chipper, glasses, super nice. Not what you’d expect. Flat-chested, brown nipples, bush trimmed a little, always smiling.

**KATHY** recoils at the naked, clinical inventory—a look of offense, insult, and jealousy colliding.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Brown nipples? Trimmed bush? That’s his takeaway? I cannot believe this is what stuck. This is personal.

She’s furious, and, beneath it, aching. Why *her*? Why *not* me?

**JEFF**
Anyway—things got funnier after that.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Five years later, I wrote *“Typing Lab.”* Top 40. Kathy took her anger—turned it into *“Why Her and Not Me?”* That one hit number one. You tell me who came out ahead.

**GILLEY** and **BILL** are in tears, barely breathing. **KATHY** is a storm—aroused, angry, intensely alive. She locks eyes with **GILLEY**, silent challenge burning.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
The ice queen’s melting. My timing is perfect.

He grins, all teeth, returning her look. This is the moment he’s been waiting for—and Kathy, for once, is going to let it rip.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – DAY**

The guys are still wiping laughter from their eyes, breathless, faces red. **KATHY**’s clearing her throat is like a gunshot; the energy in the garage snaps from raucous to alert in half a second.

**GILLEY** (still half-laughing, trying to play it cool)
Well, shit. Didn’t see you standing there, **KATHY**.

**BILL** (grinning, sheepish)
Yeah, uh—didn’t mean to scare you off.

**JEFF** (awkward, earnest)
Just telling stories. You know. Classic guy material.

**KATHY** arches an eyebrow, voice all steel.
Right. Guy shit.

Just then **JEREMY** and **JIM** come through the door, amps and snare balanced, half-tuned, already sensing the static.

**JEREMY** (spotting the tension)
What, we miss the afterparty?

**JIM** (dropping his bag)
No, just the punchline.

**GILLEY** waves it off.
Just **JEFF** being…very, very **JEFF**.

The band settles into a new, jagged rhythm—cords coiling, knobs twisting, the music about to break the silence.

**KATHY** slips over to **GILLEY**, close enough to feel the heat off his skin. No hesitation, just want.

**KATHY** (low, private, all business)
I’m wet right now.

**GILLEY** freezes, then recovers—cool as hell, one eyebrow up, dangerous smile flickering.

**KATHY** (quieter still)
After practice. No bullshit. I want you.

She reaches into her pocket, flashes a three-pack of condoms between her fingers—silver glint, no shame.

**KATHY** (a beat, softer)
I came prepared.

**GILLEY**’s eyes go dark and hungry.
Never doubted you, not once.

**JEREMY** (not looking up from his amp, deadpan)
You’ll want a four-pack.

The tiniest crack appears in **KATHY**’s composure. She ignores him.

**KATHY** (to **GILLEY**, matching his cool)
Don’t worry. I’ll improvise.

Their eyes lock—battle lines drawn, anticipation thick in the air.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He wasn’t shocked. He was ready. That’s what scared me. That’s what made me want it more.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
Hell yes. Finally, the temperature’s right.

## **INT. W. O. WRIGHT’S COLLEGE BAR – NIGHT – LATE FEBRUARY 1991**

The jukebox is silent. Every TV glows with desert fire. CNN runs on a loop: night vision green, maps crawling with arrows, anchors who look more tired every night. Half the bar wears camo. The other half looks guilty for not.

**KATHY**
No.

She shoves cash at the register, tucks the bag under her arm, and walks out. The neon pharmacy cross flickers overhead, one tube dead, buzzing in the daylight.

---

## **EXT. PARK LAYNE DRUGSTORE PARKING LOT – CONTINUOUS**

In the car, she sits. The bag is silent on her lap. She takes out the blister pack. No water. Swallows one, then the next. Her throat works hard.  For a moment, she stares straight ahead at the golden arches.  Her reflection in the windshield is gray, tired.  She hits EJECT on the tape deck; the band’s latest demo spits out. She doesn’t even look at it.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Just like buying gum.

But her hand trembles a little on the keys.  She wonders, not really asking:  Is this a good day to skip practice?  The answer doesn’t come. She just sits. Alone. The world rushes by on Dayton-Lakeview. She feels nothing, but she knows the feeling will return. Later.

**(SOUND):** Wind. Muzak leaking through the drugstore door. A faint, ghostly memory of Def Leppard’s “*Animal*” rides the air, gone before it can finish a chorus.)

**FINAL IMAGE:**
Kathy, alone in her car. The McDonald’s sign looms—bright, monstrous, indifferent. Her consequence, her secret, her cost.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S FAMILY DRIVEWAY – LATE AFTERNOON – CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY**’s car rolls up, dust and gravel popping beneath the wheels. The sun is low and cold. Band cars already line the yard. The garage door is propped open. Inside, faint music and shifting shadows.

At the end of the driveway, **MR. GILLEY** fumbles with the mailbox, head down in the wind.

For a split second, **KATHY** remembers him at her first gig: *You’re the best thing that ever happened to this band, kiddo. Don’t forget it.*

That memory flashes, cuts—then reality:

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He believed in me.  And I…I just let everything get out of my hands.

She straightens her coat. This is her line in the sand.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
It’s my body. My mess to fix. Never again.

She squares her shoulders and heads toward the music.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – CONTINUOUS**

It’s chaos, but good chaos—guitar cases, cables, amps, chatter.  **GILLEY** isn’t in the room.  **JEFF** and **JIM** are in deep conversation by the tool bench. **BILL** is hunched over his keyboard, tuning up.  **KATHY** steps in, command in her walk, but this time she avoids **JEFF**’s eyes. She locks in on **GILLEY** reentering from the house. Just a subtle shake of her head: Not today. Not again.  He nods, expression unreadable. He gets it.

She goes to **JIM**.

**KATHY** (level, purposeful)
JIM, I need your help.

**JIM** (surprised, genuinely interested)
With what?

**KATHY**
I need a piano. For real. I want to learn. I want to add it.

**BILL** (half-joking, a little threatened)
But…I play keys.

**KATHY** (gentle, but unwavering)
You play whatever a song needs, Bill. That’s why you’re good. Don’t box yourself in with that Casio.

She looks back to **JIM**.

**KATHY**
You know where I can get one?

**JIM** (warming, already making plans)
If there’s one in the township, I’ll find it.

**KATHY**
And violin, Bill. Can you dust that off, too?

**BILL** (shrugs, half-smiling)
Sure, if Jim gets me one.

She’s already moving on, the energy different now—a little more adult, a little more focused.

The room shifts. **JEFF** finally notices, tries to catch her as the band wraps up. He steps out of his lane, voice almost shy:

**JEFF**
Hey, **KATHY**…You wanna…take a drive? Just around?

There’s that old awkward, good-hearted earnestness. For a moment, she softens—just a bit.

**KATHY** (tired, but not unkind)
Thanks, Jeff. But I think I’m just gonna head home.

**JEFF** tries to hide his disappointment, then perks up. He digs out a cassette, its homemade label rough and cheap.

**JEFF**
Wait—before you go.  You gotta check this out.

He hands her the tape:  A grainy black-and-white photo, an outstretched hand, “*Up In It*” in block letters.

**KATHY** (reading, skeptical)
The Afghan Whigs?

**JEFF** (a little nerdy, a little hopeful)
Yeah. Their demo, before they blew up.  It’s wild. Gritty. We could totally steal half their sound.

She turns the tape over in her hand, her face unreadable.  She almost says yes. She almost asks him to walk her out.

**KATHY** (soft, decisive)
Thanks, Jeff. Really. But…not today.

She hands it back. For a moment, **JEFF** hesitates—then just smiles and puts it in his pocket.  She leaves, quiet but upright, out the garage and into the last light of day.  **JEFF** stands in the mess, tape in hand, just a silhouette against the clutter and the gold of the dying sun.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S FAMILY DRIVEWAY – EVENING – CONTINUOUS**

Winter light is dying, cold wind sweeping across the bare gravel. **KATHY** moves briskly, boots biting into the ice, her face set in that way only exhaustion brings. She scrapes the last stubborn patch of frost from her windshield, each drag of plastic on glass louder than her own thoughts.  She climbs inside, breath steaming, hands shaking as she fumbles with the ignition. Headlights blink to life. Out of the corner of her eye—a shape. **JIM**, already there by the door, hands jammed in his jacket, jaw clenched.

She jumps. Tries the window—frozen. Sighs, pops the door.

**JIM** (voice tight, barely keeping it together)
What the hell was that, Kathy?

**KATHY** (tired, wary)
Not now, Jim. I just need to go.

**JIM** (leans in, voice sharp)
No—you don’t get to just go. You think Jeff’s an idiot? You think I’m an idiot? He doesn’t get it. You know he doesn’t get it. And you—

(shakes head, angry)
You were basically drawing him a fucking map.

Kathy looks away, her hands tight on the wheel.

**KATHY** (defensive, brittle)
I wasn’t—
(stops herself)

**JIM** (cuts her off)
Yes, you were. He missed every single sign. Every look, every word. He’s not built for this, Kathy. He’s not built for…games.

He pauses, voice lowering, a little more gentle.

**JIM (CONT’D)**
We talked. Last night. He’s trying, you know? Actually trying.

(takes a breath)
But listening goes both ways. You can’t just expect him to know.

Kathy doesn’t look at him, jaw working.

**KATHY** (quiet)
Is it…too late?

**JIM** (soft, almost laughing)
With Jeff? You could disappear for ten years, call him tomorrow, he’d start right back up.

(beat, more serious)
But if he ever figures out how to *feel* about all this…how to actually read what’s happening…

(beat)
That’s when it changes, Kathy. For all of us.

He meets her eyes, serious, direct.

**JIM (CONT’D)**
So be grateful he doesn’t get it yet. Because next time?

(pause)
Next time you won’t get a free pass.

Long silence. The wind rattles the car. Kathy’s eyes fill, but she blinks it away.

**KATHY** (voice small)
Jim…I’m sorry. I’m just…I’m a mess.

He reaches out—a friendly hand, nothing more. She flinches, sharp.

**KATHY (CONT’D)**
Don’t. Please. Just—don’t touch me.

He pulls back, stung.

**JIM** (quiet, trying one last time)
Kathy…

**KATHY** (broken, desperate)
I said—leave me the fuck alone!

She slams the door, locks it. Sits in the sudden silence, staring straight ahead.

Jim stands outside, hands shoved deep in his pockets, snow drifting around his feet. He stays there, just watching her taillights recede, the sound of the wind swallowing up whatever he might have said.

---

## **INT. KATHY’S CAR – DRIVEWAY – NIGHT**

**KATHY** grips the wheel, forehead pressed to cold vinyl. Tears stream down, quiet at first, then harder—raw, silent, not for anyone but herself.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
What am I even doing?

She wipes her cheeks, fingers shaking. A strangled laugh, then another sob. For a moment, she just breathes—slow, desperate, trying to pull herself back together.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Sorry, Jeff. Sorry, Jim.  I don’t know how to fix this.

She sits there a while. Finally, she wipes her face one last time, jams the key in the ignition, and drives off into the dark, headlights sweeping over the empty garage, the frost still melting where her hands just were.

---

## **INT. GILLEY’S GARAGE – LATER**

**JEFF** and **JIM** wind cables, stacking amps, the clatter oddly loud in the silence that hangs after a bad fight. No one says much.

**JEFF** (quiet, not looking up)
You think she’ll be okay?

**JIM** (shrugs, tired)
Hope so.

They pack in silence. Then:

**JEFF** (tentative, almost a whisper)
Hey, Jim…

(beat)
Can I ask you something?

**JIM** (looks up, wary)
Shoot.

**JEFF** (awkward, earnest)
It’s…about Kathy.

Jim’s expression softens. He waits.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
I think…I think I like her.

(pause, voice catching)
Not just band stuff. Like…for real.

Jim gives a small, knowing smile.

**JIM**
Yeah, I kinda guessed.

**JEFF**
But I don’t know if…

(trails off, embarrassed)
Forget it.

**JIM** (gentle, a hand on Jeff’s shoulder)
Just talk to her. Like a person.

(beat)
Don’t overthink it.

**JEFF** nods, biting his lip. He pulls his jacket on, pausing at the door.

**JEFF**
Thanks, man.

Jim just nods.

**(VISUAL):** Jeff slips out into the night, his silhouette briefly framed by the porch light before he’s gone.

Jim stands in the garage, still and thoughtful, watching the door. A hint of a smile—equal parts hope and worry.

---

## **INT. GILLEY'S ROOM – NIGHT**

A single bulb, low wattage, glows above the tangled sheets and cluttered guitars. The faint, echoing chords of U2’s “So Cruel” drift in from a stereo just outside the door—music not *for* them, but for the house.

The bed is chaos: Kathy straddling Gilley, the covers half-off the mattress, her knees pressing into his ribs. He’s insistent, hands firm on her hips.

No condom this time. She let him talk her into it, or maybe she didn’t put up much fight. It blurs. She’s not thinking about the future. Not thinking about anything except right now, and not even that, really.

The TV in the corner spits out a steady stream of static and muffled war updates. Somewhere, a general points at a map, lines moving across sand.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
You’re dangerous, you’re beautiful.

She rocks her hips, going through the motions. Gilley grins—teeth flashing in the low light—and she tries to meet his eyes. She tries to summon the electricity from the first time, but her body feels distant, numb, like she’s watching from across the room.

Clothes are everywhere—her tights tangled with his jeans, a crumpled condom wrapper glinting on the floor like a warning sign she’s already ignored.

She arches her back, forces a moan, breathes heavy, trying to remember what it felt like to *want* this.

Gilley’s hands move up her sides, skilled, practiced, sure of themselves. He knows what she likes. Or at least, he knows what most women like. She wonders if that’s good enough.

He leans up, whispering rough into her ear:

**GILLEY (whispering)**
You like it rough, don’t you?

She lets out a noise—half laugh, half sob—then pushes him back, flipping the script, taking control, or pretending to.  She grinds against him, hands digging into his shoulders, nails biting skin. The music swells, Bono’s voice full of accusation and longing.

Her movements become mechanical, precise, like she’s hitting marks in a routine. He can’t see her face now, just the toss of her hair, the arch of her back.  She throws her head back, eyes squeezed shut, mouth open in a practiced *O*. Fakes it. Really, truly fakes it. It’s almost a relief, how easy it is.

Gilley thrusts up into her, grips her hips tight. He finishes with a grunt, face contorted in pleasure and something else—maybe satisfaction, maybe something meaner.

Silence falls, except for the news anchor in the background:
“…coalition forces advancing into Kuwait…”

Kathy collapses beside him, spent. She bites her lip, forcing a smile, staring up at the cracked ceiling. Her heart is pounding but she feels nothing but empty.

**GILLEY** props himself up on one elbow, watching her. He knows—*he knows*—but says nothing. The silence stretches.

She looks away, her smile brittle.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I’m so cruel.

The lamp buzzes. The TV hisses. Outside, somewhere, artillery booms, the sound finding its way through old window glass.

Gilley rolls away. Kathy lies still, eyes open, listening to the war and the sound of her own quiet, useless heartbeat.

---

## **INT. GILLEY'S ROOM – NIGHT**

Not romantic. Just dim and worn out: cheap lightbulb, dirty sheets, stale smoke, the taste of sweat and whiskey thick in the air. The kind of night you forget, if you’re lucky.  A radio plays—thin, bluesy guitar. Not for atmosphere. Just something to fill the silence after.

Gilley, not even bothering to hide it, flicks the unopened condom aside and lets it hit the floor. He flicks Kathy’s breast with two fingers—barely affectionate, barely awake.

**GILLEY** (dry, bored)
Hey. I think this is the last time.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
Spent match. Fizzled fuse. Next spark, please.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
What am I, stray? He feeds me, lets me sleep, then opens the door and expects me to trot off grateful.

Kathy, still in the chemical afterglow, blinks—doesn’t really register what he’s said, not right away.

Gilley leans in, as if closing a deal, not a moment:

**GILLEY (soft, definite)**
Seriously. We can’t keep doing this.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Keep doing *what*? Fucking, or pretending it matters?

She blinks again. Anger starts, slow and cold.

**KATHY (flat, sarcastic)**
Not good enough for you? Or just want something…new?

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
New is always better. New is the point.

He shrugs, naked and casual, as if talking weather.

**GILLEY**
It’s not that, Kathy. It’s the chase. The game. This? This gets boring. It ruins the fun before it starts.

She sits up, confusion hardening into anger.

**KATHY**
Then why the hell did we just *fuck*?

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Maybe if I say it loud enough, it’ll echo back a reason.

He stops, faces her, sheepish, careless.

**GILLEY**
Didn’t hit me until after.

Her jaw clenches, eyebrows knitting.

**KATHY**
Is that normal for guys?

He grins, shrugs again—nothing matters.

**GILLEY**
Normal’s boring.

He tosses out a joke-smile, lets it die.

**GILLEY**
Hard to lie right after.

She meets his eyes, voice flat and raw:

**KATHY**
So how was it…*for you*?

She already knows. He knows she knows.

**GILLEY**
Great. Could get addictive.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
For her. I’m done.

She stands, already half-dressed, pulling her boots on with practiced indifference.

**KATHY**
So, just pretend it never happened?

**GILLEY (quiet, not unkind, just done)**
Yeah. Already have.

She finishes, posture straightening, but her face is drained.

**KATHY (cold, shutting down)**
Fine. See you at practice.

Radio cuts to static. News bulletin, brief, cold: war, casualties, gunfire. Just background.

Gilley starts gathering his things, already moving on.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
Breakfast. Coffee. Find a new game.

Kathy’s V.O. is smaller, jagged:

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I hate him. I hate myself more.

Camera lingers: bed, used condom, rumpled sheets, fading heat. All the evidence of a night that didn’t mean a thing.  Radio lurches into some happy pop song, sugar high, blaring over the mess as the scene cuts.

---

# **CHAPTER NINE: TO GAIN THE WHOLE WORLD**

---

## **EXT. W.O. WRIGHT’S - LOADING DOCK - FRIDAY MORNING**

A bleak June shower hangs over W.O. Wright’s. A beer truck rumbles at the loading dock, engine coughing in the cold. **JEREMY**, bleary-eyed in his battered work jacket, stands next to the driver—a burly guy with hands like catcher's mitts.

**(SOUND:)** Engine rumble, hiss of air brakes, crunch of gravel.)

The driver shoves a stack of delivery sheets at **JEREMY**.

**DRIVER**
Alright, kid. Here’s the damage.

Jeremy flips through three dense pages—his jaw drops.

**JEREMY** (Total disbelief)
Twenty-three thousand nine hundred?

**DRIVER** (Whistles)
Somebody had a hell of a party. This is triple the usual. Gonna take us an hour.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Six A.M., moving twenty-four grand worth of beer. This is not the rock-and-roll life I imagined.

---

## **EXT./INT. W.O. WRIGHT’S - END OF MAY 1991**

**Jeremy** and the driver haul endless stacks of beer—sweat, grunts, dollies squeaking over puddles and mud. Inside, kitchen staff roll out pizza dough, the manager looking like he hasn’t slept in days.

**(SOUND):** Beer cases thumping, muffled cursing, breath mist in the freezing air.)

Finally, the last dolly clatters into the storage room. **Jeremy** sags against a wall, staring at the mountain of beer.

**JEREMY**
What the hell happened?

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Seriously—did a fraternity throw a convention in here?

The manager, not recognizing **Jeremy** as anyone but “the beer kid,” answers without looking up.

**MANAGER**
Tuesday night. Live show. We got *wiped out*.

**JEREMY**
Wiped out? You ran out of beer?

**MANAGER**
Every tap, every bottle. It was chaos.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Running out of beer at W.O. Wright’s—that’s like running out of oxygen at an oxygen bar.

The driver groans, massaging his back.

**DRIVER**
This is two tons, easy. I need a chiropractor.

**MANAGER** (Looking at the stacks, calculating)
With markup? That’s sixty grand of beer. All of it moves in a week.

**Jeremy**’s jaw drops again.

**JEREMY**
Sixty thousand dollars?

He stares at the stacks—no longer beer, but pure, uncut cash.

**(VISUAL):** Quick pan: stacks of Coors, Miller, and Rolling Rock—suddenly golden, precious.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
The empty, echoing bar. **Jeremy**, suddenly aware: this is big money—if you know how to move it.

---

## **INT. BEER WAREHOUSE – LATER**

The beer truck is empty, the warehouse echoing with the end-of-shift chaos: drivers hurrying to clock out, forklifts buzzing past, and the low hum of fluorescent lights overhead. The air is cool, sharp with the scent of hops.

**JEREMY** pushes through the crowd, searching for his dad near the cluttered computer station.

**JEREMY**
Dad!

**DAD** (looks up, tired but warm)
Hey, kiddo. Long day?

**JEREMY**
That W.O. Wright’s order…it was nuts.

**DAD**
Yeah, I heard. What’s up?

**JEREMY**
It was like a Wal-Mart order. How does a bar need that much beer?

**DAD** (grins, tapping the computer)
Want the numbers? Come see, son.

He brings up the W.O. Wright’s account: an ASCII graph, recent orders spiking off the chart.

**DAD**
Five times their usual. Take a look.

**JEREMY**
Five times?

**DAD** (nodding, pointing to the screen)
And check out the pattern—always after certain nights. Spiky as hell.

**JEREMY**
Why?

**DAD**
That’s a sales question, not warehouse.

He points toward the lone **SALESMAN** packing up.

**JEREMY**
Thanks, Dad.

**(JEREMY charges across the warehouse, hopping into a forklift, blaring the horn. Workers scatter. The camera follows—kinetic, almost absurd.)**

He screeches to a halt beside the salesman.

**JEREMY**
Dude!

**SALESMAN** (recognizing him, grinning)
Dude!

(They chest bump, the salesman wincing at the beer grime.)

**JEREMY**
You got a sec?

**SALESMAN**
For you? Always. Owe you from those Slaughterhouse passes.

**JEREMY**
Don’t worry about it. I need info. W.O. Wright’s—what’s going on?

**SALESMAN** (smiling, leans in)
It’s the bands, man. Live music. They pack the place. Beer’s flying out the door.

**JEREMY**
Tuesdays?

**SALESMAN** (with a wink)
Especially Tuesdays.

**JEREMY**’s eyes widen.

**JEREMY**
Wait—us?

**SALESMAN** (nods, grinning)
You got it.

**(The warehouse suddenly feels electric. JEREMY stands in the middle, beer stains on his shirt, realizing the band is a business engine now. The moment lands—hard.)**

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE – DRIVEWAY – EVENING**

Long summer shadows crawl across the driveway as the band packs up after a marathon practice. Instrument cases slam shut. Car doors thud. Voices overlap, already checked out.

**JEREMY** (trying for gravitas, not quite there)
Hey, uh—guys, can I talk to you for a second? When we’re done?

**KATHY**, already pulling on her jacket, waves him off.

**KATHY**
Can’t. Got a date.

**JEFF** (hauling his guitar into **JIM**’s trunk)
Yeah, **JIM** and I have a thing downtown. Another gig, maybe.

**GILLEY** just breezes past, heads inside, hits the garage button. Doesn’t say a word.

**(VISUAL):** Quick cuts: **KATHY** vanishing, **JEFF** and **JIM** slamming doors, **GILLEY** disappearing behind the closing garage. Jeremy, deflated, left holding his news.

He’s alone except for **BILL** and **JIM**.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Crushed it. Really.

**BILL** (grinning, voice low)
No bra. That’s not just a date, that’s a *date*, if you know what I mean.

He nudges **JEREMY**, who rolls his eyes. **JIM** can’t help but snicker.

**JIM (V.O.)**
Maturity level: puddle.

**JEREMY** (dead serious now)
Guys, this isn’t about Kathy’s boobs. Listen. Work today—beer delivery? I unloaded *twenty-four thousand* dollars’ worth at W.O. Wright’s.

That lands. **BILL** and **JIM** stare, not sure they heard right.

**JIM**
Twenty-four grand?

**JEREMY** (nodding, momentum building)
Just from us. Coors, Miller. Sales guy says Bud’s distributor probably did triple that.

**(VISUAL):** Jeremy’s intensity in close-up, then the shift on Bill and Jim’s faces.

**JEREMY** (leaning in, eyes wide)
That’s…eighty-four grand in beer. One bar. One week.

He lets it hang. **BILL** and **JIM** process. The moment stretches, the crickets loud in the suddenly quiet driveway.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Gears turning. You could almost see the smoke.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The camera lingers on **BILL** and **JIM**, surprise and realization dawning. Ordinary night, extraordinary news. The world is shifting under their feet.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE – DRIVEWAY – CONTINUOUS**

Crickets fill the dusk air as three silhouettes stand in the long shadows of the driveway, the world oblivious to what’s just dawned on them.

**(SOUND):** The steady chirping, distant cars, then—)

**JIM** explodes, voice ricocheting off the cold concrete:

**JIM** (blunt, incredulous)
Jesus holy fuck *shitnuggets*! Eighty-four thousand?! We sold *how much* beer? Seriously, Jeremy—how the *fuck* do you know this stuff?

**(VISUAL):** Jim’s eyes bugging out, like someone just handed him a winning lottery ticket and a subpoena at the same time.

**BILL**, still squinting at the numbers in his mind, looks Jeremy up and down, brow furrowed.

**BILL** (wary, half-joking)
Yeah, how *do* you know this? You got a side hustle in espionage we don’t know about?

**BILL (V.O.)**
My brain’s melting. Math trauma.

**JEREMY** rubs his forehead, the straight man in a room full of cartoon characters.

**JEREMY** (patient, a bit dry)
My dad’s the warehouse manager, remember? He showed me the numbers. Then I got it confirmed by the sales guy, who’s so happy he’s shopping for a *car phone* now.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Seriously, car phones. Peak baller move, 1991. You could call NASA from the Taco Bell parking lot.

**BILL** still isn’t there. His face is a Windows 3.0 loading screen.

**BILL** (slow, honestly trying)
A car phone? But…so what, man?

**JIM** (deadpan, like teaching a toddler)
*Bill. We sold the beer.* The bar is just the…middleman. *We* are the reason they ran out.

**(VISUAL):** Bill’s jaw slackens, the lightbulb flickers on. His next word is half awe, half prayer.

**BILL**
…Shit.

**JIM (V.O.)**
Finally. Welcome to the show, Bill.

The three of them stand there as the last sunlight hits, the whole world suddenly bigger, and the crickets still chirping like it’s just any other night.

**(FINAL SHOT):** Their faces—Jim grinning, Jeremy relieved, Bill awestruck—freeze for a beat. Everything’s changed. They just haven’t figured out what to do with it yet.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE – DRIVEWAY – CONTINUOUS**

The crickets are in full Summer riot, their chorus underscoring the slow crash of reality for the three band members.

**JEREMY** glances at his friends, guilt twinging as their excitement fades.

**JEREMY** (soft, apologetic)
Guys…I know this sounds like our “big break” payday, but…We only made eighteen hundred bucks.

**(VISUAL):** Jim’s and Bill’s faces fall, the gears turning behind their eyes. Hope gets replaced by the old familiar sting of disappointment.

**JIM** (genuine disbelief)
Eighteen hundred? But you just said eighty-four thousand in beer sales!

**JEREMY** (grim, nodding)
Yep. That’s what the bar grossed. But our cut? Eighteen hundred. Split six ways.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Three hundred bucks. For all that. Suddenly, being “local legends” felt like bagging groceries.

**BILL** (flat, bitter)
Three hundred dollars. That’s it?

**JEREMY**
That’s it. The bar’s using us to fill the place and keeping the real money. And it’s not just Wright’s. Every bar’s the same game. They pocket the profits, we get…pizza money.

**JIM** (his anger rising)
So we’re just…what? Free labor for their keg night?

**JEREMY** (shrugging)
Pretty much.

The crickets keep up their mocking, relentless chorus.

Suddenly, a dark blue Ford Escort cruises past, turns into the **CREMEANS** driveway. Jim’s head snaps around. Something finally clicks.

**JIM** (calm, decisive)
We need a manager.

**JIM (V.O.)**
There it was. The answer, staring us right in the face.

**BILL** (knee-jerk skeptical)
A manager? Great. Just what bands need—some asshole to screw them over.

**JEREMY**
Yeah, managers are just one more mouth to feed.

**JIM** (shaking his head)
Not just any manager. *Cremeans*.

Bill and Jeremy both look toward the house, the gears turning.

**BILL** (dubious)
Cremeans? Jeff Cremeans? He’s a business major, not a music guy. Plus, that’s *two* Jeffs on the payroll. That’s a disaster.

**JEREMY** (deadpan)
We’ve survived two Jeremys. Odds are, we can survive two Jeffs.

**(smiles, then serious)**
The most important thing is trust. Cremeans is…he’s one of us. He’ll learn the ropes fast. And he’s hungry. The guy’s allergic to bosses.

**BILL** (tentative)
But…would he even take it? And, I mean, he’s kind of a—

(beat)
—“holy roller.” This business chews people up.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Cremeans didn’t act like other churchy types. He was idealistic, but practical. Fiercely loyal. All-in or not at all.

**JIM** (confidence returning)
Trust me. He’ll get it. He wants to build something. And he’ll look out for us.

The three stand together in the dusk, the air heavy with uncertainty and the first faint glimmer of hope.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Three friends in a driveway, suburban lights flickering on around them. Something’s shifting. Next move: theirs.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE – DRIVEWAY – LATER**

The band circles around **CREMEANS**, giving him the look-over that only old friends (and one doubting Saint Stephen) can muster.

**(SOUND):** The last latches snap on instrument cases, birds chirp in brittle winter air, a Mountain Dew cap clicks as it’s spun restlessly.)

**KATHY** (with a sly grin, nodding toward Gilley)
I think you’ve shown as much interest in our music as Gilley’s shown in—

(pause, deadpan)
—anything but his own dick.

**(VISUAL):**
Kathy’s smile, all teeth and trouble. Gilley, bristling but not about to take the bait. Cremeans, unbothered, calmly sipping his pop.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I tried to poke the bear. Didn’t even scratch his armor.

**CREMEANS** (shrugging, a gentle, unbothered smile)
Let’s not sell me short just yet.

**JEFF** (offering a palm for their ancient greeting, monotone)
Jeff.

**CREMEANS** (slaps his hand, equal monotone)
Jeff.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
That’s brotherhood. No explanation necessary.

A brief, solemn silence. It’s their “secret handshake” and the others recognize the bit.

**CREMEANS** addresses the group now, setting the Dew bottle on the hood of a car like a trophy.

**CREMEANS** (matter-of-fact)
Actually, I was invited.

**GILLEY** (squinting, thrown off)
Invited? Who invited you? My dad didn’t say anything.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
What’s the angle here?

**CREMEANS** just grins—wider this time, but reveals nothing.

**(VISUAL):**
The group stands in a loose semicircle, their body language shifting—less about testing, more about curiosity. For the first time, Cremeans seems right at home. There’s an almost imperceptible flicker of relief in Kathy’s eyes; Bill, already deciding if he likes this guy.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
The camera holds on **CREMEANS**, Mountain Dew in hand, mysterious as ever. Something new is on the table, and they can all feel it.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE – DRIVEWAY – CONTINUOUS**

The band shifts, restless. The easy rhythm of old friends is suddenly offbeat with **CREMEANS** here—watching, listening, quietly confident.

**(SOUND):** Car doors thud shut. Someone coughs. A dog barks two lawns away. The faint fizz of a Mountain Dew being opened, then sipped.)

**CREMEANS** stands steady, letting the silence fill in around his question.

**CREMEANS** (level, but not unkind)
So, half the band skipped the meeting last night. Just wanted to know why.

**(VISUAL):**
The camera glides across the group:

- **GILLEY** fidgets with his keys, squinting at the horizon.
- **KATHY**'s jaw clenches.
- **JEFF** straightens his glasses, blinks twice.
- **JEREMY** just waits, unreadable.

**GILLEY** (trying for nonchalance, but the lie tastes bad)
Long week. Practice, work…just tired out, man.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
Yeah, tired. That’s always safe. Nobody can argue with tired.

**KATHY** (forced brightness, failing to meet Cremeans’s eyes)
I had, uh…plans. Nothing important.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
“Plans.” As if “something to do” involved writhing naked with **GILLEY** in his stinky bedroom. I was so full of shit.

**JEFF** (soft, tripping over the words)
Paper due for poli sci. Had to…prioritize. Sorry.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
He doesn’t buy it. Nobody ever does. Why do I bother?

**JEREMY** (matter-of-fact, maybe even proud)
Bill and Jim and I were talking business. Bar math, not band practice.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
It was the truth. And suddenly, the only truth in the room.

**(VISUAL):**
**CREMEANS** listens, expression open, but his eyes never stop moving. Every micro-lie and awkward shuffle registers.

He lets a beat hang in the air, then finally speaks.

**CREMEANS** (slight smile, perfectly controlled)
Well. I get it. Life’s busy.

(pause, glances at Kathy, then Gilley)
But if we’re going to pull this off…We need everybody in the same room, same page. Band or business—it’s all the same when money’s involved.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
You can’t lead people you can’t read. And these people? I grew up reading them.

**(VISUAL):**
For a split second, nobody says a word. Even the birds seem to hush. In that Moment, the band knows: this guy isn’t here to power trip or be a babysitter. He’s here to turn this ship, and he’ll do it without breaking a sweat.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
**CREMEANS** takes another sip of Mountain Dew. The others look at him—some sizing him up, some almost grateful someone’s calling out the bullshit. It’s the first time in a long time the whole group feels…*seen*.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE – DRIVEWAY – CONTINUOUS**

The summer sun is harsh and clear, throwing sharp shadows. **CREMEANS** stands in front of the band, the Mountain Dew bottle perched like a trophy on **GILLEY**’s hood. No one speaks. For a Moment, you can almost hear the world spinning a little faster.

**CREMEANS** (steady, but warming as he goes)
Jim, Jeremy, Bill—

(nods at each)
—pitched me on being your manager. Not a joke. Not a babysitter. A *manager*. For real.

He fixes his gaze on the last three—**GILLEY**, **KATHY**, **JEFF**—waiting to see if they’ll flinch.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
If you want me, I’m in. Majority rules. But let’s be clear—this isn’t about hanging out and eating pizza. This is about *not* getting screwed by every bar owner from here to Dayton.

A tense beat as everyone processes this.

**JEFF** (quietly, not hostile)
You’re still in college.

**CREMEANS** (smiling, sure of himself)
So’s half the band. You work, you study, you play gigs—this is no different. I’ll make the time.

He takes a breath—then, his voice changes. More preacher than neighbor.
His vision, fully unleashed:

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
I stayed up last night reading everything I could find on band management. Taxes, contracts, booking, publishing, copyright law.

(shrugs)
Not glamorous, but if you want to *make it*—even regionally—you gotta be smarter than the guy on the other side of the table.

He holds up a finger.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Here’s what I see:

- We incorporate. Real business.
- We keep books, split profits, pay taxes, write off everything from drumsticks to gas.
- We claim every mile and every burger as a business expense.
- We copyright your songs.
- We put *our* contracts in front of *them*.

**(VISUAL):** The camera tight on his face, you can see the nerves under the bravado—but more than that, a rare kind of clarity. He’s already thinking three moves ahead.

**KATHY** (dry, arms crossed)
This is supposed to be about music, not receipts.

**CREMEANS** (grinning, sharp)
Exactly. The less time you spend being broke, the more time you spend writing, rehearsing, playing shows. If you want to make music *sustainably*, you need someone running interference with all the adult crap.

(looks at each of them)
You want to be a band, or just another group of kids with day jobs?

For a moment, even **GILLEY** is silent.   **KATHY** looks down, considering.
**JEFF** chews his lip, mentally doing the math.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
He sounded like he was building a spaceship. Half of it made no sense to me. But God, it was electric. For a second, I believed.

**CREMEANS** (softer, with a trace of humility)
Look, you can say no. But if you want to *build* something…I want in. Let’s do it right.

He leans back, hands out—open. No hard sell. Just conviction.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
The band stands at a crossroads—literally and figuratively. Cremeans’s Mountain Dew sweats on the hood. The wind gusts, flipping a page of setlists taped to a guitar case. The moment hangs, charged with possibility.  Change is coming. They can feel it.

---

## **EXT. GILLEY’S RESIDENCE – DRIVEWAY – CONTINUOUS**

A slight, uncertain breeze kicks through the circle of friends. For once, everyone is still. Even the dog barking in the distance seems to wait for the next line.

**JEFF** (earnest, slightly breathless)
So, let’s be real: a band is a democracy, right?

(pauses, squints)
But not, like, a modern one. Think…post-Revolution, pre-Constitution.

(grins at his own cleverness)
We’re operating under the Articles of Confederation here. Everything’s gotta be unanimous.

**(VISUAL):** The camera flashes to a faux-historical, black-and-white tableau of the Founders signing parchment, powdered wigs and all, then back to the sun-bleached driveway.

**JIM** (with real delight)
The Articles! Oh hell yeah, I get this one.

**KATHY** (smiling, can’t help herself)
So…you’re saying we need consensus?

**JEFF** (waving a dismissive hand)
No, no, not consensus. Unanimity. It’s different. Under the Articles, nothing happened unless *everyone* agreed. That’s why the whole thing kinda sucked.

**BILL** (flat, practical)
That’s exactly why it failed, man. It was a clusterfuck.

**JEFF** (jabbing a finger, almost giddy)
Exactly! But also…not the point.

**JIM** (cheering him on)
Partially correct is still pretty correct, in this garage.

**GILLEY** (with a lazy, wolfish grin)
Partially correct…partially erect. Now *that* is band consensus.

Everyone groans, except **KATHY**, who nearly laughs, the first honest sound from her in days.

**JEFF** (undeterred, ramping up)
And hey, let’s not forget! Ohio achieved statehood under the Articles. If it was good enough for the Buckeye State, maybe it’s good enough for us.

**JEREMY** (head in his hands, mock misery)
Jesus, Jeff, enough about Ohio.  We've got our own constitution!

(to Kathy)
You in or out?

A long pause. **KATHY** stands with her arms folded, jaw set. Something changes in her eyes—annoyance melting into an almost conspiratorial amusement.

**KATHY** (slow, measured)
I have a vision for this band. It’s big, loud, and probably more fun than you can survive, Cremeans.

**CREMEANS** (impeccably calm, but a tiny smile cracks)
I figured as much.

(leans in, lowering his voice)
Let’s get the paperwork done. I’ll stay out of your hair until tax time. Then, you can drag me out for whatever you need. We’ll revisit the rest in three months.

The band lets the silence stretch—a strange, warm consensus settling in.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
God, he *is* reading my mind. That’s terrifying.
(and just a little thrilling)

**(FINAL SHOT):**
The sun throws long shadows—everyone together but uncertain, like explorers about to shove off from shore. Something new is happening. They all feel it.

---

# **CHAPTER TEN: THE RISE**

---

**SOUND:**
The track kicks off—early R.E.M. energy, all jangling guitars and insistent drums, underscored by the *tick-tick* of a kitchen clock that sounds suspiciously like a countdown. In the background, the distant *blat-blat* of a muted TV newscast, a dog barking somewhere outside, the fridge kicking on, the world still indifferent.

**INT. CREMEANS’ KITCHEN — NIGHT**

The kitchen is pure Midwest: laminate countertops, bad linoleum, a box fan humming in the window.

**CREMEANS** is hunched over the battered table like a codebreaker in a war movie, face lit jaundiced by a flickering overhead bulb. His Mountain Dew sweats in a faded “Jesus is My Co-Pilot” koozie.

**CAMERA: EXTREME CLOSE-UP:**
A yellow legal pad, curling at the edges. Every line is filled—city names in all caps, dollar amounts circled, crossed out, recircled.
- *“DAYTON $200”*
- *“CINCINNATI $600??”*
- *“LOUISVILLE…TOLL ROADS?”*
- “Backline rental—find out wtf that actually means.”
- “Shoe rental? (Not a typo?)”

Receipts pile up: gas, White Castle, a blurred Speedway slip. A $2 tip for “PAUL - pizza,” scrawled in Sharpie on a napkin.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
It started simple. Cities. Drive times. Money in, money out. A yellow pad, a dream, and a really sketchy map of Kentucky.

**PULL BACK:**
The table is a disaster—legal pads stacked like bricks, envelopes stuffed with cash and change, a “borrowed” AAA TripTik from 1989, flyers for punk nights in Covington. The phone blinks: seven voicemails, one of which is probably his mother.

Cremeans’ glasses are off, rubbed clean, then smeared again as he scrawls notes, bites the cap, does the math a third time. He’s running on gas station coffee now, the Mt Dew abandoned in favor of something that burns.

**CUTS—A FRENZIED RHYTHM:**
- Cremeans tracing a shaky triangle: Dayton, Cincinnati, Indy.
- Underlining *“$200 guarantee + 10% of bar?”*
- A new pad, margins black with math:
- *“Mileage 112”*
- *“Gas $1.19/gal”*
- *“Tolls??”*

A sudden inspiration—he flips to a new page:
*“Infrastructure.”*
— Under that:
- *“Van insurance?”*
- *“What IS a rider?”*
- *“Bill has a cousin in Louisville? CALL.”*

The camera pushes in, the energy dizzying but meticulous, an obsession bordering on mania.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
A yellow pad only gets you so far. Eventually, you need…infrastructure. (He underlines it. Twice.) Otherwise, you’re just playing for beer money and pizza crusts.

He nods to himself—nobody else is up, the house is silent except for the TV burbling about the end of Desert Storm and the low, hopeful hum of someone building a new world out of receipts, phone numbers, and a bad map.

**JUMP CUTS:**
Cremeans at the same table, 2am, then 4am—each angle a little more ragged, the handwriting a little less legible. The pad fills up; he turns the page, dog-ears the corner. The city triangle now includes Columbus, Cleveland, Lexington. The plan is getting bigger, scarier, real.

---

## **THE KNITTING DESK**

**INT. CREMEANS’ LIVING ROOM – LATE NIGHT – MAY 1991**

**SOUND:**
A cheap box fan churns stale air by the window; frogs in the ditch outside croak in rhythm with the *thud* of a washing machine out of balance. The house feels both asleep and anxious, like the night is stretching just for him.

**CREMEANS** is kneeling at his mother’s old knitting desk—a fragile thing of spindly legs and floral inlay, now buried under a plotter calendar that looks like it’s plotting a military campaign. The wood creaks with each scribble, as if protesting its fate.

**CAMERA: GOD’S-EYE OVERHEAD:**
The calendar is chaos—each day scribbled over in red and blue, black marker circling certain dates like a siege.
- *“Bogart’s – 3800”*
- *“Canal St. – 2000 (DOOR CUT!)”*
-  *“WRIGHT STATE FESTIVAL – THIS ONE MATTERS”* circled twice, arrows drawn, asterisks everywhere.

A fat, battered highlighter rolls off the edge and is caught midair, no hesitation.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
My mother used to knit baby booties here. Christmas mittens. Now it’s where I plan small-scale financial domination. And maybe—just maybe—pay for her new dishwasher.

**RHYTHM: TARANTINO-FAST CUTS:**
– **CREMEANS** slaps a sticky note—*“Lexington? Ask about power drops”*—onto a Friday.
– Dials a battered beige push-button phone, notebook tucked under chin.

 **CREMEANS (muttering):**
“No, we can’t play a freaking brunch. Nobody wants to hear us cover Hüsker Dü at ten a.m.”

– Sips a room-temp Diet Rite with the reverence of a detective savoring bourbon in a noir.
– Jots numbers: *“30% door? If we bring our own mics? Christ, who do they think they’re dealing with?”*
– Quick cut: Flicks a spent pushpin at a map. It sticks dead-center in Louisville.

**WIDE SHOT:**
The desk is a riot—legal pads, cables, a war zone of highlighters and club flyers. In the midst, a half-finished scarf spills over the edge, a white flag or maybe just a reminder of gentler ambitions.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
The desk didn’t like it. Neither did she. But empire doesn’t care about heirlooms.

He pauses—finger hovering over the calendar—reminded, for a Moment, that every general’s war room started as somebody’s kitchen, somebody’s dream.

**VISUAL:**
He picks up the scarf, absentmindedly winding it around his hand, and—almost embarrassed—tucks it out of sight before attacking the next date. The past can wait. For now, it’s about drive times, guarantees, and making sure nobody, not one club in Ohio, forgets the name *Commuted*.

---

## **THE GIGS**

**MONTAGE – VARIOUS VENUES – LATE MAY 1991**

**SOUND:**
A battered, overdriven guitar riff kicks in—something scuzzy and hungry, with just enough wrong notes to sound alive. The crowd’s roar surges and drops, half threat, half celebration. Glass bottles *clink*, monitors *hum*, someone shouts for “*Free Bird*” and gets booed down.

**VERHOEVEN-STYLE RAPID CUTS:**

— **INT. VFW HALL – TROTWOOD – NIGHT**
**KATHY** launches into a solo, sweat flicking off her jaw, boots planted wide, her face a snarl of concentration and freedom. The crowd bounces, lost in the beat.

— **EXT. BOGART’S – CINCINNATI**
The marquee flickers, black plastic letters almost falling off: *COMMUTED + GUESTS*. The line outside snakes around the block, kids stamping cold feet, passing smuggled beers hand-to-hand.

— **INT. CAMPUS SHOW – WRIGHT STATE**
A low stage under flickering fluorescents. **GILLEY** lunges toward the mic, shirt half-unbuttoned, his howl swallowed by the amps. A couple of frat boys pump fists in the air; a girl flashes the band. **KATHY** barely registers it—she’s locked in, her world a single chord.

— **INT. CANAL STREET TAVERN – LATE**
The air is thick with smoke and cheap cologne. **JIM’s** snare snaps so loud it turns heads at the bar. Some kid in a Sonic Youth T-shirt loses his balance, pukes into his Converse, then wipes his mouth and keeps dancing.

**CAMERA: WILD CLOSE-UPS**
— **KATHY**’s eyes, wild and alive.
— **GILLEY**’s mouth, split in a scream and a grin.
— **CREMEANS** side-stage, notebook in one hand, Mountain Dew in the other, mouthing lyrics like a coach watching his team win.
— A dropped beer glass fizzing into a pile of cables.
— A bouncer rolling his eyes as he drags two idiots apart.

**SLOW MOTION:**
**KATHY** leaps off a monitor, hair flying, boots over the pit, arms flung wide—hovering, a freeze-frame of what it means to be *here, now, alive*.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
It wasn’t tight. It wasn’t clean. But Jesus, it *moved*. You could feel it in your chest, in your teeth. In the pit. In the parking lot at two A.M.

**FINAL IMAGE:**
A mess of hands, faces, sweat, lights—music blurring into noise, noise blurring into pure joy. The band is just shapes, shadows, echoes. The Moment is everything.

---

## **THE SCHEDULE**

**MONTAGE – MAY INTO JUNE 1991**

**SOUND:**
A wall clock ticks—a clean, steady pulse. The tick speeds up, doubling, tripling, morphing into a neurotic snare rush under a fuzzed-out riff. The calendar *flips* and *flips* and *flips*.

**VISUAL STYLE – FULL VERHOEVEN FRENZY**

**RAPID CUTS:**

— *Calendar close-ups, in Cremeans’ tight, decisive handwriting:*

*May 10: Dayton VFW Hall – 8PM
May 12: The Clubhouse, Springfield – 10PM (door split)
May 14: Yellow Springs Pizza Basement – “PAY IN PIES” (red ink, underlined twice)
May 18: Bogart’s, Cincinnati – $3800, circled three times with a star
May 21: Wright State Spring Fest – “DO NOT BE LATE” in desperate block caps*

**CAMERA: OVERHEAD SWEEP**
The schedule multiplies—dates crash together, pen lines connect city to city like a madman’s crime board. Weekdays vanish. Sleep vanishes.

**FLASH CUTS BETWEEN DATES:**

— **KATHY** slumped across a snarl of cables, a cigarette gone cold between her lips, guitar still strapped on.
— **CREMEANS** on two phones, shouting, “Yes, we have our own mics now! No, the van’s not on fire—*today*!”
— **JIM** hunched over a battered snare, swapping bloody tape with surgical focus.
— **GILLEY** in a cramped green room, shirtless, chugging a warm Pabst, eyes wild, set list taped to his chest.
— *A whiteboard in the van: “MUST CALL MOM” in all caps, erased and re-written a dozen times.*

**SOUND BRIDGE:**
Calendar pages rip away in time with a ferocious drum fill—*thwack-thwack-thwack*—as the schedule blurs from one week into the next.

**SMASH ZOOM:**
*JUNE 22 – INDIANAPOLIS – CLUB RETINA – FIRST HEADLINE SHOW (star, exclamation point, “NO EXCUSES”)*

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
At some point I stopped asking if we could play. I just started booking us, showing up, and daring anyone to tell us to leave.

**FINAL IMAGE:**
A giant wall calendar in Cremeans’ cluttered room—ink bleeding through, post-its layered five deep, every day spoken for.

A sticky note at the top: **“IF YOU SLEEP, YOU MISS THE VAN.”**

**(SOUND: The clock *explodes* into wild, offbeat fills—time no longer means anything. Only the next gig.)**

---

## **THE VAN**

**EXT. CREMEANS’ DRIVEWAY – DAY – JUNE 1991**

**SOUND:**
A distant lawnmower whines, half-buried under static as the garage radio limps through CCR’s “*Up Around the Bend*.” A neighbor yells at a dog. This is Ohio suburbia at noon: nothing moves but the humidity.

**CREMEANS** stands next to the Ford Econoline—a battered hulk with more personality than resale value. One hand on the hood like he’s blessing it. The other raised in silent triumph.

The van is a patchwork: faded blue-gray, a primer panel, the shadow of “Larry’s Plumbing—Since 1977” half-scraped off. Rust laces the wheel wells like frost.

**CAMERA: LOW ANGLE HERO SHOT**
**CREMEANS** is all optimism and sweat, grinning like he’s just signed with Atlantic.  Behind him: cookie-cutter houses, chain-link fences, distant ballgame. In front: the future—boxy, lurching, with 180,000 miles and an appetite for oil.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Transportation. Not glamorous. Not sexy. But you don’t take the hill if you can’t get the whole platoon there—alive, mostly awake, and (usually) on time.

**CAMERA: SLOW 360 PAN — VAN DETAILS:**
— A cracked rearview, duct-taped twice, faith holding it together.
— One tire with more patches than tread.
— Vinyl seat ripped down the seam, foam like cheap cake.
— Bumper sticker: *“I’m not drunk, I’m just avoiding potholes.”*

**CUT TO – VAN INTERIOR:**
Cremeans swings open the back doors. It’s chaos, but the good kind—amps jammed in like Jenga blocks, cabs wedged under cymbal bags, a leaky cooler sloshing flat Mountain Dew, and the sacred box of always-tangled orange extension cords.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
You can’t control the crowds. You can’t control the sound guy. But you can make dang sure your gear arrives in one piece—even if your dignity doesn’t.

**WIDE SHOT:**
Cremeans stands arms akimbo, staring at his $1,600 miracle like a general surveying the battlefield.

**GILLEY (O.S., deadpan)**
It smells like feet and broken dreams in here.

**CREMEANS (grinning, never looking back)**
That’s the smell of progress.

**(SOUND: The van door SLAMS shut—echoing like a gauntlet thrown at fate.)**

---

## **THE WAREHOUSE**

**INT. DAYTON AIRPORT PERIMETER – SMALL INDUSTRIAL WAREHOUSE – DAY**

**SOUND:**
A pen scratching like a nervous insect. The echoing *ka-chunk* of a steel hangar door groaning open for the first time in years. A distant jet engine, the rumble felt more than heard. This is the edge of the world, or at least the edge of Vandalia.

**CREMEANS** signs the lease with the gravity of a man who knows this moment will live forever in band mythology. Sweat trickles down his temple. His signature is crisp, defiant. The property manager, a woman in a padded windbreaker and unforgiving shoes, passes the keys over like she’s transferring the family rifle. No smiles. Only the transaction, sacred and cold.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Storage. Rehearsal space. And—eventually—world domination headquarters.
*“Every empire starts with a warehouse, right?”*

**VISUAL STYLE – VERHOEVEN CAMERA MOVEMENT:**
The doors creak and shudder open. **CREMEANS** leads the way—shadow tall, steps loud on bare concrete. For a moment, he just stands in the middle, letting the echo answer back.

**CAMERA: SLOW PAN ACROSS THE SPACE:**
Dust motes tumble in a weak shaft of sunlight. It’s big, too big, but the bigness feels right. There’s a battered metal desk, graffiti from a long-dead skate crew, a bulb swinging on a cracked wire. The only window is smeared with grime and hope. There’s no bathroom (just a condemned outhouse), a beehive is already humming in the south wall, but the fuse box works. That’s enough.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
It didn’t matter that the bathroom was condemned. Or that there was a beehive in the wall.  We had *space*. Space to be wrong, to be loud, to be more.

**MONTAGE – THE FIRST MOVES:**

- **KATHY** drags in a battered mic stand, electrical tape and all, leaving a trail of amp cords like breadcrumbs.
- **JEFF** wheels in his Jim's kit, pausing to look up at the high ceiling, grinning like a kid who’s just been let loose in a cathedral.
- **JEREMY** hauls in a cooler and a folding chair, pops a Miller Lite, and takes the first slouching seat.
- **CREMEANS** cracks a fresh Sharpie and, with all the seriousness of a sacred ritual, sketches a crooked band logo on the wall:
    *“COMMUTED HQ – TRESPASSERS WILL BE SHOT, RE-BOOKED, AND PAID IN COINS”*

**WIDE SHOT – STATIC CAMERA:**
All of them scattered inside the giant, echoing shell—tiny, laughing, already plotting. Hope vibrates in the empty air.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
We weren’t just chasing gigs.  We were building a base.  A myth.  A place to be as loud as we dared—no apologies, no neighbors pounding on the walls.

For the first time, it felt real.  It felt like the start of something big.

---

## **THE BLOW JOB**

**INT. BACK ROOM – POST-GIG – NIGHT**

**SOUND:**
The thump of a distant subwoofer, dull and relentless. The sharp *chirp* of a car alarm somewhere in the alley, fading into glass crunching and a burst of laughter that already sounds like memory.

The room is painted in sick yellow from a single bulb, swinging slow. Water stains bloom on the ceiling. The floor sticks. The air is a mix of old beer and industrial bleach, with a note of something animal underneath.

**KATHY** kneels.

She’s not framed sexy, not degraded, not even truly seen—she’s a shape at the edge of the frame.  The guy above her is just torso, exposed cock and a generic shirt. Nothing for the audience to latch onto but Kathy’s *unreadable face*.

**CAMERA: EXTREME CLOSE-UP on KATHY’S FACE:**
Eyes glassy. Lips moving like she’s repeating a word she can’t quite remember.
It’s mechanical, but not habitual—she’s *opting out*, going somewhere deep inside, the way you might listen to silence after a fire alarm.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This wasn’t escape.  It was subtraction.  Subtract the noise. Subtract the self.  Make it quiet, if only for a minute.

**JUMP CUTS – VERHOEVEN DETAIL:**

- Her necklace, out of place, knocking softly against her collarbone.
- The man’s hand, not cruel, just careless, brushing her hair back like he’s adjusting his prop.
- Kathy’s hand in the carpet, fingers clenched, holding onto *something*—not him, not even the moment, just proof she’s there.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Everything else was turned up—stage, van, the world in her head.  But here?  Muted.  I’d take it.

**CAMERA: OVER-THE-SHOULDER**
A garish show flyer taped to the wall, all cartoon flames and neon, promising *COMMUTED LIVE!* The colors are ridiculous, absurd—Kathy, in contrast, is grayscale, barely holding contrast with the world behind her.

**She finishes.**  Rises. Doesn’t speak. Doesn’t look at him. Jacket zipped, sleeve wiped, motion efficient—like she’s erasing a blackboard.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Color was for other people.  I just wanted quiet.

**SOUND:**
The door shuts behind her. The bass from the main room swells up, swallowing what happened in the quiet.

---

## **THE TOAST**

**INT. WAREHOUSE – NIGHT – JUNE 1991**

(SOUND: The band’s own cassette demo roars out of battered monitors—full of clatter, mistakes, and fire. Laughter ricochets off the cinderblock walls. Amps buzz, someone’s shoe squeaks on concrete, bottles clink together like wind chimes.)

**QUICK VERHOEVEN-STYLE SHOTS:**

— **KATHY** tips back her head in laughter, eyeliner smudged, eyes bright and defiant, red Solo cup half-full and dangerously tilted.
— **JIM** whacks out a double-time roll on a greasy pizza box, making the slices jump.
— **BILL** sprawled backwards on the thrift-store couch, half his shirt untucked, shoes off, one sock inside-out, harmonizing badly along to the tape.
— **JEREMY** in the corner, holding a Miller Lite and an open roll of duct tape like both are sacred tools.
— **JEFF** perched on a road case, knees up, air-drumming with one hand, singing the wrong lyrics, grinning like a little kid at Christmas.
