— **CREMEANS** in cargo shorts, *KINKO’S ROCKS* tee stuck to his back, Mountain Dew held aloft like a sword of destiny.

**CREMEANS (shouting over the chaos, mock-formal):**
To loud amps, late nights, and never—*never*—asking permission.

**BAND (bellowing, howling, off-key):**
TO COMMUTED!

**ALL CLINK—**
Red Solo, Mountain Dew, half a tallboy, a socket wrench, someone else’s shoe. The sound is pure, unfiltered joy.

**JIM** jumps up on a chair, pumping his fists.  **BILL** shouts, “PLAY IT AGAIN!”  **KATHY** spins herself in a lazy circle, arms wide, soaking it in.  **JEREMY** tapes a band setlist to the wall, upside-down.  **JEFF** just sits there, soaking up the laughter like it’s heat.

**KATHY (V.O.):**
This wasn’t supposed to happen. Not to us. Not in this ugly little city, not in a warehouse by the airport. But here we were.

**CAMERA: SLOW ZOOM OUT—**
The warehouse glowing with string lights and punk hope, pizza crusts and tangled cords on the floor, every face lit up with sweat and hunger and belief.

**KATHY (V.O.):**
And for one night, one stupid, beautiful night—We belonged to the future.  We belonged to each other.

---

## **EIGHT MINUTES TO ORBIT**

---

**(SOUND):** The unmistakable opening synth chords of Peter Schilling’s “Major Tom (Coming Home)” echo like liftoff countdown alarms — pure, neon 80s. Every beat pulses with momentum.

**(VISUAL):** Cuts are staccato, stylized — more music video than cinema. The color palette runs from stark kitchen fluorescents to vaporwave blue-pinks. Jump zooms, overexposures, and swish-pans: this is kinetic, hungry, *alive.*

---

## **COUNTDOWN BEGINS**

**INT. CREMEANS’ KITCHEN – NIGHT – EARLY JUNE 1991**

(SOUND: The synths fill the cramped kitchen like rocket fuel hissing. Peter Schilling’s voice hovers, alien and urgent.)

The kitchen is *carnage by paperwork*:

- Flyers stabbed to the corkboard with steak knives.
- Photocopied contracts, all band names underlined in different day-glo markers.
- The yellow legal pad is now a *relic of war*, the handwriting increasingly frantic and slanted, stained by cheap gas station coffee.

**CAMERA:**

- A jumpy CLOSE-UP of a digital wall clock. The numbers flicker, skipping, *9:48:34…9:48:29…* Like time is stuttering before ignition.
- Fingers stabbing the keys on a calculator: *CRUNCH, CRUNCH, CRUNCH*.
- A date on the Ohio map: *“JUNE 22 — INDIANAPOLIS — CLUB RETINA — HEADLINE”* circled so hard it’s torn the paper.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Ground control to Major Tom.  Every band says “the sky’s the limit.”  I said, **let’s see how far the engine’ll take us**.

**INSERTS — MTV-CUT QUICK HITS:**

- A battered duffel bag full of flyers, each gig name growing in font size.
- CREMEANS’s face in blue kitchen light, glasses fogged, jaw locked.
- His hand jamming a highlighter across the words *“DOOR DEAL”* and *“90 MIN SET”*.

- A pack of Sharpies. In permanent ink: **“DO NOT DARE LOSE”**.

**CLOCK — THE MINUTES DROP FAST:**
*9:47:59…9:47:45…*

**CREMEANS stands, knocking over a mug — “World’s Okayest Boss” — coffee waterfalls off the table, soaking flyers and receipts. He doesn’t care. He’s already moving, already planning the next six steps._

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Noise? That was their department.  But blueprints? Blueprints were mine.

**SOUND — SCHILLING BREAKS INTO CHORUS:**
*“This is Major Tom to Ground Control…”*

**CREMEANS FLIPS OPEN THE FOLDER:**
Inside: the *Q3 TOUR – MASTER PLAN.*  Hand-drawn routes spider across the Midwest, circled club names, cryptic codes in the margins. *Nothing* is left to chance except the music.

**CUTAWAY — WIDE ANGLE, SLOW MOTION:**

- Cremeans’ silhouette in the kitchen window, floodlit by a streetlight, the whole world outside going dim.
- His eyes tracking up from his blueprints to a horizon only he can see.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
You can wish on a star, or you can build the rocket.

---

## **LIFT OFF (JEFF’S POV)**

**Jeff walks in—just looking for a snack, maybe a little quiet—and is hit by something else entirely.** The *kitchen* is no longer just a kitchen. It’s a command center. Paper everywhere, phone lines jammed, pens moving like launch codes are being written in real time.

- **Cremeans** is at the old knitting desk, transformed into a war room. The plotter calendar dominates, like a general’s map of the front.
- Dates are getting circled so hard the Sharpie almost rips through.
- On the wall, venues and numbers flash by in Jeff’s head like digital target readouts: **Indianapolis. Bogart’s. Columbus. Canal Street Tavern. Wright State.** Each one is labeled in Cremeans’ handwriting and, in Jeff’s mind, in all-caps like mission milestones: IGNITION. BLAST OFF. LIFTOFF. STAGE SEPARATION. ORBIT.

**Jeff’s inner monologue:**

- *“I don’t know what he was doing exactly. But I was pretty sure NASA had less paperwork.”*
- *“It was like watching someone plan a war they secretly hoped would go nuclear.”*

But the crucial thing? **Jeff** doesn’t fully get the math, or the business side, or all the talk of net/gross/tips. But he *sees the look in Cremeans’ eyes*. That wild conviction. That infectious certainty.

And **Jeff**, who usually needs facts and data to believe in anything, finds himself—*despite himself*—starting to believe in this crazy, rocket-powered vision.

**Emotionally:**

- Jeff feels a bit out of his element, watching this storm of logistics, but—
- He’s *inspired* (even if he’s a little horrified).
- Cremeans’ ambition is *contagious*.

**Final image:**
As the camera pushes in on Jeff’s face, he’s half-grinning, half-nervous—but most importantly, **he’s all in**.

*He doesn’t have to understand every calculation to know he wants to see where this rocket goes.*

---

## **ACCELERATION (GILLEY’S POV)**

**SOUND:** “Major Tom” crashes in—synths and snare colliding, the room vibrating with raw momentum.

**GILLEY** steps out—*and the world locks in around him.*

**GILLEY (V.O.):**
Some people spend years learning to fake it.  Me? I didn’t have to.  The second those lights hit—*I remembered.*

**GLAM-ROCK DREAMSTATE – RAPID CUTS:**

- **Smoke billows** at his feet, spotlighting GILLEY like a goddamn demigod.
- He’s got the mic stand by the neck, **spinning it preacher-style**, eyes wild, sweat shining.
- The crowd is faceless—just a storm of hands, noise, and flashing teeth.
    **But they all want him.**
- **KATHY** is a silhouette beside him, hair flying—locked in, but never competing.
- **GILLEY** howls into the mic, eyeliner smeared, shirt half-open, every muscle alive.

**GILLEY (V.O.):**
Every stage felt like déjà vu.  Not a climb—*a return*.  You can’t fake presence.  You *either burn or you don’t.*

**INSERT SHOTS – PURE JOY:**

- **Kids in the front row** losing their minds, singing every word.
- GILLEY shirtless, arms stretched out, *glowing* in the spotlight.
- **CREMEANS in the wings,** grinning, mouthing along—like he knew this would happen.

**CAMERA: CLOSE ON GILLEY’S FACE – END OF THE SET:**
He’s out of breath, grinning, *electric*—the kind of high you only get when you’re exactly where you’re meant to be.

**GILLEY (V.O.):**
This is it.  This is *me.*  And I never want to leave.

**This is the *victory lap***—and every night is proof: Gilley isn’t chasing the dream, he’s *already living it*.

---

## **BREAKING THE SOUND BARRIER (JEREMY’S POV)**

**MONTAGE – MULTIPLE VENUES & THE WAREHOUSE – MAY INTO JUNE 1991**

**SOUND:** Calendar pages whipping by, sharp as propellers. Synths pulse underneath—nervous, restless, alive.

**JEREMY** is everywhere—one day hauling a handtruck stacked with kegs, the next slinging a Les Paul into a battered road case. Grease under his nails, but calluses too.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
It started as a weekend hustle.  Then Thursdays.  Then every night they’d book us, I’d show up—work boots, stage boots, didn’t matter.

**VISUAL STYLE – MTV GLITCH JUMP CUTS:**

- **Calendar pages** fly at warp speed—dates strobing:

    - **Columbus: $5000 – HYPERBURN**
    - **Bogart’s: $3800 – PLASMA ENTRY**
    - **Dayton Spring Fest: $3700 – MAX CAPACITY**

- Overlaid: **gear thrown in vans, cables snaking across sticky floors, Jeremy’s arm flexing as he lifts a heavy cab onstage.**

- **Quick flashes**:
- Jeremy unloading cases, then minutes later, **ripping through a solo under the lights**.
- Chugging a Miller Lite, high-fiving the sound guy, sweat flying, *alive*.


**JEREMY (V.O.):**
Some guys got to write the songs.  I got to make them loud.

**ZOOM IN – WHITEBOARD IN THE WAREHOUSE:**

- **JUNE 22 – INDIANAPOLIS – “HEADLINING”** is circled twice, big, in blue marker.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
I wasn’t just pushing beer anymore.  Maybe there was more to the grind than the warehouse.

**FINAL SHOT:**
Jeremy tuning up backstage, hands quick, grin wide. The stage lights flare up—**and suddenly, he’s not the delivery guy.**  He’s the *hero with the guitar,* finally breaking through.

**SOUND: Quick whip-pan to the next date—calendar still burning.**

---

## **REACHING ESCAPE VELOCITY (JIM’S POV)**

**EXT. PARKING LOT OUTSIDE THE WAREHOUSE – LATE AFTERNOON**

**SOUND:** A battered tape deck clicks. “Major Tom” is mid-chorus, warbling through blown speakers. The wind flips a Burger King bag across hot asphalt. The van gleams — somehow both menacing and absurd.

**JIM** stands, arms crossed, soaking it all in.

The Econoline, no longer “the van.” Now **THE SHIP**:

- Matte-black, sharpie-scratched stencils, a homemade rocketship tearing across a full moon.
- *COMMUTED* slashed across the side in jagged white, like it means business and/or vandalism.

**JIM (V.O.)**
Is this what astronauts feel like, staring at the Saturn V?  Nah. This is better.
This one’s *mine.*

**CAMERA: FULL 360 CIRCLE PAN – VAN AT THE CENTER**
Everything around the van blurs:  Fast food wrappers, chain-link fence, the echo of a ride cymbal dropped on pavement.

**CREMEANS (O.S., dead serious in his best NASA voice)**
“Jim Brown, you are go for launch.”

**INSIDE:**

- Amps stacked like Tetris.
- Cables coiled, color-coded.
- A sacred **drummer’s corner**:

    - ALL the weird toms.
    - The octobans.
    - The half-melted ride with duct tape scars.
    - Space for the *monster kit*.

**JIM (V.O.):**
You ever been the guy who always has to squeeze his gear in last?  Not anymore.

He sits in the drummer’s corner. Breathes.  Sketches out a wild new kit design on a receipt. It’s ridiculous. It’s perfect.

**JIM (V.O.):**
There was room for all of it.  Room for *me*.  Room for the noise we were about to make.

He grins, wicked and proud.  **For once, the world fit him. Not the other way around.**

---

## **ESTABLISHING ORBIT (BILL’S POV)**

**INT. DAYTON AIRPORT WAREHOUSE – LATE AFTERNOON**

**SOUND:** The key in the lock, *clack*. The steel roll-up door groans open, echoing like the intro to a stadium show. “Major Tom” peaks in the background, synths swirling around the concrete void.

**BILL** stands in the doorway, blinking into the sunlight streaming through high dusty windows.

He steps inside. The *space* hits him first—cold, oil-stained, humming with potential. The kind of place where every noise ricochets forever.

**BILL (V.O.):**
You could park three garages in here.  You could land a plane.  You could build a whole damn world.

**CAMERA: SLOW PAN, VERHOEVEN STYLE**

- The drum kit in the corner, catching a sunbeam.
- **KATHY**’s amp stack, wires spilling out like nerves.
- **GILLEY**’s stand, proudly propped up by two bricks and a bad attitude.
- The wall of flyers—half peeling, all loud.

There’s a table with merch (all larges, no mediums, nobody’s fault), a coffee maker with a suicide note taped to it, and a broken stool **CREMEANS** calls “the boardroom.”

**CREMEANS (clapping hands, grinning):**
Welcome to mission control.

**BILL (V.O.):**
The reverb here is gonna make every chord sound like Zeppelin at Knebworth.  I could just *whisper* and the room would throw it back, twice as big.

He walks across the concrete, claps once, listens to the echo spiral off.

**BILL (V.O.):**
This wasn’t a practice spot.  It was an amplifier.  For music. For mistakes. For every dumb, brilliant idea we could throw at the walls.

He sets his gear down, already eyeing the rafters for the best overhead mic spot.

**BILL (V.O.):**
God help the neighbors.  This place is gonna *scream*.

---

## **ASTRONAUT’S HOLIDAY (KATHY’S POV)**

**INT. BACKROOM OF BAR – NIGHT – POST-GIG**

**SOUND:** Reverb bleeding through cinderblock. A snare hit, slow and drowned. Laughter somewhere down the hallway—blurred and untranslatable.

The light is anemic, tinged with yellow, stripping the color from everything. Dust in the air makes halos around the bulb. The room feels far away from the music, far away from anything real.

**CAMERA: VERHOEVEN-STYLE SURREALISM**
— **KATHY** in profile, face slightly out of focus.
— Her eyes open, fixed on nothing.
— The man is a cipher: a boot, a wristwatch, the shine of a belt buckle. Forgettable. Absolutely forgettable.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Floating.  Not high, not lost—just *unhooked.*  No up, no down, no anchor.

Her hands move automatically. There’s nothing erotic, nothing given, nothing taken. Only the act. Her breath is steady. Detached.

**CAMERA PULLS BACK:**
Gig posters ripple behind her, shadows warping in the wake of a lazy ceiling fan.
*“COMMUTED – ONE NIGHT ONLY”* is just legible, its corners peeling.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
He said thank you.  Like I’d done him a favor.  Like I was doing *anything* at all.

She tugs her shirt straight. Wipes her mouth with the back of her hand.  Doesn’t look at him. Won’t. Doesn’t have to.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
People think space is cold.  It’s not.  It’s *nothing.*  And nothing’s worse.

She zips her jacket—a little too fast, too tight—like she’s strapping herself in.  A warning sign. A dare: Don’t ask.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I’m fine.

Seriously.

You believe me, right?

**CAMERA: STATIC, LINGERING**
She leaves without a word.  The door swings shut. Posters flutter. The music outside is just a rumor.

**The room is silent. And so is she.**

---

## **MISSION ACCOMPLISHED**

**SOUND:** “Major Tom” cresting into its last chorus — *“Coming home…”* — while the warehouse shakes with celebration.

Confetti falls like busted insulation from the ceiling — somebody definitely poked it with a broom handle. Cheap string lights flicker and strobe, powered by a duct-taped surge strip jammed into a cracked outlet. The whole place looks like a prom for space nerds got crash-landed in a loading dock.

**CAMERA: CLOSE-UP – CREMEANS’ HAND**
He lifts a plastic bottle of Mountain Dew. There’s a little red-and-silver rocket sticker wrapped around the label.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Thus according to prophecy.  Behold: the Dew of Destiny.

**THE TOAST – ALL VOICES:**
*“TO COMMUTED!”*

**CAMERA: RAPID CUTS – FACES IN CELEBRATION**

— **KATHY**, head back, laughing, pizza crust in hand.
— **GILLEY**, fake-soloing on a broom, hair wild, tongue out.
— **JIM**, spinning a drumstick, eyes crossed like a circus act.
— **BILL**, saluting the Dew bottle, deadly serious.

**CREMEANS** grins like he’s launching the first shuttle to Mars.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
This was supposed to be dumb.  Just a side hustle.  A reason to yell and maybe scam free nachos.

**POP!**
Somebody cracks cheap champagne.
**POP!**
Simultaneously, **CREMEANS** snaps his Dew like a captain christening the fleet.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
But it was *working*.  Not clean. Not safe.  But real. Loud. Ours.

**CAMERA: SLOW ZOOM OUT – WAREHOUSE WIDE**
Everybody’s toasting, mugging, yelling.  The party lights flare like afterburners.  Confetti settles on amps, wires, drums, cheap beer cans.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
We weren’t coming home.  We were just learning how to leave.

**FINAL SHOT:**
The camera pulls back, satellite-style — the warehouse a lit-up capsule in blackness, glowing with noise, hope, chaos.

The last line of *“Coming home…”* echoes out, and the screen fades to black.

---

# **CHAPTER ELEVEN: GUN FOR HIRE**
## **INT. DOWNTOWN SPRINGFIELD – BANQUET HALL – AUG 1991 – NIGHT**

---

(SOUND: *Bruce Springsteen’s “Dancing in the Dark”* blasts from rented speakers. Laughter bubbles like cheap champagne. Silverware clinks. Heels scrape across parquet. The full, gaudy joy of a Midwest wedding, beneath a massive rented chandelier.)

The room is pure spectacle — white chair covers, twinkle lights, melting ice swans, a DJ in a tuxedo T-shirt. The dance floor’s a mosaic of high heels and polyester, every Midwestern cousin grinding to Springsteen’s heartbreak anthem.

**VISUAL:** The camera floats — catching glitter, sprayed hair, fake smiles, distant uncles with disposable cameras — until it lands on **KATHY, JIM, and BILL**. They’re spinning each other around, faces glossy with sweat and drunken joy. They look like they’ve stepped out of a John Hughes movie: lit up, vivid, slightly unreal.

**V.O. (THE DANCERS):**
They weren’t dancing for fun.  They were dancing to forget.  To deflect.  To drown out the other half of the band — sitting at the bar, dressed for a funeral.

---

**AT THE BAR – JEFF & GILLEY**

Both slouched in rental tuxes, shirt collars limp, hands around sweating whiskey glasses. They don’t look at the dance floor. They don’t look at each other.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
We were ghosts in a dream we didn’t believe in.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
A thousand-dollar party for a five-dollar mistake.

A glass slams down — JEFF’s — sharp, wrong, ignored by the room. Except **JEREMY** notices.

**JEREMY** (drunk, glowing, bride nowhere in sight):
Hey, guys! You having a good time?

**GILLEY** (deadpan):
Highlight of my fucking year.

**JEFF** (ugly grin):
Just peachy.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
They weren’t happy.  They weren’t subtle.  I was too dumb, or too in love, to care which.

**JEREMY** (oblivious):
Ceremony went great, right? The caterer even got the chicken right. No fights! That’s gotta be a record.

**GILLEY:**
No fights *yet.*

**JEFF** (too casual):
We need to talk.

Suddenly the world tilts — still in the banquet hall, but it feels like a showdown. Three men, one bar, no happy ending.

**JEFF:**
I checked my bank account.

**CLOSE-UP:** His eyes — cold, focused.

**JEFF (CONT’D):**
I also checked plane tickets. Acapulco. Mexico. Round trip. For three.

**GILLEY** nods, grim. Like they’ve rehearsed this.

**JEFF (V.O.):**
We needed an out. Not just from the band. From *everything.*

**JEREMY** (thrown, desperate):
You’re not serious.

**GILLEY:**
Dead serious. We leave tonight.

**FLASH CUT — VERHOEVEN-STYLE FANTASY:**
Sun-soaked Acapulco. Cheap motel. Empty stage on the sand. The dream flickering, melting.

**JEFF:**
Two-diamond hotel. With a pool.  Mom’s AAA card got us twelve percent off.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
It wasn’t even the words.  It was the *look* in their eyes.  Like they already left, and were just waiting for me to realize it.

**JEREMY:**
I just got married.

**GILLEY:**
Exactly.

**JEFF:**
You don’t belong here either, man. You know it.

**JEREMY** (rising, pissed):
Are you guys insane?! This isn’t a game! I’m starting a *life* here!

**GILLEY:**
No. You’re quitting the band. You’re quitting *us.*

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
They didn’t want to rescue me.  They wanted to drag me back down with them.

**(SOUND:)** *“Dancing in the Dark”* — *You can’t start a fire, You can’t start a fire without a spark…*)

**JEFF** (cold):
We’re leaving. You’re either in or you’re not.

**FINAL SHOT – THE THREE AT THE BAR**
Triangle of tension. Static and silent, while the rest of the party whirls. The camera *zooms out* — the laughter now sounds like mockery.

**JEFF (V.O.):**
We weren’t a band anymore.  We were in the wreckage.

---

## **INT. DOWNTOWN SPRINGFIELD – BANQUET HALL – NIGHT**

**(SOUND)**: The music cuts. No needle hiss — just dead, sucked-out silence. A glass clinks somewhere. Someone coughs. Even the air feels paused.)

The mood fractures. Guests sense something off, glancing toward the bar. The tension around **JEFF**, **GILLEY**, and **JEREMY** is bulletproof.

**TIM WRIGHT enters.**

US Navy Service Whites. Medals, ribbons, every crease perfect. The only man in the room who seems *deliberate.* The camera tracks his legs — white fabric glowing like a religious icon — but his walk is all predatory muscle.

**TIM** (Voice sharp, carrying)
What’s the hold-up?

The three at the bar don’t turn fast. They rotate as one. **JEFF**’s jaw ticks. **GILLEY**’s face is set.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Tim never left his ship. He brought it with him.

**JEFF** (Dead)
Private function, Tim.

**GILLEY** (Without looking)
Yeah. Move along.

**TIM** (Grinning, ignoring)
Met your bride, **JEREMY**.

He lets it hang.

**TIM (CONT’D)**
Cunt.

The room holds its breath. A grenade in a velvet box. No music, nowhere for the word to go but *in*.

**VERHOEVEN CLOSE-UP:**
**JEREMY** blinks, stunned.  **JEFF** and **GILLEY**…smile.

Not friendly. Not forgiving.
*Permission.*

**JEFF** (Soft, lethal)
Yeah, she is.

**GILLEY** (Dry, with teeth)
Real cunt.

**TIM (V.O.)**
They’re joking, I think. But it felt like watching a bridge burn and not feeling the heat.

**TIM** (Confused, cracks showing)
What the hell are you talking about?

**JEFF** (Low, flat)
Not your business.

**GILLEY** (Stepping closer)
So beat it, shit-for-brains.

**TIM**’s fists clench. His medals twitch.

**TIM**
What the *fuck* did you just say?

**JEFF**
I said: beat it.  Naval etiquette, right?

**GILLEY**
Let it go, Tim.

A beat. No one blinks.

**TIM** (Half-whisper, lost)
You think you’re tough now?

**GILLEY** (Even lower)
I don’t need a uniform to be respected.

That lands. You can see it break something in Tim.

**JEREMY** (Quiet, desperate; hand on Tim’s arm)
Tim, please. Stop. It’s my wedding.

**CAMERA: CLOSE-UP — Tim’s face.**
The anger. The calculation. The loss.

**TIM** (Fading, muttered)
Fine. Just remember…I’m still watching.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
He didn’t mean it as a threat. But it was.  Because now he wasn’t our brother. Just a man in white.  And we were all in black.

**WIDE SHOT – RECEPTION**
The music and laughter return, oblivious. “Shout” blares. Life resumes. But at the bar?  Three men, staring at the ghost Tim left behind. Not moving. Not forgiving.  Already rewriting the story.

---

## **INT. PLANNED PARENTHOOD CLINIC – DAY**

**(SOUND)**: The soft drone of fluorescent lights. A muted printer. Voices muffled behind closed doors.)

**NURSE JOHNSON** (mid-50s, brisk-warm) sits across from **KATHY**, who isn’t broken, but isn’t whole either. Hoodie zipped. Shoulders tight. Eyes glassy but sharp. She’s holding it together—barely, but enough.

**NURSE JOHNSON** (gentle, professional)
Let’s talk birth control options. You mentioned the IUD?

**KATHY** (flat, but clear)
Yeah. Something long-term. No drama. No pills to forget.

**NURSE JOHNSON** (nods, already making notes)
Perfect. We’ll schedule you for insertion. Next Thursday morning work?

**KATHY**
That works.

**VISUAL**: CLOSE-UP—Nurse Johnson’s hand, turning appointment book pages, steady as a surgeon. Then to **KATHY**—her chin lifted, posture straightening.

**NURSE JOHNSON**
Take ibuprofen an hour before. Try not to be on your period. I’ll walk you through the rest.

(Pause, businesslike)
We’ll do an STI screen and some history, too.

**KATHY** (even, no shame)
Twelve.

**NURSE JOHNSON** (a half-blink—no judgment, just processing)
Twelve, in the last twelve months?

**KATHY**
Yes.

**A flicker—Nurse Johnson’s only tell—but she nods, unflinching.**

**NURSE JOHNSON**
Thanks for being honest. That helps us take care of you right. That’s all that matters.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
She didn’t ask why. She didn’t get small. She didn’t offer a sermon or a sigh.
She just took me as-is, like I was a car up on blocks, not a write-off.  In progress.

**NURSE JOHNSON** (sliding over a folder)
Here’s the info—procedure, aftercare. Call if you need anything, or if you change your mind.

**KATHY** takes it. Hand steady. She almost says thank you, but just nods. That’s enough.

**VERHOEVEN-STYLE:** **KATHY** pushes out through the glass doors—midday sun floods over her, harsh, bright, clean. She squints, but keeps going, pamphlets clenched like a hall pass.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Not a fix. Not an apology. Just a line in the sand. Not this. Not again. Not like that.

**FLASH MONTAGE:**

- **KATHY** reading the pamphlet in harsh lamp-light, biting her nail.
- **KATHY** restringing her guitar, hands steady.
- **KATHY** passing a dive bar she used to haunt, not even glancing.
- **KATHY** laughing, loud and easy, at something **JEREMY** says offscreen—she only hears herself after the fact.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I still didn’t know what the *right* thing looked like.  But I sure as hell knew what the *wrong* thing was.  And for once, I wasn’t doing that.

**FINAL SHOT:**
**KATHY** walking down the street, sun in her face. No music, no slow-mo, no applause. Just the rhythm of her own footsteps, moving forward.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I didn’t know it yet, but that day?  That was agency.  That was the beginning of not giving a single fuck about what anyone else thought.

The shadows are long. The journey’s longer. But this time, **KATHY** walks it standing up.

*Fade out.*

---

## **INT. PLANNED PARENTHOOD CLINIC – PROCEDURE ROOM – THURSDAY MORNING**

**(SOUND)**: The snap of latex gloves. The hum of air conditioning. Speculum clicking.  Soft footsteps in the hallway.

**KATHY** is half-scooted down the table, feet in stirrups, hoodie bunched under her shoulders. She stares hard at the ceiling stain like it owes her money.  She’s somewhere between annoyed and bracing herself.

**NURSE JOHNSON** (calm, businesslike)  
Okay, speculum’s in. You’ll feel some pressure.

*Metal click. Cold, uncomfortable, but not agony.*

**NURSE JOHNSON (CONT’D)**  
I’m just cleaning the cervix—cold swab. Then I’m going to measure the uterus. That part can cramp. Deep breath in… and out.

A thin metal _sound_ slips through the cervical opening.

**KATHY**’s whole body tightens. Her hand fists in the paper.

**KATHY**  
…fuck.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
There it is. You’re doing fine. One more cramp when the IUD goes in.

*Another sharp, deep bolt of pain. Kathy sucks air through her teeth, jaw locked, eyes still glued to the stain.*

**NURSE JOHNSON (CONT’D)**  
Device is in. I’m trimming the strings now. Almost over.

A snip. The speculum eases out of her vagina. The room suddenly feels bigger.

**NURSE JOHNSON (CONT’D)**  
Okay. You can put your feet down. Just stay lying there a minute. Any dizziness?

**KATHY** (flat)  
No. Just hate.

Nurse Johnson smiles with half her mouth, checks a watch.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
That tracks. You might cramp today and tomorrow. Spotting is normal. If you get a fever, foul discharge, or pain that feels like someone’s stabbing you with a screwdriver—call us. Immediately.

She sets a small **sample bottle of ibuprofen** on the tray, plus a pad.

**NURSE JOHNSON (CONT’D)**  
You took ibuprofen before you came?

**KATHY**  
Yeah. Couple hundred milligrams.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
Good. You can take more this afternoon. Don’t be a hero; it works better if you stay ahead of the pain. No tampons for a few days. Call if you can’t feel the strings.

She hands over folded aftercare papers.

**NURSE JOHNSON (CONT’D)**  
Questions?

**KATHY** (already pushing herself up)  
No. I’m good.

She moves a little too fast; the room tilts. She grabs the table.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
Easy. Breathe. You okay?

**KATHY** (through gritted teeth)  
Fine. Just… ready to be done.

Nurse Johnson gives her a quick, measuring look — that tiny flicker when Kathy casually mentioned **how often** she has sex in the intake interview. The flicker vanishes; professionalism snaps back into place.

**NURSE JOHNSON**  
You did great. Take the day as easy as you can.

Kathy pulls on her jeans with careful movements. She takes the aftercare sheet.

Leaves the **ibuprofen bottle** sitting there.

**CUT TO:**

---

## **INT. KATHY’S BEDROOM – LATER THAT DAY**

Kathy’s curled on her side, heating pad clutched to her belly, hoodie half-zipped. The aftercare sheet lies open beside her; “IBUPROFEN” is underlined in yellow.

She fingers the empty _cardboard_ sample sleeve — the pills themselves are still in her purse, rattling faintly when she shifts.

A cramp hits—sharp, hot. Her face screws up. She reaches toward the purse, hesitates.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
I could knock it down. Be sensible. Follow directions like a good girl.

She pulls her hand back. Nails dig into the blanket.

**KATHY (V.O.) (CONT’D)**  
Or I could remember what this is for. Why I’m doing it. Pain’s just another kind of silence.

She exhales hard, stares at the ceiling, rides it out.

---

## **EXT. INTERSTATE 90 WESTBOUND – PRE-DAWN**

The Ford Econoline and JEFF’s battered Escort crawl toward Chicago under a bruised Indiana sky. Sodium vapor lights blur past in sickly orange streaks. The landscape is all industry, all aftermath: chain-link, rust, and smoke.

**SOUND:** Tires thump over frost-heaved concrete. In the van, a cheap FM radio buzzes, lost between two stations. In the Escort, the mixtape hisses, rewinds, warps “*Where Is My Mind?*” into pure static.

**VISUAL:** Quick cuts: Oil refineries ghosted in haze. Empty lots full of wild grass and burned-out shoes. Every window reflects the same tired eyes.

---

## **INT. FORD ECONOLINE – CONTINUOUS**

BILL has the road atlas open, one knee propped on the dash, finger tracing the line west.

**BILL** (dry)
Gary’s next. Then we shoot north. Pray the Skyway’s still up.

**BILL (V.O.)**
If you play in a band, you see America’s real heart: rest stops, off-ramps, and all the towns that make the weather report but never the news.

GILLEY leans forward, scanning the gray horizon.

**GILLEY** (soft, as if to himself)
Place looks like hell coughed it up and forgot to swallow.

A pothole the size of a baptismal font shakes the van like an earthquake. Something in the back rattles and falls over.

---

## **EXT. GARY, INDIANA – PRE-DAWN**

They pass the sign: **WELCOME TO GARY, INDIANA**. Bullet holes in the metal. Graffiti: *SORRY*. A playground slides into view, nothing left but a scorched frame and a cracked swing.

A crumbling overpass stands like the fossil of some extinct optimism.

**VISUAL:** The sign, smeared with rain and light, recedes in the rearview mirror. A lone tricycle lies upturned in a gravel median, as if the world’s already ended and nobody told the toys.

---

## **INT. FORD ESCORT – CONTINUOUS**

**JEFF** drives, jaw set, eyes fixed straight ahead. **JEREMY** fumbles with a tri-fold Chicagoland map, creases growing deeper with every wrong turn.

**KATHY** is balled up in the back seat, hoodie half-zipped, her skin the color of bad news. One hand is pressed white-knuckle to her side.

**JEREMY** (muttering)
Why does every damn street in Chicago have six names? None of these maps agree.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Dayton’s a handshake. Chicago’s a chokehold. If you’re lucky, it’ll let go.

The car rattles over wounded concrete. Sodium light smears across the windshield.  **JEFF** drives, jaw set. **JEREMY** is fighting the Chicagoland map like it insulted his mother. **KATHY** is curled in the back seat, hoodie hood up, one arm wrapped around her stomach.

Another cramp rips through. She bites the sleeve.

**JEFF**  
You sure we shouldn’t have pushed the appointment? You still look—

**KATHY** (hoarse, cutting him off)  
They said cramps for a few days. I’m on schedule.

**JEFF**  
We can stop at a rest area. You can take more—

She snorts.

**KATHY**  
Jeff, unless they’ve got morphine and a time machine, keep driving.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
Ibuprofen. “Stay ahead of the pain.” Right. Rookie mistake. I’m not ahead of anything. Just hanging on and pretending it’s a choice.

She shifts, wincing, eyes squeezed shut as another wave hits.

Jeremy glances back, helpless.

**JEREMY**  
You gonna tell me if this crosses into “hospital” territory?

She cracks one eye open.

**KATHY**  
If I pass out or start seeing God, you’ll be the first to know.

She curls tighter, hand pressing down as though she can pin her uterus in place.

**KATHY (V.O.)**  
Some choices bite twice. Once in a clinic. Once on the road.

---

## **INT. FORD ECONOLINE – SAME**

GILLEY glances at the Escort through the side mirror, spots KATHY’s hunched shape.

**GILLEY** (low)
She doesn’t look right.

**BILL** (grim)
Neither does this city.

**BILL (V.O.)**
Gary’s not a place. It’s a verdict.

---

## **INT. FORD ECONOLINE VAN – SKYWAY APPROACH – NIGHT**

The **Sears Tower** — an obsidian blade in the sky, barely visible through haze.

**BILL** (pointing, kid-on-Christmas)
There! Sears Tower!

**GILLEY** (deadpan, unblinking)
That’s twenty-five miles out, man. We’re not even in the same area code.

**BILL (V.O.)**
Chicago wasn’t just a city. It was a continent. And we were just bugs on the windshield, heading for the lights.

---

## **INT. FORD ESCORT – CONTINUOUS**

**KATHY** is all sharp angles and clenched fists, eyes squeezed shut. **JEREMY** scrambles with a plastic water bottle, hands shaking. **JEFF** grips the steering wheel, silent, jaw set like a lock.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
This was supposed to be adventure. Big music, big city, all that. But Kathy — she was off script. She was fighting a battle the rest of us couldn’t even see.

**KATHY** (breathless, half-laugh, half-moan)
Christ, this hurts.

---

## **EXT. SKYWAY BRIDGE – NIGHT**

The van and Escort crawl to the apex, the entire city of Chicago blooming below — blue-white neon, sodium vapor, a circuit board of dreams.

**VISUAL:** The skyline is both promise and threat, flickering like something unstable. The highway ahead, the city beyond, all of it pulsing, alive.  In the back of the Escort, **KATHY**’s face is turned to the glass — not for the view, but just to keep the air moving. She’s not sightseeing, she’s surviving.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
All I wanted was to not bleed. All I got was this pain.  Maybe that’s the price. Maybe this is just what it costs to change — for real.

**SOUND:**
The engine’s relentless drone, radio static, Kathy’s sharp intakes of breath. For everyone else: anticipation. For her: just endurance.

They roll past a garish billboard:  **"HURT? CALL BART!"**  A lawyer with a shark’s smile, lit up brighter than the skyline.

**VISUAL:**
The sign glows garishly, too big, too bright — mocking the pain inside the car.

**FINAL SHOT:**
The convoy slips into the city’s electric sprawl. Out there: hope, danger, noise.
Inside: a girl with new metal in her body, trying to remember what hope feels like.

---

## **INT. FORD ESCORT – CONTINUOUS**

The car’s interior is humid with tension. The highway unspools outside, but inside, time slows to a crawl.

**JEREMY** shifts, the map crinkling in his lap. He glances at the rearview, voice low, trying to sound casual.

**JEREMY** (tentative)
So…uh, **KATHY**…did they tell you what it’d be like? After?

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
I just wanted to say something useful. Something that didn’t sound like a script from health class.

**KATHY** (flat, almost amused)
Yeah. They “briefed” me. Like I was about to parachute into Normandy.

(Pauses, then quieter)
They left out the part where it feels like someone’s yanking out your insides with a coat hanger.

She shifts, sharp breath hissing between her teeth.

**KATHY** (CONT’D, muttering)
And I forgot to take anything this morning. Genius move.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Their concern wasn’t the problem. The problem was I didn’t want to need it.

A long silence. The tape hisses. The car vibrates.

**JEFF** (softly, reaching)
If you want—

**KATHY** (immediate, sharp, not looking up)
Don’t.

The single word has teeth, but her voice is barely above a whisper.

**(VISUAL):**
Close-up — Kathy, pale and resolute, eyes fixed on the seat back.  **Jeremy** nods, a soft “okay,” his own jaw clenching as he looks away.  **Jeff** drops the idea, hands tightening on the wheel.  The unspoken truce is: let her hurt, but don’t try to fix it.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
She wasn’t mad at us. Just…done. And sometimes you have to let people be done.

The car hurtles onward, the city growing in the distance, everyone locked in their own orbit of concern and helplessness.

**JEREMY** (wistful, almost in awe)
Can you believe **CREMEANS** now? Pager. Business cards. The whole “rock manager” act.

(Pause)
Last year, he didn’t even own a suit his mom didn’t buy.

**JEFF** (with a crooked smile)
Still borrows his dad’s ties.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
It felt like we were still in high school—just with more gas money and worse hangovers. But **CREMEANS**? He was already living in the next chapter.

---

# **CHAPTER TWELVE: A BAND DIVIDED CANNOT STAND**

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – TUNNEL – NIGHT**

The band, with **CREMEANS** trailing, emerges from the gray mouth of the journey into the cathedral of their ambitions. A concrete tunnel yawns before them—bleak, cavernous, swallowing sound and light and nerves.

Footsteps echo with military precision. Wind whistles through concrete gaps. Far off, a hollow mic-check thump.

The camera tracks from behind—a long lens, their figures shrinking as the tunnel stretches. The flicker of overhead fluorescents. Shadows tall and restless.

**KATHY** limps, one hand at her abdomen. Her jaw set, sweat blooming at her brow. This is not cramping—this is mutiny.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
This wasn’t pain. This was revenge. My uterus staging a full-blown insurrection.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
If I could collapse right here, I would. Maybe get a sympathy write-up in the student paper. But that’d be too easy.

**CREMEANS** stops, pivots—worry etched deep.

**CREMEANS**
You okay? You look like you’ve been shot.

Noir lighting—his face half in shadow, half in dread.

**KATHY** (weak, flat)
Fine. Just…playing through.

She steps again, almost folds.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
She wasn’t okay. We all knew it. But nobody knew what to say.

**CREMEANS** leans in, lowering his voice.

**CREMEANS**
You don’t have to do this. We can—

**KATHY** (sharp, breathless)
We *are* doing this. Shut up.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Tour manager? Sure. Medic? Not a chance.

They walk on. The tunnel widens. Ahead, the field glows—Dyche Stadium, pulsing with the promise of what could be.

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – TUNNEL – EVENING**

The tunnel stinks of Gatorade, dried sweat, and the kind of cleaning chemical that never quite covers the mildew. The band stands in a crooked huddle under flickering fluorescents. Distant feedback from a soundcheck rattles the vents.

**Cremeans** glances at his watch. He’s checked it three times in two minutes, as if he expects it to start counting backwards and save him from this disaster in waiting.

**CREMEANS**
We’re up at two tomorrow. That’s fifteen hours. I’m going to say this one time: What’s the plan?

He gets six blank stares in return. The word “plan” bounces off the group like a Nerf dart.

**JEFF** (leans against the cinderblock wall, half-smiling at some internal joke)
Plan? Sure. I’m going to infiltrate the library, dismantle the Western Canon, and—if there’s time—kick Derrida in the balls.

**JIM** (laughs)
Isn’t he dead?

**JEFF**
Exactly. Easier target.

He considers for half a beat, then shrugs, the joke turning sour.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Or maybe I’ll just hit the first dive bar, drink until I forget why I ever learned to read, and let Sartre pick up the tab.

**BILL**
(rolling his eyes, thumbs out a number on his phone)
I’m ordering pizza. I’m calling every girl I ever met in Evanston. And if anybody else touches my pineapple again, I’ll break their fucking fingers.

**BILL (V.O.)**
Nourishment, nostalgia, nookie. The holy trinity. I’m not ashamed. Somebody’s gotta fuck tonight and it won’t be Jeff, Mr. Derrida’s-corpse.

**KATHY** (tugs her hoodie down over one bare thigh, mischief and pain both showing up at the edges of her mouth)
I’m thinking: find the dumbest frat, steal their keg, and lead a rooftop singalong. I might even wear underwear. But probably not.

She glances around, daring someone to judge her. Nobody does.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
If I’m going to bleed tonight, it should at least be loud.

**JIM** (grinning, eyes shining, adrenaline already fizzing)
Party until I black out. Then find the nearest regret and French kiss it.

He slaps Gilley on the back, almost too hard.

**JIM (V.O.)**
If chaos was a vitamin, I’d be pissing neon.

**JEREMY** (soft, almost to himself, checking his notebook like it’s a Ouija board)
I’m calling my wife. I need proof I exist outside this band.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
God, I miss her. More than I should. More than I’ll admit if anyone asks.

**GILLEY** (glancing at the exit, eyes alight with mischief, voice low and confidential)
Scoreboard. Christmas lights. “69.” Don’t ask. You’ll see it, or you won’t.

He grins—anarchy is religion and he’s the high priest.

**(INSERT: For just a second, we see him already perched up there—legs swinging, a crown of red and green bulbs buzzing around his head like a halo for the damned.)**

**CREMEANS** (stares, stricken, like a middle school substitute teacher who just realized his class has knives)
You’re…all serious? This is your plan?

He looks at the Mountain Dew in his hand like maybe there’s vodka in it, or should be.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Fifteen hours until the biggest show of our lives, and I’m babysitting the cast of a punk rock *Lord of the Flies*. This isn’t a band. It’s a slow-motion car wreck, and I’m riding shotgun with the airbags removed.

He glances over the group one last time—pizza orders flying, Jim already halfway to the exit, Gilley plotting larceny, Kathy’s pain turning to rage and back again, Jeremy dialing home and pretending not to tear up.

Behind them, the tunnel. Ahead, the stadium. A night to be wasted.

**Cremeans** takes a long drink, clutching the bottle like it’s holy. He leads them out into the dark, a shepherd guiding his flock of beautiful idiots into the wild.

**SMASH TO BLACK.**

---

## **THE LIBRARY (INITIAL DECEPTION)**

**INT. NORTHWESTERN UNIVERSITY LIBRARY – NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

(SOUND): U2’s “Zoo Station” erupts, distortion thick as wet wool. The guitar riff isn’t just a cue—it’s a threat. The band explodes out of the tunnel and Jeff peels off, swallowed by the fluorescent sanctum of academia.)_

It smells like toner, sweat, and ambition—freshly shampooed carpet, but under it all, the staleness of a thousand deferred dreams. Students are hunched over books like parishioners in pews. No one looks up. No one breathes too loud. Overhead, the lights buzz a half-step out of tune with the music in Jeff’s head.

Jeff strides in, overdressed for the occasion—blazer slung over a T-shirt, tie slouched somewhere between neck and shame. Wire frames perched low on his nose. He’s playing at adulthood, half method actor, half stoned.

He stalks the stacks, eyes sharp and empty, hunting something sacred and idiotic. He picks a fat book with the giddy confidence of a man about to fake his way through an oral exam.

**(Insert: “Post-Structuralist Literary Theory: A Reader.”)**

He flips it open, finds a random page titled “Hyperreality and the Death of Meaning.” Nods at it like he’s found porn.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Immersion in local culture. Phase one: infiltration.

He yawns so hard he cracks his jaw, then slides a battered steel flask from his blazer’s inner pocket, never breaking eye contact with the page. He takes a slow pull—vodka, cheap and antiseptic—eyes watering as it sears its way down. Still, he doesn’t stop. He *grins* at the pain.

A passing grad student gives him a nervous side-eye. Jeff holds up the book, deadly serious.

**JEFF** (deadpan, whispering)
Baudrillard is my co-pilot.

The student blinks, stutters a laugh, and hurries off, probably to call campus security.

Jeff ambles over to a study pod, slaps the fat tome on a table, sets his flask on top of it, and considers the tableau: Literature and liquor, sacred and profane, all on the altar of higher education.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Phase two: corrupt the canon.

He leaves the book—open, flask-shaped ring forming on “*Simulation and Simulacra”*—and slides out of the library, the doors hissing shut behind him like the world’s saddest confession booth.

---

## **THE REAL IMMERSION**

**EXT. EVANSTON STREET – OUTSIDE A DIVE BAR – 2 A.M.**

(SOUND): “Zoo Station” is now roaring in his skull, the snare like a train jumping tracks. The neon from the bar windows flickers, trying to keep time. Jeff stumbles through the door, hair vertical, tie a noose around his shoulder, shirt open at the throat like he lost a bet with fashion itself.)_

His hand clings to a half-empty tequila bottle. It’s his partner, his crutch, his plus-one to every bad idea. The air is electric with the possibility of violence—someone’s yelling about karaoke, someone else is puking on a Civic. Jeff could be in Berlin, or Dayton, or nowhere.

**BOUNCER** (shouting from the door)
That’s it! No Springsteen in German, ever again! You’re banned till the end of time, pal!

**JEFF** (spinning, grinning, bottle raised)
*Ich bin der Boss, motherfucker!*

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Apparently “immersion in local culture” means tequila, broken German, and discovering the limits of human dignity with a crowd of strangers who can’t remember your name.

He bows deeply, tequila sloshing. He nearly overbalances, catches himself with a slap against the bar’s brick wall. A cheer erupts from inside, punctuated by the shrieked opening notes of “*Like a Prayer.*” Jeff salutes—solemn as a priest at a funeral.

Then, his shoe finds a wet pizza box—he goes down like a felled scarecrow, arms flailing, bottle spinning through the air in a shimmering arc.

Cut to black. The pulse of the bassline keeps thumping. Regret is for tomorrow.

---

## **THE UNDERGRADUATES (UNSUSPECTING VICTIMS)**

**EXT. NORTHWESTERN UNIVERSITY LIBRARY – NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

(SOUND): “Zoo Station” churns, its machinery chewing itself, low and sick under the campus lights.)_

Two undergrads—fresh-faced, baggy-sweatered, armor-plated with textbooks—shuffle out the library doors, their conversation brittle with caffeine and terror of mediocrity. One wears a Star Trek pin. The other wears stress like cologne.

Suddenly, **JEFF** lurches out of the dark. The tequila bottle swings from his fist like a censer. His eyes are lit up—too much, too wide, somewhere between revelation and psychosis.

He blocks their path with a kind of manic joy, throwing his arms out as if to bless them or mug them, maybe both.

**JEFF**
You guys! *You guys.* Listen—I’ve cracked Derrida. I *killed* the author. *With this!*
(*He brandishes the tequila bottle. In the neon, it glows like a magic wand or a Molotov.*)

The undergrads freeze, trapped between the dream of higher learning and the nightmare of Midwest nightlife.

**UNDERGRAD #1**
Uh…we, um, we have a seminar in the morning…

**JEFF**
Good! Great! Let me audit, but only if I can scream about Lacan during roll call.
(*He grins, unblinking. His tie swings like a metronome that’s lost the beat.*)

**JEFF (V.O.)**
I was Socrates, if Socrates had tenure at AA. Diogenes with shoes from Filene’s Basement. These poor bastards—they were my students, and I was ready to ruin their transcript.

He leans in, his voice dropping to a gravelly whisper. He recites, not Derrida, but the Night Ranger lyric, and pins them with the fervor of a man who’s never been told “no.”

**JEFF**
*Motoring…what’s your price for flight?*

(*He points at Star Trek Pin. Stern.*)
That’s *punctum*, right? Barthes wrote that. That’s the wound. That’s the—wound.

The undergrads exchange a look—one that says: We are going to die, and my mother will blame my choice of major.

Jeff sways, then bestows his blessing:

**JEFF**
Go. Learn. Sin bravely.

He stumbles off into the dark, trailing the chorus, his shadow twitching on the pavement.

---

## **THE DEBATE (A DISASTER)**

**EXT. CAMPUS QUAD – LATER THAT NIGHT**

The quad is nearly empty except for one folding chair, a trashcan masquerading as a podium, and a lamppost that throws harsh light like a prison spotlight. Crickets sing. The world holds its breath.

**JEFF** is at the center, elevated on a blue recycling bin, tequila bottle gripped like a gavel. His audience: a nervous couple hurrying by, and a raccoon, squat and defiant, chewing something with intent.

(SOUND): “Zoo Station” now glitches in his brain, all teeth and feedback. The quad is his coliseum.)_

**JEFF** (*to the raccoon, with Socratic thunder*)
The problem with “différance” is you can’t spell it sober!

(*He sloshes tequila across his shirt, undeterred.*)
And you!

(*points at the raccoon*)
You get it, don’t you? You little semiotic fuck!

The couple speeds up, heads ducked, not breaking stride. The raccoon freezes. Jeff is undaunted.

He lurches onto the folding chair, waves the tequila bottle like a scepter. He starts to sing—off-key, wheezing, desperate:

**JEFF**
Every rose has its thorn…just like every night has its dawn…

The raccoon blinks. It’s unclear if this is disgust or enlightenment.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Was I making a point? Maybe. Maybe the point was that there is no point, and the point is the wound, and the wound is…tequila.

He makes a dramatic move to mount the bike rack behind the trashcan, foot slips, he tumbles in slow motion, knocks the recycling bin sideways, the bottle clattering off the rim and rolling into the dark.

He ends up sprawled in the damp grass, tie across his face, the raccoon now investigating his shoe. Overhead, a campus security light flickers—on, off, on, off—casting him in and out of existence beneath a poster for “Mindfulness Yoga.”

**JEFF** (slurred, to the raccoon)
You’re the only one who understands me, Roland.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
The debate was…spirited.

The raccoon gives up, waddles off in search of a less tragic meal. Jeff’s eyes roll back as the night swallows him whole, the beat of “Zoo Station” still thumping in his chest like an aftershock.

*Cut to black. Regret pending.*

---

## **THE TEQUILA-FUELED EPIPHANY**

**EXT. UNIVERSITY PARK – VERY LATE NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

(SOUND): “Zoo Station” is coming apart, tape flutter, every note dragging its feet in the mud. The air is thick with dew and the faint, sour reek of lawn fertilizer.)_

The quad is a graveyard for ambition at this hour. Security lights gutter, the lamps buzz and stutter, threatening blackout with every surge. Jeff sits slumped on a bench, tequila bottle resting in his lap, his tie now a failed tourniquet for dignity. His knees are spread wide like a man ready to take a punch.

Across from him, a squirrel perches atop a trash can, clutching a sandwich crust with the dignity of royalty and the focus of someone who has never, ever paid tuition.

Jeff watches, pupils blown. Time stretches and twists—seconds become elastic, moments syrup-thick. The squirrel chews. Jeff laughs—no, he cries—no, it’s both, a laugh that splits its own skull.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
The squirrel gets it. The squirrel *is* the text. There’s no meaning left but hunger and repetition. We’re all just crust-chasers in the library of Babel.

He wipes at his eyes, bottle still balanced like a scepter. The squirrel, haloed by a shaft of flickering light, chews on—a minor deity in a trash cathedral.

**JEFF** (*soft, awestruck*)
You get it, right? There’s no center. No origin story. Just…text. Just tail. And I have neither.

He starts to sob, but the sob is wrapped in a giggle, and the giggle is half a hiccup. He folds forward, head in hands, tequila pooling at his feet.

---

## **THE SQUIRREL (AN UNWILLING PARTICIPANT)**

**EXT. UNIVERSITY PARK – CONTINUOUS**

Jeff slides off the bench with the slow, shaky purpose of a religious pilgrim halfway through his penance. The bottle swings at his side, forgotten but ever-present.

He approaches the squirrel as if closing distance with a war correspondent or a ghost. The grass is wet, sticking to his knees as he crouches, face level with his accidental therapist.

**JEFF**
Let’s *talk*, okay? Just you and me. Two lost souls parsing a cosmic meat grinder. You ever stare down the void and find only…tail?

He extends the bottle—a toast, a confession, a final offering.

**JEFF (CONT’D)**
You ever read Baudrillard? Hyperreality? No? Just me?

The squirrel freezes. For a second, it considers—really considers—then bolts into a bush, sandwich crust first, tail flagging a sharp fuck-you to philosophy.

(VISUAL): We’re in Jeff’s spinning POV, the world lurching, the sound of tiny claws a Doppler echo that feels like existential rejection.)_

Jeff shouts after it, voice cracking:

**JEFF**
Coward! FACE YOUR ONTOLOGY! Come back! Tell me who authored your narrative!

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Gone. The only soul that ever listened. Even squirrels have their limit for bullshit.

He collapses in the grass, surrounded by flyers, wrappers, and tiny hotel-sized bottles. The quad reclaims him as just another mistake.

“*Zoo Station*” sputters out—a final gasp, then silence. In the foreground, the squirrel—caught in a sudden shaft of heroic light—bounds off, the soundtrack briefly swelling with a mocking, operatic flourish. The world spins on, uncaring.

---

## **THE NAVIGATION**

**EXT. EVANSTON RESIDENTIAL NEIGHBORHOOD – DEEP NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

(SOUND): His shoes slap the sidewalk, one a half-beat behind the other, echoing down a street lined with trees older than regret. Wind chimes tinkle from porches—an accidental requiem for youth. Somewhere, a dog barks the threat of suburbia.)_

Jeff moves down the block like a marionette with cut strings, arms swinging, bottle now a sad, swinging pendulum. His eyes are glassy, but behind them a fierce logic whirs—broken, but working. He passes under pools of streetlamp glow, each one a little interrogation booth. Victorian houses loom: tall, pretty, and judgmental.

He stops, squints at a street sign. The words ripple and blur, turn themselves inside out. He nods anyway—certainty is its own reward.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Navigation…never my strong suit. Even with a compass, I’d find north and ask it for a cigarette. Tonight, I’m plotting a course with tequila and the ghost of Columbus. No one survives this voyage, not even me.

He salutes a mailbox marked “HENDERSON,” raises his bottle in a toast to the American postal service, and mutters:

**JEFF**
The center cannot hold. Mail is just signifier, man.

He turns and walks directly into a hedge. There’s a dull, leafy *thump*. For a second, the world goes green. A cat stares at him from the window, eyes full of ancient pity.

He disappears into the shrubbery.

---

## **THE AWAKENING**

**EXT. HENDERSON FRONT LAWN – PRE-DAWN**

The first rays of sun sneak over the rooftops, gold and pitiless. Dew has soaked the grass, his shirt, his pride. Jeff lies facedown in a nest of wet leaves, the sprinkler arcing cold jets over his back like an indifferent god. His tie has migrated north, knotted around his forehead like a failed attempt at heroism.

(SOUND): The *chhh-chhh* of the sprinkler, birds gossiping above, the faint creak of a swing set somewhere down the block.)_

A robin lands nearby, considers Jeff, then decides he’s beneath even their notice.

Water spatters his face. He blinks awake, sputtering, vision full of grass blades and sunlight and utter, magnificent defeat.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Turns out, “local culture” means learning to sleep wherever gravity dumps you. Lawns, hedges, existential despair—take your pick. Sprinklers come standard.

He sits up, grass clinging to his elbows, book still glued to one palm by last night’s spilled mascara and sweat. The flask jangles from his belt loop. He scans his surroundings—a world that’s gone on without him. He’s miles from glory, miles from home.

He looks at the rising sun, then at the sky, then at the sprinkler that nails him right between the eyes. He flops back, defeated, lets the water baptize him.

**JEFF**
(*muttering, mostly to the gods of lawns and mistakes*)
Never again. Until next time.

He rolls over, the frame spinning up, sprinkler still working, birds still singing, the world uncaring.

**CUT TO BLACK.**

---

## **THE WALK OF SHAME**

**EXT. EVANSTON – LAKESIDE BIKE PATH – DAWN**

The air is crisp, sharp enough to flay what’s left of Jeff’s dignity. Sunlight shivers on Lake Michigan; the water is still, unsympathetic. Jeff stumbles forward, a textbook case in entropy. Shirt buttoned wrong—buttoned with aggression, not accuracy. Tie wilted and defeated, hanging like a dead tongue. Shoes don’t match, laces trailing in the dew. Grass stains on his knees, leaves in his hair—nature’s way of tagging him “found object, damaged.”

He passes a squad of joggers—spandex, headphones, sweat that smells like hope. They move as one organism, legs pumping, faces taut and empty of consequence. One runner, a woman with a ponytail and the jawline of a prosecutor, slows as she passes Jeff. She gives him the kind of look reserved for roadkill that might still twitch.

Jeff returns the stare, bloodshot eyes flickering with the battered pride of the newly damned. He tries to straighten his posture, fails, and limps on.

(VISUAL): In slow-motion, the joggers pass in a golden blur—angelic, invincible, untouchable. Jeff is a ghost moving backward through time, every step a confession. “Zoo Station” deconstructs itself, the riff dissolving into melancholy echoes, a hangover with strings.)_

**JEFF (V.O.)**
This isn’t satire anymore. This is my biography. I am the joke and the punchline, both at once.

---

## **THE REUNION (A DISASTER)**

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE TUNNEL – MINUTES LATER**

Cremeans paces, his clipboard a shield, his pager chirping with existential dread. The rest of the band waits, faces pinched with anticipation and contempt. Sunlight seeps in, hard and unkind.

**JEFF** stumbles into the tunnel, silhouette hunched, eyes wild. He looks like a man who survived the apocalypse and brought the weather with him. His clothes drip with the residue of every bad choice—tequila, humiliation, grass stains, and the faint reek of animal.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Ground control to Major Tom…we have a problem. And that problem is about to vomit in the loading dock.

No one speaks. The silence is heavy, primed for violence or laughter. Jim blinks, once, twice—his jaw drops.

**JIM**
Holy shit. He made it.

The band stares at Jeff—half disgusted, half amazed, all in awe of his survival. Jeremy covers a laugh with a cough. Bill shakes his head. Kathy makes a sign of the cross, just in case.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Maybe post-structuralism was a bad idea on tequila. But that squirrel…it understood me, man. Better than most people ever did.

(VISUAL): The band is clustered together, backs straight, instruments gleaming. Jeff stands apart, an oil stain in a white shirt, the human cost of the evening’s philosophy lesson.)_

From the field, the opening notes of their first song begin—loud, merciless, the world moving forward without apology.

---

**FINAL SHOT**

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BLEACHERS – LATER**

Jeff sits alone, legs splayed, elbows on knees. Rows upon rows of empty seats yawn before him—each one waiting to be filled, to bear witness, to judge. He looks small, inconsequential, absolutely human.

(SOUND): The last faded echo of “Zoo Station.” The stadium breathes. His own breath—ragged, trembling, alive. The world is enormous, indifferent, hungry.)_

**JEFF (V.O.)**
It started as a joke. But the punchline? That was all mine.

*(The camera floats up, higher and higher, until Jeff is nothing but a blot, a rumor, a cautionary tale etched into the morning. The architecture of regret.)*

**TEXT ON SCREEN:**
**DYCHE STADIUM – EVANSTON, IL – 8:13 A.M.**

**FADE OUT.**

---

## **THE MISSION BRIEFING (SELF-DELUSION)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM – PARKING LOT – NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

(SOUND): The unmistakable, spoken intro of “Rico Suave”—“Suave…suave…Rico…Suave…”—slinks through the humid night air like cologne and catastrophe. The lot is bathed in ugly halogen, shadow slicing everywhere. The stadium looms in the background, not so much a fortress as a dare.)_

Gilley is gone. Rico is here.

Half his shirt is open, exposing what might be muscle, might be nerves. Aviators glint under stadium lights, utterly unnecessary but godlike. Chewing gum with the ferocity of a man who’s lost too much and intends to lose more. Every muscle flexes for a nonexistent audience. His right hand flashes a finger gun at the band van, then, satisfied, he tilts his jaw skyward—wind (from somewhere) ruffling his hair just so.

(VISUAL): Dutch angle, fake lens flares. The parking lot is every late-night music video, but with trash bags blowing by instead of models. A stray cat hisses, sprints out of frame.)_

**RICO (V.O.)**
Operation: 69. This was no ordinary prank. This was destiny, danger, debauchery, all rolled up in a man’s cologne-soaked confidence. The risk? Immeasurable. The reward? Eternal scoreboard immortality.

He yanks a pair of purple novelty sunglasses from his pocket, slides them *over* the aviators. He is now shielded from the sun, the moon, and reality itself.

He starts toward the stadium, breaking into a slow-motion jog, hips rolling like he’s been hired to seduce a camera lens, not sneak past campus security. His chest puffs out, his ass follows. He looks like a man who read about machismo once, then poured tequila on the page.

He stops mid-stride, glances left and right—no witnesses except the ghosts of failed athletes and that one vengeful cat. He winks anyway, then vaults a low parking barrier with the grace of a drunk antelope, landing in a heap but popping up instantly, untouchable.

**RICO (V.O.)**
If anyone was watching, they were already in love. Or in fear. Maybe both. That’s what it means to be Rico.

He heads for the perimeter fence, gum still snapping, mission locked in.

---

## **THE INFILTRATION (A COMICAL CLIMB)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM – PERIMETER FENCE – NIGHT**

Rico crouches low behind a bush (that offers zero cover), muttering action movie nonsense:

**RICO (whispered)**
Breach. Extraction. Tango down. Full penetration. God, I love this job.

He pops his neck, adjusts his double sunglasses, and surveys the wall. It’s just concrete, maybe eight feet high, but in Rico’s mind it’s the Berlin Wall, Mount Everest, and a Mexican border crossing all at once.

He tries to vault it with a running leap, but clips a garbage can.

**SFX: METAL CLANG, the can skittering away, raccoon scattering like a shell-shocked extra.**

Rico sprawls in the dirt, mouthful of mulch. He pops up instantly—spits out a leaf.

**RICO (V.O.)**
Stealth is overrated. They never see you coming if they’re too busy pitying you.

He attempts a tactical somersault (it’s more of a sideways flop), and lands at the base of the fence. His fingers paw at brickwork, shoes scrabbling for anything resembling a foothold. He finds a rusted storm drain, jams his sneaker in, and hauls himself up, muscles shaking, shirt riding up to reveal a streak of questionable tattoo and too much belly.

A security camera stares. The red “record” light blinks.  Rico grins and blows it a kiss.

**RICO (V.O.)**
Thirty feet of pure concrete hate. No plan, no gear, no backup. Just Rico and a hamstring so tight it could play first chair in the orchestra.

With a final, ugly grunt, he flops over the top—knees, elbows, face—and lands flat on his back, sprawled and sweating, but grinning like a porn star who made rent.

He lies there a second, hands outstretched to the night.

**RICO** (*breathless, triumphant*)
Scoreboard, baby.

---

## **THE SECURITY GUARD (AN UNWITTING ACCOMPLICE)**

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – SECURITY OFFICE – NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

The air is heavy with the scent of microwave burritos and ancient dust. The *Security Office* is barely more than a shoebox with a wall of old tube monitors and one paunchy guard—mustache drooping, polyester pants threatening mutiny. He’s glued to a black-and-white TV hawking Civil War chess sets, eyes flickering, brain idling somewhere in the fog between infomercial and dream.

**INFOMERCIAL (V.O.)**
And *you* too can own a set of commemorative Civil War chess pieces for only three easy payments of $29.99!

The guard’s jaw slackens. Sweat beads beneath his chin. A baloney sandwich sits at his elbow, wilted and accusatory, untouched and unloved.

Behind the grimy office window: **Rico**. He’s hunched behind an offensively fake plastic ficus—leaves so shiny you could see your reflection if the lighting weren’t so bad. Rico’s shades glint beneath the emergency lights. He tiptoes, knees high, back low, as if auditioning for *Looney Tunes Gone Latin.*

Two steps. Freeze. He hugs the plant like a life raft.  Three more steps.

Freeze.

He spins the ficus to “camouflage” from a security camera that’s already pointed at the floor. The ficus makes a half-hearted squeak. Rico narrows his eyes, peering through the leaves with deadly seriousness.

**RICO (V.O.)**
Most people see a ficus. I see a goddamn invisibility cloak. You know what you call stealth this sexy? Illegal in twelve states.

(VISUAL): A sudden whip zoom—a Tarantino crash-in—right to Rico’s wide, mad eyes through the leaves. The cut splices against the guard’s half-blinking stare, the sandwich shifting imperceptibly as gravity claims it.)_

Rico glides past the booth, holding his breath, daring the gods to break the spell. The guard remains comatose, finally reaching for his sandwich as if it’s the climax of a tragedy.

Rico vanishes around the corner, ficus abandoned, the mission alive.

---

## **THE TUNNEL CRAWL (A TIGHT SQUEEZE)**

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – MAINTENANCE VENTILATION SHAFT – NIGHT**

(SOUND): The soft, panicked rasp of tank-top cotton against galvanized steel. Rico’s breath echoes, every exhale a minor existential crisis.)_

Rico, now down to a grease-stained white tank, army-crawls through a shaft that was clearly designed for raccoons, not sex gods. Every movement is a negotiation with physics:

Left elbow—wedge.
Right hip—jam.
Both knees—scream for mercy.

A thousand dust bunnies stick to his arms and neck. Something ancient and furry brushes his cheek. Rico freezes, eye twitching, sweat pooling in the small of his back.

**RICO (V.O.)**
Turns out, Rico Suave isn’t quite as smooth when he’s crawling through Satan’s vacuum cleaner. My dignity’s been left behind with my last clean pair of boxers.

He pulls forward, shorts hiking higher, a cobweb draping across his forehead like a bridal veil at a funeral.

(VISUAL): Extreme close-up on Rico’s one wild eye, darting. Suddenly, a taxidermy raccoon (from a forgotten Wildcat display) flashes by in a fever-dream hallucination. The duct rattles ominously. Rico’s breath catches. He pushes on.)_

**RICO (V.O.)**
Rico never quits. Rico never surrenders. Rico just…really, really needs some Gold Bond and maybe a tetanus shot.

He drags himself forward, leaving a trail of self-respect and skin cells behind.
Somewhere, “Rico Suave” still pulses, distant and triumphant. The man will not be stopped.

---

## **THE SCOREBOARD ASCENT (A DANGEROUS STUNT)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM – SCOREBOARD STRUCTURE – NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

(SOUND): Heroic orchestral blast rips through the air, crashing into the greasy synths and comic bravado of “Rico Suave.” The crickets fall silent as the night pivots to spectacle.)_

The scoreboard rises above Rico—an obsidian slab, wires trailing, bolts half-rusted. It is both monument and dare, the final boss in a platformer no one else is playing.

Rico stands below, now with *fingerless gloves* (borrowed, stolen, or hallucinated—who knows?), a harness clamped around his hips like a chastity device for idiots. He grins, mouth full of blue gum, eyes glassy with altitude sickness and destiny.

**RICO (V.O.)**
Adrenaline was pure jet fuel. My heart was trying to kick its way out. This was Everest. The Berlin Wall. That jungle gym from second grade, except now I had tequila and hubris and a slightly better mustache.

He throws a coil of rope over his shoulder, bounces once on his heels, and launches into the climb. First try: a heroic leap, immediately loses grip, dangles one-handed, curses in Spanglish. Recovers. Shimmies up a support beam, boots slipping, chest hair catching on a rusted bolt.

Halfway up, he wedges a sneaker in a gap, forehead pressed to steel for balance.

A pigeon erupts from a hidden nest above, flapping in his face.

**RICO**
¡No me jodas! I’m working here!

He flips the bird off one-handed, regains balance, and continues upward—legs bicycling, harness riding higher, ass now the most visible thing in Cook County. He pulls himself onto a narrow ledge, panting, sweat stinging his eyes.

(VISUAL): Low-angle heroic shot—Rico silhouetted, dangling from a beam, teeth bared, the night behind him infinite and inviting disaster.)_

---

## **THE CHRISTMAS LIGHT ACQUISITION (A SHADY DEAL)**

**INT. DYCHE STADIUM – STORAGE ROOM – NIGHT**

Rico crashes through a warped door with a shoulder tackle worthy of a telenovela. The air inside tastes like mouse droppings and old plastic. The light overhead buzzes and flickers, threatening to die at any moment.

A shelf lines one wall—holiday casualties stacked and forgotten: fake holly, an extension cord tangled around a melted snowman, a cracked Santa head leering in the dark.

But Rico’s quarry is there—a box of Christmas lights, wires knotted, colors still radiant despite a decade of neglect.

(VISUAL): Close-up on Rico’s eyes, pupils dilated, nostrils flared like a raccoon who’s found the dumpster of his dreams. The lights glint in the box, haloed by the flickering bulb above. Tarantino crash-zoom to his hand reaching out, trembling with anticipation.)_

**RICO (V.O.)**
Red for love, green for envy, blue for regret, yellow for whatever the hell I wanted it to be. But tonight? Tonight was all about celebration. You don’t conquer the scoreboard with shame. You do it with technicolor sin.

He lifts the tangled lights reverently, kisses a bulb for luck, and then jams the whole box into his backpack. The cracked Santa winks in the shadows.

Rico spins, slams the door, sprints out—hair wild, face shining with the promise of neon glory. He barrels toward the stairs, backpack jangling, a one-man holiday parade headed for infamy.

(SOUND): “Rico Suave” chorus blares, the world suddenly brighter and dumber.)_

---

## **THE WIRING (A COMICAL ELECTROCUTION SCARE)**

**EXT. SCOREBOARD CATWALK – NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

Rico is sprawled on the narrow catwalk behind the scoreboard, the wind whipping at his tank top, the city lights glimmering in the distant dark. He’s surrounded by a nest of Christmas lights—twisted, knotted, half-blinking, their colored bulbs like mutant fruit ready to explode.

He grins, teeth bared, hair plastered to his forehead in sweat-drenched curls.
In one hand: wire strippers he’s never used before.
In the other: a bundle of exposed copper, frayed and twitching with forbidden energy.

A battered metal box looms beside him—slapped with a label that screams:

> [!caution]
> HIGH VOLTAGE – AUTHORIZED PERSONNEL ONLY

Rico squints, wipes his brow with the back of his hand, and chews his gum hard enough to break a filling.

**RICO (V.O.)**
I’d seen Die Hard like twenty times. How hard could it be? Red to green, black to blue, all the colors of the rainbow. The worst that happens? I die as I lived—stupid and overconfident.

He jams a wire into the box. Instantly—SPARKS.

The lights stutter, his whole body seizes up cartoonishly, and for one holy moment his hair stands out in every direction—lit from within, a neon halo of dumbass courage.

**SFX:** BZZZZAP! A flash. The scent of burning plastic and fresh regret.

Rico convulses, eyes bugging, legs flailing, every muscle clenched in a rictus grin. He looks, for a split second, like a coked-up raccoon in a tanning bed.

He yanks his hand away, staggers back, smoke curling from his knuckles. He coughs, wheezes, and then—smiles. Teeth faintly blue, pupils dialed to eleven.

**RICO (V.O.)**
I was aiming for “Bond villain.” I got “shocked raccoon with a minor death wish.” And yet? Glorious.

---

## **THE MESSAGE (A MOMENT OF TRIUMPH)**

**EXT. STADIUM FIELD – NIGHT**

The camera floats high above the field. The stadium is empty, silent as a cathedral—except for the monstrous scoreboard, which blazes to life in a confetti of colored light. There, towering over Evanston, over the band, over fate itself:

**69**

Multicolored, incandescent, burning like a sacrament.

(SOUND): “Rico Suave” hits its chorus, a wall of sound and machismo, the dumbest song for the dumbest crime. The beat slams down like a judge’s gavel.)_

Rico stands atop the catwalk, shirt open to the waist, chest heaving, arms thrown wide to the world. He looks down at his masterpiece, then out at the empty seats—his audience of ghosts and gods.

**RICO (V.O.)**
Mission accomplished. One number. Two digits. Infinite stupidity. Rico Suave has left his mark—on the scoreboard, on the city, on the night itself.

A sudden gust whips his shirt behind him, flag-like, ridiculous and heroic. He lifts a bottle of Mountain Dew, salutes the cosmos, eyes shining with the sacred tears of a man who has done something unspeakably dumb and gotten away with it.

Below him, the stadium is lit in tacky, ridiculous holiday glory—a cosmic in-joke visible from every window for miles.

**FINAL IMAGE:**
Rico silhouetted atop the catwalk, arms up, “69” glowing behind him, a monument to every horny, idiotic, beautiful urge of youth.

A legend, crowned in sweat and Christmas lights.

---

## **THE SECURITY GUARD’S RETURN (A SUDDEN INTERRUPTION)**

**INT. STADIUM CONTROL ROOM – NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

Ancient monitors crowd the room, their dials and bulbs glowing like tired Christmas ghosts. A plate of nachos, now cemented to the desk by time and cheese, sits untouched. The room pulses with reflected neon—*“69”* flickering across every surface like a dirty Morse code.

(SOUND): Low hum, then a *beep*. A red indicator blinks awake on the master panel. Reality intrudes.)_

The guard—jolted from his infomercial coma—leans forward, eyes squinting, nose twitching, mouth going slack. He zooms in on the feed. There, on the main screen:

**Rico, arms thrown high, hips cocked, a living shrine to “69.”**

The guard’s face shifts:

**Dull fatigue.**
**Blink.**
**Stunned disbelief.**
**Blink.**
**Utter, howling annoyance.**

He snatches up his walkie-talkie, thumb mashed hard enough to leave a dent.

**SECURITY GUARD (deadpan):**
Mother of God…

*(He sighs, mutters into the static, and for the first time in his career, wonders if the night shift pays enough.)*

---

## **THE DESCENT (A HILARIOUS FALL)**

**EXT. SCOREBOARD STRUCTURE – CONTINUOUS**

From his perch, Rico glimpses movement—a pale face, a glint of polyester, doom incarnate. The guard’s silhouette is advancing. Rico’s eyes balloon. Instinct takes over.

**RICO (shouting, wild):**
Abort! ABORT! El Policia! ¡Mamá!

He whirls, tries to sprint for the catwalk, but the world has other plans. One sneaker snags a Christmas cord—Rico’s body snaps forward, airborne for an impossible, idiotic moment.

(SOUND): Drum fill, then a long, slow WHUMP as he vanishes from view.)_

(VISUAL): Slo-mo glory. Rico’s limbs pinwheel—one hand still clutching a wad of tinsel, his mouth a perfect O of panic. The Christmas lights detonate around him, a Niagara of blinking color. The scoreboard “69” pulses above, the world’s most tasteless halo.)_

He lands, face-up, flat, in a heap of foam padding and lost self-respect. The stars swim above him, the world spinning, the taste of Mountain Dew and regret sharp on his tongue.

Overhead, the scoreboard buzzes, flares, and with one final, tragic pop—dies. A tiny plume of smoke wafts up, haloed by the stadium lights.

(SOUND): From the dying speakers—one last “Rico…Suave…” sighs out, mournful and sublime.)_

**RICO (V.O.):**
Gravity. The ultimate party crasher. Turns out, gravity is a bitch.

---

## **THE APPREHENSION (A COMICAL ARREST)**

**EXT. SCOREBOARD BASE – NIGHT**

Rico lies tangled, limbs woven through a snarl of Christmas lights, blinking like a downed alien craft. He kicks at the cords, trying to look nonchalant but managing only interpretive flailing.

(SOUND): Static crackle, the heavy clomp of a bored man with authority issues and sore feet.)_

The security guard approaches—a silhouette of tired Midwestern vengeance, cuffs dangling from one meaty fist, face unmoved by spectacle or supplication. He looms over Rico, who blinks up from the floor—shirt ripped, hair frizzed, surrounded by broken bulbs and the sad remains of a Mountain Dew six-pack.

(VISUAL): Low-angle shot—the guard fills the sky, a titan made of polyester. Rico, still trying to pull himself upright, grins and winks. The guard’s eyebrow doesn’t move an inch.)_

**SECURITY GUARD (deadpan):**
You got a permit for that public art installation, son?

Rico spits out a bit of tinsel, tries to shrug in a way that says “I meant every second of this.”

**RICO (V.O.):**
Even in handcuffs, Rico Suave never loses his cool. Suave is a state of mind. Prison is just another venue.

He offers his wrists with a courtly bow. The guard snaps on the cuffs, then awkwardly hauls Rico upright—lights still knotted around his legs, extension cord trailing like the world’s worst tail.

Rico tries to strut as he’s frog-marched away, tripping on every third step, still grinning for the cameras that aren’t there.

---

## **THE MORNING AFTER (A HANGOVER AND A HEADACHE)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM PARKING LOT – MORNING**

Sunrise smears gold and regret across the parking lot. The stadium looms silent, its digital face freshly scrubbed of all sin—now blaring “Kraft Singles Family Night – Friday at 7!” in chipper, corporate pixels. Not a trace of “69” remains.

Rico is collapsed on the curb, sunglasses covering half his battered face, head drooped between his knees. Next to him: a warm bottle of Pedialyte, half-empty, worshipped like holy water. He sips, winces, sips again.

(SOUND): Birds chirp, the L-train moans in the distance, and somewhere a car stereo blares a warbled echo of “Rico Suave.” The world is bright, cruel, and so, so ordinary.)_

(VISUAL): The camera drifts up from Rico’s slumped, post-glory carcass—tank top stained, Christmas light still tangled in his shoelaces—up to the scoreboard, which could not care less.)_

**RICO (V.O.):**
They say glory fades. But hangovers? Those are immortal.

He lifts his head, adjusts his collar, and leans back—wincing, grinning, eyes already searching for the next impossible scheme.

**FINAL WIDE SHOT:**
Rico alone, tiny in the wide parking lot, surrounded by nothing but empty asphalt and the lingering taste of idiocy and legend.

(SOUND): “Rico Suave” outro buzzes, faint and triumphant, from a passing car lost in the new daylight.)_

---

## **THE PAYPHONE (A LONELY OUTPOST)**

**EXT. DYCHE STADIUM – OUTER WALL – NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

(SOUND): “Gonna Make You Sweat (Everybody Dance Now)”—that iconic piano riff and faux-orgasmic vocal—*blasts* in from the stadium, echoing off cold concrete and dying autumn grass. The night is sticky, half-lit, charged with bad decisions and static electricity.)_

Jeremy Evans, out-of-place, out-of-time, stands hunched beneath a flickering sodium lamp. The *stadium* rears behind him, monolithic, uncaring. The only outpost of civilization: a battered, grimy payphone perched on a graffiti-tagged pole, wires exposed like veins.

He digs deep in his pocket—fingers trembling, knuckles white. Quarters, dimes, a Canadian penny, maybe a button, definitely some lint. He weighs the coins, anxiety crackling.
