(VISUAL): Every detail is humiliatingly close-up: the oily, half-smeared plexiglass; Jeremy’s hands, damp and awkward; a lone neon-green bug crawling in lazy circles across the phone receiver. He flinches, shoves the bug away, then wipes his hand on his jeans, twice.)_

He takes a deep, shuddering breath. The band is off getting drunk, getting laid, getting legend. Jeremy—alone, resolute—prepares to call his wife. He could be standing on the moon for all the warmth in this night.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
Gonna make you sweat…gonna make you…dial home, explain to your wife why you sound like you’re standing outside a prison, why the payphone smells like hot piss and burnt plastic, why you miss her so much it feels like a punch.

He steps into the booth. It *closes* behind him with a click that sounds like a coffin lid. He’s in the confessional now—ready to sin, ready to beg forgiveness, ready to worship.

---

## **THE DIAL TONE (ANTICIPATION)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – CONTINUOUS**

Jeremy lifts the sticky receiver, pinches it between thumb and forefinger like a lab sample, and holds it to his ear. He can hear his own breath—short, rapid, almost panicked.

The world outside shrinks away. It’s just him, the phone, and the hard, metallic promise of regret.

He punches in the number—each *click* of the button is a minor earthquake in the booth’s cramped acoustics.

(SOUND):
- The slap of quarters into the metal slot, spinning and landing with a *clink* that’s too final.
- Each digit pressed: a sharp, metallic *pop*—every number a countdown.
- The dial tone hits: blaring, insistent, flat as a funeral bell.)_

(VISUAL):
- Jeremy’s Adam’s apple bobs with a nervous gulp.
- His wedding ring flashes, awkwardly proud, in the payphone’s jaundiced light.
- Flash cut: his wife, at home, hair falling around her face as she brushes it—soft, slow, a world away from this concrete cell.
- The coin-drop spinning, spinning—roulette for the lonely.)_

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
This is it. Moment of truth. The first phone call of married life. Please let it sound like love. Please let her laugh. Please, God, don’t let her hear what’s in my voice.

He closes his eyes, jaw clenched, the world holding its breath with him.

---

## **THE RING (AWKWARD SILENCE)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

Jeremy stands locked in the booth, shoulders hunched, knuckles blanching around the plastic receiver. Each ring feels like an accusation. Once. Twice. Three times. His breath comes shallow, sweat breaking on his upper lip. He glances around, but there is no escape—only the ugly yellow light, the stadium behind him, and the crackle of static in his ear.

(VISUAL):
- Extreme close-up on his hand, every tendon flexed and trembling.
- Sweat beads, magnified, glitter along his brow.
- His foot taps, then kicks against the payphone’s metal base in an arrhythmic, nervy beat.
- The overhead bulb flickers, buzzes—each ring growing louder, more insistent, the world pressing in.)_

(SOUND):
- The ring tone overlaps with the relentless “Gonna Make You Sweat” thumping in his head.
- The two merge, an anxious, hellish mash-up, impossible to ignore.
- Every second is a dare to hang up, to run, to stay and hope she answers.)_

Jeremy stares at the phone, eyes wide, The Fugitive praying for rescue or damnation.

---

## **THE ANSWER (THE WIFE’S VOICE)**

A *click*. A breath. Then—her voice, soft and half-awake, drifting across a thousand miles of wire and bad decisions.

**SHE THAT SHALL BE LEFT UNNAMED (V.O.)** (*groggy, surprised*)
Hello…?

Jeremy’s brain blanks. His mouth moves before he can stop it—reflex, fear, tequila. He blurts out:

**JEREMY** (too loud, too bright, way too chipper)
*Everybody dance now!*

(SOUND):
- The music in his head dies—needle-scratch, silence.
- All that remains is the distant buzz of the payphone, the echo of his own humiliation ringing in his ears.)_

(VISUAL):
- Jeremy’s face, frozen in horror, eyes wide as saucers.
- Sweat slips down his temple, slow and accusing.
- The silence on the other end stretches—cold, eternal, as if the universe itself is giving him a timeout.)_

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
Wrong song. Wrong everything. God, just hang up. Or let the ground swallow me whole.

He stares at the receiver, waiting for the verdict.

---

## **THE SMALL TALK (A DISASTER)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

Jeremy leans back against the plexiglass, its surface streaked with names, phone numbers, and crude anatomy. His hand is welded to the receiver, knuckles pale, every muscle in his body locked between flight and apology.

He tries to recover, fails, tries again. All he can muster is small talk, as if that could save him from the chasm now yawning between them.

**JEREMY**
So, uh…how was your day?

(SOUND):
- The ghost of “Everybody dance now!” loops in his brain, now sinister, taunting, a song forever ruined.
- He mouths the phrase in the reflection, lips moving with clownish precision.
- He tries a wink at his own reflection—fails, the gesture landing somewhere between desperate and deranged.
- Outside, a pigeon lands on the pavement, head cocked, judging.)_

**WIFE (V.O.)** (*soft, tired, a hint of longing*)
It was okay. I just…miss you.

Jeremy’s heart lurches. He wants to say it back—wants to say something real, something with weight. Instead, he flashes a grin no one can see, all game show host teeth and flop sweat.

**JEREMY** (*like a slogan he can’t unsay*)
Gonna make you sweat!

A beat. The silence crackles. He knows he’s lost control, but he can’t stop.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
Subtlety is for people who know what they’re doing. Timing is for people who haven’t lost their minds. I had neither. I had the booth, the song, and an ache I couldn’t even name.

---

## **THE HONEYMOON RECAP (TOO MUCH INFORMATION)**

Jeremy barrels on—desperate to steer the conversation anywhere but here, and crashing into every guardrail in sight.

**JEREMY**
Remember that time on the beach? When the umbrella blew away and you chased it—

(*he lowers his voice, but not enough*)
- in your swimsuit?

He laughs, a little too loudly. He breaks into a whispery, off-key falsetto—

**JEREMY** (*sings, shoulders shimmying, feet twitching*)
Gonna make you sweeeaaat…

The booth is now less a phone box, more a padded cell. His body bounces in time, a one-man disaster of longing and humiliation.

**WIFE (V.O.)** (*horrified, whispering*)
Jeremy! There are other people in the house!

He pauses, mouth still open, eyes wide as the night outside.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
Details. It was about the details. The way her skin looked under the sun, the way her laugh sounded, the memory of almost being naked together in public. But mostly the details. I should’ve stopped talking five sentences ago.

(VISUAL):
- The camera circles Jeremy as he pantomimes the scene: one hand shading his eyes, the other rubbing imaginary sunscreen on his arm, face lost in the memory.
- A moth, drawn to the payphone light, flutters, burns, drops dead. Jeremy watches it fall—one more casualty.)_

---

## **THE BAND UPDATE (A GROSS MISCALCULATION)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

Jeremy tries to rally, rolling his shoulders, raising his voice as if the world should hear how far he’s come. He jams a fist in his pocket, then throws his arms wide—like he’s already onstage, lights blazing, crowd roaring.

**JEREMY**
We’re playing in front of fifteen thousand people! You should see it—it’s incredible!

(SOUND):
- BOOM—“Everybody dance now!” *explodes* in his head, all subwoofer and sweat, his heart pounding like a rave.)_

(VISUAL):
- Slo-mo: Jeremy’s arms stretch to the sky, body arching in a pantomime of triumph.
- The camera pulls back—he’s alone, encased in neon filth, audience of one.
- A rat scurries past the booth, pauses to sniff the air, then disappears.)

Her voice—flat, distant, unmoved—drops through the receiver like an ax.

**WIFE (V.O.):** (*deadpan, distracted*)
That’s great, honey. But I really need to go.

The words slap him. The applause in his head dies, replaced by static and the faint hum of the street.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
I was losing her. Fast. This was a mic drop, but I was the mic—falling, tumbling, headed straight for the dumpster fire behind the stadium.

---

## **THE DESPERATE PLEA (A COMPLETE FAILURE)**

Desperation kicks in. Jeremy’s grip on the phone tightens. His voice cracks—raw, naked, no longer performing for the invisible crowd.

**JEREMY**
I miss you so much! I can’t wait to see you again! Please, just—please.

(SOUND):
- The beat in his head won’t quit. The chorus blasts back—an irresistible, humiliating compulsion.)_

He mouths the words one more time—only this time, he *means* it, full-body, hips rocking, eyes manic.

**JEREMY**
(*mouthing, thrusting, eyes pleading*)
Gonna make you sweeeat…

(VISUAL):
- Rapid zoom: Jeremy’s face, eyes wild, ring of sweat shining in the booth’s jaundiced light.
- Quick flashes: Honeymoon memories—her mismatched socks, spilled wine, a seagull dive-bombing their lunch, laughter and sunburn and love that feels very far away.)_

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
I had officially gone off script. The wrong movie, the wrong genre…And no one was yelling “cut.” Just me, the phone, the ghosts, and the beat.

---

## **THE HANG UP (A DEVASTATING BLOW)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

The silence hits with a *click*—hard, final. For a split second, Jeremy just stands there, receiver pressed to his ear, breath caught. He looks at the phone as if it’s betrayed him, as if it could explain what just happened.

(SOUND):
- The music in his head melts down: “Everybody daaaaance…” warping, stretching, breaking into static.
- The hum of the city creeps in—wind, distant siren, a world that doesn’t care.)_

(VISUAL):
- The flickering streetlight overhead gutters, flares, dies, plunging Jeremy into a colder dark.
- His hand drops the receiver. It swings in a slow, mournful arc, the sound of plastic tapping metal—a metronome for shame, a pendulum marking the seconds since he lost her.)_

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
Ouch. That hurt. Like getting ghosted with a dial tone. Like dancing alone in a club where the DJ just left.

He stands, hollowed out, the world suddenly very big.

---

## **THE REPLAY (A MOMENT OF SELF-AWARENESS)**

**EXT. PAYPHONE – NIGHT, PRE-DAWN**

Jeremy leans against the battered booth, head bowed, eyes shut. Every beat of the past ten minutes plays back—each line, each desperate plea, each hip thrust replayed in excruciating clarity.

(SOUND):
- The C+C Music Factory chorus echoes, lower, slower, becoming a dirge.
- The street is still, except for the distant growl of a garbage truck—last call for dignity.)_

(VISUAL):
- Wide shot: Jeremy is a silhouette, small and solitary, hunched in the half-light of dawn.
- The street is enormous, empty, unfeeling.
- The receiver dangles, forgotten, tapping quietly in the silence.
- No one is watching. No one will remember. Except him.)_

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
Maybe “Gonna Make You Sweat” wasn’t the best soundtrack for a romantic call. Maybe “I Just Called to Say I Love You” would’ve done it. Maybe I should’ve just kept my damn mouth shut. Maybe—just maybe—I’ll get it right next time.

The sun breaks on the horizon, pale and pitiless. Jeremy straightens, shoves his hands in his pockets, and walks into the coming day—one more fool in love, song stuck in his head, hope stuck to his heels.

---

## **THE DEJECTED WALK (A WALK OF SHAME)**

**EXT. STREET OUTSIDE DYCHE STADIUM – DAWN**

Jeremy steps out of the payphone’s shadow, shoulders folded forward, head hung low. The streetlight above him gasps, flares, and finally dies, leaving him in the blue-gray predawn.

(VISUAL):
- Slow-motion: Jeremy’s figure, getting smaller, swallowed by the empty street as the city exhales around him—delivery trucks hiss by, joggers stretch and lope past, sprinklers cough to life on brown lawns.
- Trash whirls in little eddies at his feet, wrappers and dust following in his wake.
- “Everybody dance now…” in his head, now a funeral march, dragging on in warped half-time until it finally fades out altogether.)_

Jeremy keeps walking, invisible, unseen, a ghost trailing regret and last night’s sweat.

---

## **THE REALIZATION (A HARD TRUTH)**

**EXT. PARK BENCH – NEAR STADIUM – CONTINUOUS**

He drops onto a bench, exhausted, bones buzzing with the last of the adrenaline and tequila. The world feels too big, the air too bright.

Jeremy twists his wedding ring, round and round his finger, thumb worrying the metal until his skin turns red. He stares at the cracks in the sidewalk, breath thick, every part of him aching.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
Marriage. Not just another party. Not another gig. It’s a different kind of dance—one where you can’t just follow the beat, can’t just mouth the chorus and hope she laughs. I was stepping on her toes. She felt it. I felt it.

**JEREMY (V.O.):**
The tequila wore off. The bravado wore off. All that was left was me. And all I could do was hope it was enough.

(SOUND):
- No more music. Just birdsong, the distant shush of traffic, and the weight of Jeremy’s long, rattling sigh.
- The sound of a day beginning, indifferent to his pain.)_

(VISUAL):
- WIDE: Jeremy on the bench, stadium rising behind him, the payphone a cold gray beacon in the background.
- He stares into the nothing, small and silent, a monument to every stupid, aching, beautiful thing he tried to say and failed to say.)_

**FINAL SHOT:**
Jeremy sits, unmoving, the empty daylight framing him and the payphone—a silent shrine to missed connections and necessary humility.

---

## **TITLE CARD:**

**DYCHE STADIUM. EVANSTON, ILLINOIS. THE NIGHT BEFORE THE GIG.**

(SOUND): The Prodigy’s “Firestarter” doesn’t just play—it shreds. Synths screech, bass rattles the air, adrenaline and disaster fuse in the beat. The camera whip-pans, blurry and kinetic, as each band member peels off into the night. Kathy? She’s a missile, her flight path set for impact, not escape.)_

## **THE MISSION (SELF-DESTRUCTION)**

**EXT. NORTHWESTERN CAMPUS – NIGHT – SEPTEMBER 1991**

Kathy tears across the quad, boots chewing up the pavement, jaw set, eyes wild under streaks of mascara and streetlamp glare. Her walk is less a journey than an assault—on pain, on the world, on everything that thinks it can hold her back.

She rips a packet of ibuprofen open with her teeth, tongue curling around the bitter taste as she dry-swallows three at once. Before she can think, she’s already upending a plastic bottle of malt liquor, the last two inches scalding down her throat. The burn is a dare.

**KATHY (V.O.):**
I was done negotiating with pain. If it wanted a fight, I’d give it a fucking war.

She spits, wipes her mouth with the back of her hand. Her hair is half-mad already—one lock stuck to her lips, the rest blowing everywhere like a warning sign.

**KATHY (V.O.):**
This wasn’t about fun. This was about revenge. On my insides, on the patriarchy, on anyone who thinks “quietly suffering” is a personality trait. Fuck quiet. I’m going loud.

(VISUAL):
– Jump cut: Her boots hit the sidewalk—heavy, deliberate, rhythm synced to the Prodigy’s beat.
– Jump cut: Her hand tightens around a battered flask, knuckles pale.
– Jump cut: Her hair, wild as fire, the mascara already dragging south, sweat glinting on her cheekbones.
– She walks through the dark, not away from trouble but right into its teeth.)_

She doesn’t want the party. She wants to burn it down and light a cigarette from the ashes.

---

## **THE ENTRANCE (A GRAND ARRIVAL)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – NIGHT**

(SOUND): The beat *drops*—the front door slams open like a gunshot, the room pivots. Bass throbs through the floor, bodies swaying, red cups scattered, every window fogged with sweat and sex and bad decisions.)_

Kathy steps in, instantly owning the oxygen in the room. Handheld camera work—jittery, urgent, like someone running to keep up with her velocity. The lights flicker—blue, red, then strobe, catching her in mid-step, every pause a new posture: wild, glam, invincible.

She pushes through a wall of dancers, hips swinging, shoulders squared, eyes locked on the heart of chaos. She’s not hunting anyone—she *is* the hunt.

(VISUAL):
– SLOW MOTION: As she crosses the threshold, the music distorts and warps—
“I’m the bitch you hated / Filthy, faded, educated…”
Her lip curls.
– A frat boy—generic, polo-wearing, already glazed—bumps her, sloshing cheap beer down her left boot.
– FREEZE FRAME: Her glare could stop traffic. The beer pools, sticky, on her leather.
– The whole room seems to tilt, waiting for her verdict.)_

**KATHY (V.O.):**
Wrong move, Chad.

She smiles—sharp and slow, a promise and a warning in one.

---

## **THE INTRODUCTION (A BOLD STATEMENT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – NIGHT**

Kathy forges a path through sweaty, red-faced bros locked in a doomed attempt at an ironic conga line—elbows flying, fake laughter curdling the air. She shrugs them off like furniture, heads straight for the center of gravity: the karaoke setup, where some poor soul is butchering “*Pour Some Sugar On Me*.”

She vaults the crumpled ping-pong table—boot on plastic, knee on plywood, the thing creaking in surrender. The karaoke mic? Hers now, ripped from a stunned hand mid-lyric.

**KATHY** (*shouting, voice ragged, every word a challenge*)
I’M THE FIRESTARTER! TWISTED FIRESTARTER!

Her words cut the air—metal serrated, diamond sharp. The room halts. Red Solo cups frozen mid-air, ping pong balls mid-bounce. Every head pivots. The music—still roaring, but now she’s the only rhythm that matters.

(VISUAL):
– The mic shrieks feedback as Kathy throws off her battered jacket, tossing it into the seething mass of bodies.
– She stands center stage, chin up, arms wide, a storm ready to break.)_

Frat boys blink—one tries to whistle, fails. Another mutters, “Who is this chick? And why do I want her to be my major?” A third topples a beer keg, forgotten, as the focus snaps to her.

The party? It’s not theirs anymore. It’s hers.

---

## **THE DANCE FLOOR (A WILD DISPLAY)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – DANCE FLOOR – NIGHT (LATER)**

(SOUND): The Prodigy erupts—“*Hey! Hey! Hey!*” The floor shakes, the air is thick with sweat and anticipation. Kathy hits the dance floor like she’s detonating it.)_

*(RAPID-FIRE MONTAGE):*
– Kathy, boots and all, twerking on a busted recliner, three guys gawping, one filming, none brave enough to join.
– She spins, floor sticky, beer flying from a Solo cup she’s long since stolen. The cup arcs, lands on a freshman’s head.
– She locks eyes with a stunned sophomore—he opens his mouth, she flips him off with both hands, never missing a beat.
– Windmills: boots slicing air, hair wild, lips snarled in joy.

*(CLOSE-UPS):*
– Her eyes, wild and shining, hunger burning in every reflection.
– Lipstick smeared down her chin—she wipes it off with the back of her wrist, grins wider.
– Her teeth: bared, animal, primal, a full-throated threat and invitation.

**KATHY (V.O.):**
My pain? Gone. Replaced by something raw, bigger, louder. Hedonism with a purpose. Rage with a soundtrack. Unapologetic, untouchable, mine.

(VISUAL):
– Strobe lights slice her body into fragments, each flash a new myth: punk goddess, riot starter, invincible and alone in a sea of sweating, glassy-eyed frat boys.
– The crowd isn’t dancing with her—they’re surviving her, and that’s just how she likes it.)_

---

## **THE BEER PONG TABLE (A COMPETITIVE SPIRIT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – BEER PONG ROOM – NIGHT**

The room is thick with the musk of spilled Natty Light and bravado. Bros line the table, sleeves rolled, knuckles cracked, egos radiating off them like heat haze. Red Solo cups in perfect formation—a sacrificial altar to American mediocrity.

Kathy doesn’t wait for an invitation. She barrels through the mob, shoves a couple of bros aside, plucks a ping pong ball from midair, and lines up her shot. No drama, no preamble—just muscle memory and malice.

**KATHY** (*deadpan, eyes locked on her mark*)
That one’s for *Roe v. Wade.*

She sinks it—dead center. The cup explodes with foam, the table shaking. Silence rolls across the room. One bro stares, mouth agape. Another tries to high-five her and misses by a mile.

(VISUAL):
– The camera tightens on the ball, slow motion, arc perfect, impact inevitable.
– Jumps to hyper-speed: splash, splash, splash—Kathy’s hand a blur as cup after cup vanishes, her face unreadable, the bros’ confidence sloughing off like old skin.
– Their grins turn to grimaces, bravado melting to confusion, then awe, then fear.)_

**THE FRAT TABLE (V.O.):**
She didn’t come to party. She came to *dominate*.

One bro wipes sweat from his brow, another mutters “Bro…she’s, like, really good.” The rest just stare, recalibrating their entire worldview.

---

## **THE CONVERSATIONS (A SERIES OF INAPPROPRIATE COMMENTS)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – VARIOUS LOCATIONS – NIGHT (LATER)**

Kathy’s not just making her rounds. She’s turning every conversation into a dare, every interaction into a test.

– She corners a finance major, eyes wild, breath hot with malt liquor.

**KATHY:**
I’m a firestarter, man. I burn things down.

**FRAT BOY:**
Uh…cool?
(He edges away, as if she’s holding actual matches.)

– She finds an ROTC pledge, hair buzzed, tie askew.

**KATHY:**
I once faked a psych eval just to avoid a math final. Wanna make out?

**FRAT BOY:**
I—I have a girlfriend…
(He flees, blushing so hard he nearly combusts.)

– She ambushes a philosophy major, reciting Nietzsche backwards, lips brushing his ear. He blinks, too high or too scared to call her bluff.
She laughs, deep and dirty, and moves on, leaving him in existential crisis.

(VISUAL):
– Jump cuts: Kathy’s face inches from her victims, lips twisted in a wicked grin.
– Frat boy eyes wide, hands defensive, always on their heels.
– Her triumphant, almost feral smile as she prowls from group to group—every line a threat, a joke, a confession she dares you to top.)_

**KATHY (V.O.):**
I was on a mission. To forget. To erase every thought I’d had that day, maybe a few brain cells while I was at it. Chaos was my lover tonight.

The energy crackles, building—combustible, manic, desperate. And she’s riding it all the way to the edge.

---

## **THE SHOT GLASSES (A RAPID DESCENT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – KITCHEN/DRINKING STATION – NIGHT**

A semicircle of partygoers forms, pounding on countertops, chanting her name.
**“KATHY! KATHY! KATHY!”**

She’s surrounded, gladiator-style, by red-eyed bros and mascara-smudged sorority girls. But Kathy’s not flinching—she’s performing.

She lifts a shot—down it goes. Slams the glass.  Lifts another—grins, lets the vodka burn, winks at the nearest frat bro who’s now slightly afraid.  A third. Then a fourth. Each new pour makes her hand shake a little more, but her eyes only get brighter, hungrier.

(VISUAL):
– CLOSE-UP: Shot glass hits sticky countertop, liquid ripples like a miniature explosion, droplets flying.
– The colors grow *brighter*, too bright—edges blur, lights begin to flare.
– JUMP CUT: Her face, laughing, mouth wide, head thrown back, neck veins sharp with adrenaline.
– JUMP CUT: Her hand wobbles, nearly spills the next shot, then shrugs and pours another.)_

She’s howling now, every “KATHY!” a drumbeat, every glass an invitation to disaster.

**KATHY (V.O.):**
This was the moment the pain took a back seat. And the tequila took the wheel.
A one-way ride to oblivion, and I was the only one with the gas pedal.

---

## **THE KARAOKE MACHINE (A VOCAL ASSAULT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – NIGHT (LATER)**

The karaoke corner is under siege. Kathy storms up, rips the mic from a dude mid–“*Tiny Dancer*,” scrolls past every safe choice, and slams her thumb on “*Firestarter*.”

(VISUAL):
– She leaps onto the coffee table, crowd parting—suddenly there are cameras out, grins, gasps.
– Strobe lights fracture her into flickering myth—every pose a painting.
– The crowd shrinks away as she *screams* into the mic, not singing but summoning something raw and loud and impossible to ignore.)_

She’s off-key, but nobody can look away. Her presence fills the room—cheekbones sharp, eyes wild, teeth bared, a punk goddess in ripped jeans and combat boots.

**KATHY (V.O.):**
Pitch? Irrelevant. Presence? Nuclear.

**KATHY** (*howling, off-key, alive*)
***I’M THE BITCH YOU HATED—FILTH INFATUATED!***

A bro, mid-sip, lets his cup fall—red plastic spinning, beer splattering the floor.
The crowd recoils, then pushes forward, energy rising. Someone yells “FUCK YES!”  Someone else whispers, “Should we…do something?”

**THE CROWD (V.O.):**
We didn’t know whether to cheer…or call campus security.

But for one wild, blaring moment, Kathy is everything the room wanted—and everything it feared.

---

## **THE NEAR-NAKED RUN (A MOMENT OF MADNESS)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – VARIOUS ROOMS – NIGHT**

The house is a minefield of bodies, booze, and bad ideas, but Kathy is past caring. She explodes from a bedroom, Delta Gamma flag snatched off the wall and wrapped around her like a toga gone wrong. Boots still on, nothing else above the waist.

She’s *howling*—wordless, triumphant, gleefully obscene.

(SOUND): The “Firestarter” bass drops into a distorted, echoing monster—every pulse a heartbeat, every echo a dare.)_

(VISUAL):
– Shaky cam follows Kathy at top speed, bare skin flashing under red and white, strobe lights snapping at her like paparazzi.
– She barrels down the hall, a streak of reckless color—one guy freezes, bong halfway to his lips, mouth hanging open.
– Another, stunned, chokes out, “IS SHE—?”
– Heads spin, necks crane, jaws drop. Nobody moves fast enough to stop her, and a few don’t even want to.)_

**THE FRAT BOYS (V.O.):**
We were stunned. We were confused. We were also—let’s be honest—kind of impressed.

Kathy rounds a corner, the flag flying, wild laughter bouncing down the hall.

---

## **THE CRASH LANDING (A COMICAL FALL)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

Still flying, topless but crowned in the Delta Gamma flag, Kathy hits the corner at a dead sprint—bare skin gleaming, boots pounding, adrenaline roaring in her ears. She slips—a smear of spilled beer and the shattered remains of six Solo cups send her airborne.

(VISUAL):
– Slow-motion glory: Kathy’s arms flail, face lit by strobes and warped by a fisheye lens, the room tilting around her.
– The Delta Gamma flag flaps like a superhero cape, her body stretched out, gravity the only thing moving faster than she is.)_

She crashes into a beanbag, the air whooshing out in a cartoonish *WHOOOMP*. Legs stick up, arms windmill, flag fluttering down like the curtain call on the world’s wildest act.

The flag drapes over her again, landing perfectly—a final, comic flourish. The crowd gasps, then erupts in chaotic applause, laughter, shouts, and a couple of panicked shrieks.

**KATHY (V.O., deadpan):**
I stuck the landing. Mostly.

---

## **THE MORNING AFTER (A HANGOVER AND A MYSTERY)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – MORNING**

Sunlight knifes through greasy windows. The world’s spinning. The couch smells like spilled beer and defeat. Kathy’s face—mascara streaked, lips swollen, pillow-creased—emerges from the cushions, eyes slitted against the pain.

A half-eaten corn dog nestles by her cheek, mustard dried and accusing. Her hair’s an epic disaster, feathers of tinsel clinging from nowhere. Every cell in her body vibrates with headache and humiliation.

(SOUND): The sad percussion of beer cans rolling, someone snoring like a chainsaw, a phone buzzing against linoleum.)_

She blinks, tries to take stock. The landscape is pure disaster:
– A frat boy curled in fetal position on the armrest, thumb in mouth.
– Another half-out, half-in the open fridge, clutching a bottle of ranch like a plush toy.
– Crushed Solo cups underfoot, flagons of ranch and ketchup like medieval relics.

**KATHY (V.O.):**
What the hell happened last night?

Her head throbs. Her tongue tastes like cigarettes and something that used to be meat. She can feel her liver actively plotting revenge.

**KATHY (V.O.):**
Everything hurt. My head. My pride. My liver was typing up its resignation letter.

She rolls upright, one eye still squinted shut, and surveys the wreckage. Whatever happened, she *won*. She survived. But she may never be clean again.

---

## **THE ESCAPE (A HASTY RETREAT)**

**EXT. FRAT HOUSE – FRONT LAWN – MORNING**

Wrapped in the battered Delta Gamma flag—now speckled with beer, grass stains, and regret—Kathy staggers across the dewy lawn. Her boots leave imprints in mud. Her dignity trails somewhere out of sight.

The world is up and moving:
– Joggers on the sidewalk, eyebrows shooting up.
– Freshmen in backpacks, rubbernecking as they part in awe and fear.
– A frat bro waves from a window, face still painted from last night. She flips him off over her shoulder, doesn’t even look back.

(VISUAL):
– Long tracking shot: The flag—her battle cape—drags behind her, the wind picking it up like the last act of rebellion.
– Wide shot: Kathy, a lone, hungover goddess, limping down the block, the frat house silhouetted behind her—a fortress battered by her wake.)_

(SOUND): “Firestarter” has faded. Only birdsong, sprinklers, the hiss of morning traffic, and Kathy’s low, half-growled groan as she disappears into the day.)_

**FINAL IMAGE:**
Kathy vanishing around the corner, flag flapping, legend made flesh—beaten, but not bowed.

---

## **THE PHONE BOOTH (A SHRINE TO LONELINESS)**

**EXT. STREET CORNER NEAR STADIUM – NIGHT**

Bill’s silhouette is carved out by the blood-red neon of the “OPEN 24 HOURS” sign—a relic of American insomnia. The booth is a ruin: glass fogged with grime, metal corroded, one side patched with gray duct tape that flaps in the wind like a warning.

He’s alone, coat collar turned up, the night wind hissing like it wants his secrets. In his palm: a roll of quarters fat enough to buy redemption—or just more regret. He thumbs the coins, cocky, knuckles scarred from old bar fights and new mistakes.

(SOUND): Stevie Ray Vaughan’s “Voodoo Chile” rips in—guitar snaking through the air, a slither of threat, feedback screaming into the dark.)_

**BILL (V.O.):**
Well, I stand up next to a mountain…and I chop it down with the edge of my hand…
Yeah, my mountain of loneliness. My hand…my phone.
Let’s dial some demons, shall we?

He grins at the glass, sees his own wreckage staring back. This isn’t nostalgia—it’s exorcism.

---

## **THE FIRST CALL (A BAD IDEA)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

Bill steps in, shuts the door—almost—just enough to be alone with the static. He spins the dial with bravado, index finger cocked like a trigger. The world shrinks to this booth, this moment, this gamble.

He leans in—one elbow up, eyes sharp, grin mean. Every dial tone’s a spin of the wheel; every ring is hope you know you shouldn’t have.

*(SPLIT SCREEN MONTAGE):*
– *An answering machine: “Hi! You’ve reached Becky and I’m not—”*
*Click. He hangs up.*
– *A woman in a nightgown, her voice shredded by sleep: “It’s 1:45 in the goddamn morning.”*
*He flinches, laughs, dials again.*
– *A guy answers, rough-edged: “She moved out, man. Months ago.”*
*Bill sighs, pinches the bridge of his nose, keeps going.*

(VISUAL):
– His face, blurred and warping behind greasy glass.
– The camera spins dizzy as he dials—faster, more desperate, each time his swagger eroding.
– The neon outside flares and buzzes, sickly, casting him in bad pink light—a sinner in confession.)_

**BILL (V.O.):**
First call was a disaster. But you don’t climb a mountain without slipping on a few ex-girlfriends.

**BILL (V.O.):**
I had a list. A glorious, stupid list. Half of them wouldn’t remember me. The other half would wish they didn’t.

He pops another quarter. He’s only getting started.

---

## **THE HANG UP (A BRUTAL REJECTION)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

He’s mid-sentence—voice trembling between hope and swagger—when the sound *cuts*. Not a word, not a sigh. Just a flat, merciless *click*. Silence expands, cold and total.

(VISUAL):
– EXTREME CLOSE-UP: The receiver on the other end SLAMS into its cradle—plastic on plastic, sharp as a slap.
– HARD CUT to Bill’s face—frozen, lips parted, eyes wide. He holds the receiver to his ear, waiting for forgiveness that won’t come.
– The buzz of the dead line surges, fills the booth. The world contracts to static, his reflection, his mistake.)_

Outside, the “24 HOURS” neon sign flickers, sputters—then dies, leaving Bill in the dark. The wind rattles the duct tape on the door. The night’s suddenly colder.

**BILL (V.O.):**
She hung up so fast, I could still hear the echo of my own dignity hitting the floor.

He stands there a beat longer—like a boxer after the knockout, waiting for the ref to call it.

---

## **THE SECOND CALL (A HIGH SCHOOL SWEETHEART)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT (LATER)**

He exhales hard—sags, then stiffens his spine. This time he dials slow, knuckle by knuckle. Hope’s a dying animal in his chest, but it’s still fighting.

RING.
RING.
CLICK.

A woman answers—voice older, softer, worn by years but still unmistakable.

**VOICE 2 (V.O.):**
Hello?

Bill straightens, tries to sound smooth—tries to channel Stevie Ray, but it comes out crooked.

**BILL** (*half-sings, half-jokes, voice rough*)
And I chop it down…with the edge of my hand…

A pause. Then a long inhale—her, weighing memory, weighing regret.

**VOICE 2 (V.O.):**
Bill? Is that you? It’s been…years. I’m married now. With two kids.

He closes his eyes. Damn. He forgot about the “married with kids” thing. Forgot about her husband being a cop. Forgot how badly nostalgia could sting.

(VISUAL):
– Flashback montage:
– Prom night, cheap corsage and cheaper liquor.
– His tux, flask bulging in the pocket.
– Awkward, slow-motion dance—her head on his shoulder, him humming the guitar solo, both too young for all of it.
– Snap back to present: Bill gripping the phone, eyes twitching, lips pressed tight, the booth starting to feel too small for his regret.)_

**BILL (V.O.):**
This was a bad idea. A mountain I should’ve left un-chopped.

He hangs on, waiting for her to say something more—but the line stays cold, and the future’s already spoken for.

---

## **THE THIRD CALL (A WRONG NUMBER)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT (LATER STILL)**

Bill wipes sweat from his brow with a sleeve gone greasy in the neon’s red wash. The quarters feel heavier now, each coin a lottery ticket for humiliation. He dials, riffing like a man who thinks jokes might save him.

RING. RING.

**GRUFF MALE VOICE (V.O.):**
Yeah?

Bill launches, voice slurred with bravado and dread:

**BILL**
Well, I pick up all the pieces…and make an island…

**GRUFF MALE VOICE (V.O.):**
Wrong number, you idiot!

Silence. Bill’s mouth snaps shut, eyes narrowing in the glare. That’s it—no apology, no punchline. Just dial tone and existential smackdown.

(VISUAL):
– Close-up: Bill’s face caught in the harsh fluorescence, a cartoon of misery—eyebrows twitching, lips twisted in defeat.
– Smash cut: Black screen, red flashing text—“DO YOU EVEN KNOW WHO YOU’RE CALLING?”—the universe itself heckling him.)_

**BILL (V.O.):**
My island of loneliness was starting to look more like a deserted rock. No coconuts. No volleyball. Just shame.

He presses the receiver to his temple, not hard enough to hurt, but just enough to know he’s still real.

---

## **THE FOURTH CALL (A DISCONNECTED LINE)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – MOMENTS LATER**

His hands are shaking now—tired, numb, still moving. He dials, dials, dials—one last shot at the past.

Nothing.

A hollow, mechanical voice:

**RECORDED MESSAGE (V.O.):**
We’re sorry. The number you have dialed has been disconnected.

(VISUAL):
– Camera pushes fast into Bill’s face: blank, drained, every hope wrung out and left to dry.
– Extreme close-up on the coin return: a single quarter ejects, spinning out and clanging against the metal tray—a sound that rings with pure disdain.)_

He palms the quarter, stares at it like it’s a cruel joke.

**BILL (V.O.):**
She changed her number. Changed her life. Left my ass back in ’88 with a mixtape and a boner.

He laughs, a brittle sound, and pockets the coin.

---

## **THE FIFTH CALL (A CONFUSED GRANDMOTHER)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT (STILL LATER)**

Bill slouches so deep in the booth he’s practically horizontal, the glass fogging with his breath. His hands dial automatically—no checking, just muscle memory and exhaustion.

RING. RING.

A frail voice, quavering and hopeful:

**GRANDMOTHER (V.O.):**
Hello? Who is this? Is this my grandson, BILLY?

He stares at the receiver, lips moving, brain stuck somewhere between Stevie Ray and self-loathing:

**BILL**
Might even raise a little sand…

There’s a pause—her confusion like static. Bill closes his eyes, lets it ride.

**BILL (V.O.):**
Close enough.

(VISUAL):
– Tight shot on the receiver, slowly spinning in his hand, the phone cord curled around his knuckles like regret.
– Insert: An elderly woman in a floral nightgown, doilies everywhere, squinting at her rotary phone like it might be a hand grenade.)_

Bill doesn’t hang up. Just listens to her breathing for a beat, lets the ache settle in.

---

## **THE SIXTH CALL (A POLICE OFFICER)**

**INT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – MOMENTS LATER**

No self-respect left. Bill dials again—numbers he barely recognizes, hands trembling, eyes glassy and red. The booth’s light hums, threatening to blow.

CLICK. RING.

**POLICE OFFICER (V.O.):**
Evanston Police Department, what is your emergency?

Bill mumbles, voice hoarse:

**BILL**
’Cause I’m a voodoo chile…

There’s a pause—a universe of bad choices in a single breath.

**BILL (V.O.):**
My emergency? My complete and utter failure to connect with another human being.

He stares up at the buzzing fluorescent tube—willing it to explode, to end him, to answer *something*.

(VISUAL):
– The bulb buzzes louder, Bill’s shadow twitching on the booth wall.
– QUICK FLASHBACK:
– Every failed call in quick-cut:
– Slammed receivers
– Angry exes
– Wrong numbers
– The quarter spinning back
– Grandma’s confusion
– The cop’s professional boredom
– Cut together like a boxing KO reel—every ring a hit, every “hello?” a knockout blow.)_

His head drops. All he’s got left is quarters and old lyrics.

---

## **THE HANG UP (A HASTY RETREAT)**

**EXT. PAYPHONE BOOTH – NIGHT**

The syllables “Evanston Police Department” drop into Bill’s brain like a piano through a plate glass window. For half a second, he’s a cartoon—eyes bugging, sweat flying, heart in his throat.

Then—*BANG!*—the receiver crashes into the cradle, a plastic death knell. Bill’s legs unspool beneath him and he’s off—staggering into the sodium glare, arms pumping, one sneaker untied, jacket flapping behind him like a fugitive cape.

(VISUAL):
– FAST-MOTION wide shot: Bill tearing down the empty street, neon sign flickering behind him, the booth buzzing and sparking like a short-circuited confession box.
– DUTCH ANGLE: His shoes slap the pavement, one lace trailing, every step another “get me the fuck out of here.”
– JUMP CUT: The booth, abandoned, neon dying, already turning into a ghost story.)_

---

## **THE EMPTY POCKETS (A FINANCIAL DISASTER)**

**EXT. SIDEWALK – MOMENTS LATER**

Bill careens to a halt, chest heaving, adrenaline crackling through the haze. He digs in his pockets—left, right, inside out. Nothing. No quarters, no dignity, not even a sticky breath mint.

(VISUAL):
– EXTREME CLOSE-UP: His hands turn out empty pockets, little white flags flapping in the night breeze.
– A lone quarter rolls from his palm, arcs in slow motion, vanishes into a sidewalk crack—one last betrayal.)_

**BILL (V.O.):**
Spent all my quarters, spent all my dignity. Guess we’re even now.

He sags, the night swallowing him whole. Somewhere, a payphone rings for no one.

**BILL (V.O.):**
Note to self: never chase love through payphones. They only return change, not feelings.

He looks up—no one is coming, no one is calling back.

**BILL (V.O.):**
My island was now completely devoid of resources. Just me, the dark, and a lesson I’d need to forget to survive.

---

## **THE DEJECTED WALK (A WALK OF SHAME)**

**EXT. EVANSTON STREETS – EARLY MORNING**

Bill limps back through Evanston’s awakening streets, boots dragging, every step a confession. Neon lights flicker out behind him, the city’s afterparty dissolving in cold blue dawn.

(VISUAL):
– Slow-motion tracking: Bill, hunched and hollow, moves past shuttered stores and glowing diner signs.
– INSERT: A jogger, fresh and full of purpose, slows to stare at him with the exact kind of suburban judgment Bill’s always drawn—like he’s a species on the verge of extinction.
– CLOSE-UP: His hair’s a matted wreck, eyes sunken, shirt half-untucked, one sleeve damp and sticky from a puddle or a night he’s not sure he survived.)_

(SOUND):
– Stevie Ray’s “Voodoo Chile” barely limps along—guitar slurred, slowed, warped like a cassette left on a dashboard in July, then trailing off into nothing but the scrape of Bill’s boots on the curb.)_

He’s a silhouette—shadow shrinking, pride deflated, nothing left but what he can carry home.

---

## **THE REALIZATION (A HARD TRUTH)**

**EXT. PARK BENCH NEAR DYCHE STADIUM – MOMENTS LATER**

He drops onto the cold metal bench, the weight of every bad idea settling in his bones. The stadium rears up in the distance, vast and unfeeling—unimpressed by anything he did, or failed to do.

He looks at his hands, at his empty pockets, at the sun crawling up behind the stone walls.

**BILL (V.O.):**
Maybe “Voodoo Chile” wasn’t the right theme for a night of desperate phone calls.  Should’ve picked “*The Sound of Silence*.” Or “*Don't Stop Believin'*.” Or maybe just let the city sing me out.

He exhales—long, heavy, the sigh of a man who finally knows what he is.

**BILL (V.O.):**
I came to conquer hearts. All I conquered was a payphone, a hangover, and my own sorry pride.

(SOUND):
– The blues fade out. Nothing but birds, the whisper of leaves, the pulse of morning traffic somewhere far away.)_

(VISUAL):
– WIDE: Bill is tiny, slumped on the bench, the world stretching huge and empty around him.
– The camera drifts back, the street swallowing him, until he’s just another ghost at sunrise—out of luck, out of quarters, and out of delusions.)_

**End of Bill’s night—beaten, but finally honest.**

---

## **THE SEARCH (A DESPERATE QUEST)**

**EXT. EVANSTON STREETS – NIGHT**

Jim barrels down the sidewalk, a missile in Chuck Taylors, eyes so wild he’s scaring off pigeons and freshmen with every stride. He swings past a pack of undergrads stumbling out of Chipotle, breathless and manic, grabbing the nearest one by the hoodie.

**JIM** (*panting, deranged*)
Have you seen the Sandman? He owes me a shot of Jaeger!

(VISUAL):
– The camera spins dizzy 360 around Jim, the world a blur of neon, headlights, startled faces.
– Random flash edits: Student faces—confused, entertained, a little scared.
– A rave poster tears free from a telephone pole, floats past. Jim sees it, *chases* it, full sprint, like it’s his ticket to Narnia.
– The riff from “Enter Sandman” claws through the air, metallic and mean, soundtrack to his breakdown.)_

**JIM (V.O.):**
Hush little baby, don’t say a word…Mama’s gonna buy you a mockingbird…and Daddy’s gonna spike it with Everclear.

**JIM (V.O.):**
I wasn’t just looking for a party. I was hunting it. Like it was Bigfoot. And I was armed with nothing but a liver and a bad idea.

---

## **THE FALSE LEADS (A SERIES OF DEAD ENDS)**

**MONTAGE – VARIOUS LOCATIONS**

**EXT. LIBRARY – NIGHT**
Jim slams fists on the library doors, breath fogging the glass. A lone librarian looks up from her desk, unimpressed, dead-eyed.

**JIM**
Where’s the bass drop, Dewey!?

She stares. He flips her off, moves on.

**INT. COFFEE SHOP – NIGHT**
Jim busts through the door, head swiveling, searching for a pulse. People look up—half reading, half dying inside. Jazz croons from a speaker. Jim sniffs, makes a face.

**JIM** (*disgusted*)
Smells like decaf and disappointment.

Barista shrugs. Nobody looks up. He’s invisible, or worse—just another late-night lost soul.

**EXT. DESERTED PARK – NIGHT**
He staggers into the playground, spins around the swings, eyes darting for any sign of life. A raccoon ambles away under the jungle gym.

**JIM**
Even you left the party!?

He drops onto a see-saw, legs splayed, staring up at the empty sky.

(VISUAL):
– Harsh, jarring cuts: Jim’s face wild, the echoing emptiness of each space.
– The lights get colder, more alien. The riff from “Enter Sandman” slows, distorts, looping on itself as Jim’s hope frays.
– Jim spins in place, world a kaleidoscope of neon and despair, his grin fading into a snarl.)_

**JIM (V.O.):**
Every door was a disappointment. Every closed sign, a personal insult.
But I wasn’t stopping. Not until I found that sandman—and punched him in the face with a beer bong.

---

## **THE FRAT HOUSE (A GLIMMER OF HOPE)**

**EXT. FRAT HOUSE – NIGHT**

He stops dead, skids on the curb—heartbeat synced to the thump of subwoofers inside. The windows bleed colored light. Someone howls. Someone pukes in the bushes. Jim’s whole body vibrates: this is it, the mythic beacon, the church of poor decisions.

He peers through the door: Kathy, whirling in the storm, sweat-slick and unbreakable, eyes wild, a goddess in boots and stolen flags. For a split second, their gazes lock. Her nod is subtle but unmistakable—*bring the chaos.*

**JIM (V.O.):**
And if that mockingbird don’t sing…Mama’s gonna buy you a diamond ring…
And that ring? It was forged in the fires of keg-fueled debauchery.  A diamond ring of pure, unadulterated party.

(VISUAL):
– Dolly zoom in: Jim’s world narrows to the open door, lights pulsing in his veins.
– Flashes: Stumbling students, flying drinks, Kathy spinning, her nod.
– The promise: inside is purpose, communion, and trouble.)_

He grins—a predator at the gates of Eden.

---

## **THE CRASHING (A GRAND ENTRANCE)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – CONTINUOUS**

He doesn’t enter—he *invades*. The door slams open, Jim striding in like a conquering hero, arms flung wide. The crowd parts, startled, as if a riot walked through their living room.

He bellows, voice cracking over the pounding beat:

**JIM**
ENTER SANDMAN!

(VISUAL):
– Slow-motion: Beer erupts into the air as Jim *leaps* onto the couch, limbs windmilling, grin stretched to manic extremes.
– The bass drops—“Enter Sandman” explodes, the room buckles.
– Students roar, someone shrieks, another surrenders a beer to Jim without hesitation, as if tribute to the night’s new god.
– A funnel appears, as if conjured. Jim grabs it, a priest accepting the sacrament.)_

**JIM (V.O.):**
I didn’t knock. I didn’t ask. I didn’t care.  The sandman had arrived—and he brought hell with him.

In that moment, chaos is king, and Jim’s crown is made of foam, sweat, and noise.

---

## **THE DANCING (A WILD DISPLAY)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – NIGHT**

Jim takes the dance floor like a tornado. His moves are part windmill, part epileptic seizure, and all raw kinetic energy. He flails—elbows out, knees high, hips working against the beat like he’s fighting off invisible demons.

(VISUAL):
– Jump cuts: Beer spraying across the lens as Jim spins through a haze of fog and laser lights.
– CLOSE-UP: Jim clips a stereo speaker with his shoulder, knocking it off its perch—music warbles, crowd screams, Jim never stops moving.
– DISTORTED ANGLE: A girl screeches as her vodka cranberry explodes from her hand, red liquid flying like arterial spray.)_

**THE FRAT BOYS (V.O., collectively):**
Who invited this guy?

He grins, sweat streaming down his face.

**JIM (V.O.):**
My moves? Unholy.  My rhythm? Nonexistent.  My impact? Devastating.

He is *the* party’s natural disaster.

---

## **THE BEER PONG (A COMPETITIVE SPIRIT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – KITCHEN – MOMENTS LATER**

Jim leans over the beer pong table, knuckles white on the edge, body weaving like a boxer between rounds. The room hushes—frat boys and party girls, everyone watching, bets whispered.

**JIM** (*wild-eyed, challenging*)
Next. I got this. I’m a goddamn sandman.

He grabs a ping pong ball, winds up like he’s throwing the final pitch of the World Series—and hurls it with all his might…

…straight into a potted fern on the windowsill.

A frat bro takes one in the forehead, blinks, and drops his cup.  The table wobbles, Red Solo cups go airborne, cheap beer floods the floor.

(VISUAL):
– SLOW-MOTION: Ping pong ball arcing into the plant.
– Wide: Cups flying, partygoers ducking, Jim grinning like a champion in a war zone.
– Groans and boos as frat boys look at each other, equal parts horror and admiration.)_

**JIM (V.O.):**
Exit light…enter night…take my hand…we’re off to never-never land…
…and maybe a few minor concussions.

Jim raises his arms. In some twisted universe, he *won*.

---

## **THE CONVERSATIONS (A SERIES OF BIZARRE ENCOUNTERS)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – VARIOUS LOCATIONS – NIGHT**

Jim haunts the party, bouncing from group to group like a poltergeist nobody invited. His eyes are wild, his grin too wide, his energy radioactive and contagious—for better or worse.

**JIM** (*grabbing a frat guy’s shoulders, breath hot, eyes wild*)
Have you seen the Sandman? He’s got the good stuff. The *real* stuff.

The frat bro pulls away, a mix of terror and pity on his face.

**FRAT BOY**
Dude, are you okay? Like…medically?

Jim laughs—too loud, too long, slapping the guy’s back like they’re war buddies in a foxhole.

(VISUAL):
– Tight close-ups: Partygoers’ faces caught between horror and fascination.
– Fisheye lens: Jim’s sweat-soaked, manic face fills the frame, eyes huge and pupils blown, the world swirling behind him.
– Beer tap hisses, foam spewing—pressure building, party tipping toward bedlam.)_

**JIM (V.O.):**
Never-never land…it was starting to look a lot like this party.  Except louder. And somehow stickier.

---

## **THE MISTAKEN IDENTITY (A COMICAL CASE OF WRONG PERSON)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – STAIRCASE LANDING – LATER**

Jim stumbles up the stairs, spots a girl from behind—dark hair, combat boots, tough swagger. That’s enough. In Jim’s world, that’s Kathy, no question.

He lurches up, voice ragged and off-key, singing the opening lines of “Enter Sandman” like it’s Shakespeare.

**JIM** (*crooning, earnest, totally gone*)
Hush little baby, don’t you cry…

She turns, eyes wide, confusion instantly turning to alarm.

**GIRL**
I…I don’t know you.

Jim freezes, halfway between serenade and collapse.
He tries to offer her a handful of beer-soaked confetti, palm dripping, smile trembling.

(VISUAL):
– Freeze frame: Her face, a perfect cocktail of confusion and “help me.”
– Jim, arm out, confetti drooping, blinking hard as reality snaps back.
– Dolly zoom: Jim’s POV, world stretching, music slowing, realization settling like a hangover migraine.)_

**JIM (V.O.):**
Turns out, serenades don’t work as well when you’re leaking rum and misidentifying strangers.

He staggers away, the wrong girl’s perfume haunting him, the right song wasted on the wrong universe.

---

## **THE STAGE DIVE (A DISASTROUS ATTEMPT)**

**INT. FRAT HOUSE – LIVING ROOM – NIGHT**

Jim sees the DJ table—a wobbly Ikea altar stacked with turntables and beer cans—and in his mind, it’s the main stage at Donington. He climbs up, all swagger and fever, arms wide like a prophet before the rapture.

**JIM** (*bellowing, triumphant*)
ENTER NIGHT!!

He leaps—drunk, airborne, believing for one glorious second that gravity is just a suggestion.

No one looks up.  He crashes to the beer-glazed tile with a *THWUMP*, the impact ringing through his bones and echoing through the battered sound system.

**JIM (V.O.):**
We’re off to never-never land…And by “never-never land,” I mean the floor. It smelled like nacho cheese and broken dreams.

(VISUAL):
– SLOW-MO: Jim’s limbs windmilling, face frozen in shock, floor rushing up like destiny.
– SMASH CUT: The impact, reverb dialed to eleven—bottles clattering, music skipping, someone yelling “Jesus Christ!”
– Cutaway: A stoner on the couch, unmoved, lifts his thumb in slow, baked approval.)_

---

## **THE EJECTION (A HASTY EXIT)**

**EXT. FRAT HOUSE – FRONT LAWN – MOMENTS LATER**

Jim’s forcibly escorted—lifted like a sandbag by two mutant frat boys, arms under his pits, shoes barely skimming the porch rail.

**FRAT BOY #1**
You’re done, Metallica.

**FRAT BOY #2**
Go mosh with the bushes.

They launch him off the porch—grassy exile, his final encore. He lands flat, blinking up at a sky gone sideways, lungs full of damp, dewy oxygen and whatever the hell just happened.

**JIM (V.O.):**
Exit light…stage right…via flight.

(VISUAL):
– WIDE, LOW-ANGLE: Jim, crumpled in the grass, steam curling off his body like the ghost of a better party.
– The frat house behind him, lit up like Valhalla, all color and noise—his temple, his Mecca, now forever closed to him.)_

He lies there, not moving, letting the world spin. The grass is cold, but merciful.

---

## **THE WALK OF SHAME (A STUMBLE BACK TO REALITY)**

**EXT. EVANSTON STREET – EARLY MORNING**

Jim limps down the broken sidewalk, one shoe missing, party hat drooping like a wilted crown. His shirt’s stained with guacamole, his jeans ripped at the knee, and his left eye is ringed in someone else’s mascara.

(VISUAL):
– Slow-motion: Jim staggers, the world a slow-tilt carousel—streetlights flicker, colors too bright, trash fluttering around his ankles like mourning crepe.
– Joggers breeze past, judgment in their eyes and speed in their stride.
– Jim lifts a limp wave at a trash can, slurring “Hey, buddy,” before realizing he’s saluting his own reflection in a puddle.)_

(SOUND):
– The last, warped chords of “Enter Sandman” fade into the ache behind his temples, each drumbeat an echo of last night’s mistakes.)_

He’s alone, but the city bears silent witness.

---

## **THE REALIZATION (A HARD TRUTH)**

**EXT. PARK BENCH NEAR DYCHE STADIUM – MINUTES LATER**

Jim collapses on a cold metal bench, body crumpling like a marionette with snapped strings. The stadium rises behind him, huge and silent—a temple of order looming over last night’s entropy.

He stares at his hands, still dusted with glitter and cheese—souvenirs from a night he’ll never fully remember and can’t quite forget.

His eyes widen, bloodshot, as shame and memory collide.

**JIM (V.O.):**
Enter sandman…enter hangover…exit dignity.

(SOUND):
– Silence, then the city’s true morning: birds chirping, L train echo, the hum of life returning.
– Jim’s breath, long and slow—a sigh carrying all the sins of a vanished night.)_

(VISUAL):
– WIDE SHOT: Jim tiny, hunched on the bench, stadium huge in the background.
– A squirrel scurries by, giving Jim a wide berth—nature’s last insult.)_

He doesn’t move. Just lets the morning wash over him. He’s spent—emptied out, but finally honest.

---

## **CREMEANS' SUPERMAN (THE RESPONSIBLE EDITION)**

**(SOUND):** R.E.M.'s “Superman” twangs into life, that perfect blend of dorky and heroic, as chaos erupts everywhere *except* here.)

**(VISUAL):**
Everything moves with time-lapse precision. The camera never wobbles. No fish-eye, no slo-mo—just good, honest competence.

---

## **THE CHECK-IN (A LOGISTICAL TRIUMPH)**

**INT. HOTEL LOBBY – NIGHT**

Cremeans marches into the lobby, clipboard swinging, messenger bag thumping against his hip. While the rest of the band is off doing body shots and vandalizing university property, he’s *winning* at adulthood.

(VISUAL):
– The camera holds steady, eye-level, as he smooths his paperwork on the marble counter, aligning it perfectly with the desk’s edge.
– The clerk glances up, almost impressed, as if sensing he’s dealing with a higher life form.
– Cut to: two room keys—laid out with surgical symmetry. Cremeans nods, satisfied, as “I am Superman” drifts through his mind, bright and triumphant.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
I am Superman…and I know that I can do anything…

Hotel check-in. The first line of defense against rock and roll chaos. I was the sandbag holding back a flood of bourbon and bad decisions.

---

## **THE ROOM INSPECTION (A THOROUGH EXAMINATION)**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – MOMENTS LATER**

Cremeans enters with the wary precision of a bomb squad tech. He scans for stains. Checks the AC, the mini-fridge, the status of the little soap bars. He inspects the bathroom like a detective at a crime scene.

(VISUAL):
– CLOSE-UP: Cremeans turns on the shower—waits, tests the temp, nods at the robust pressure.
– SLOW ZOOM: His face, calm, collected, illuminated by righteous fluorescent light.
– He lifts a towel, unfurls it, fingers the terry cloth, sniffs. Softness: 7/10. Fold: must improve. He refolds it with hospital corners.
– Swipes a Lysol wipe over the light switch. Just in case.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
You can’t manage chaos if you sleep in squalor.  This bedspread’s seen some things. But not tonight. Not on my watch.

---

## **THE BED ASSIGNMENTS (A STRATEGIC DECISION)**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – NIGHT**

Cremeans sits at the desk—legal pad out, calculator clicking, a pencil jammed between his teeth. The band is out fracturing reality; Cremeans is drawing battle lines.

(VISUAL):
– Top-down: His notepad covered in careful diagrams—Room A, Room B, columns of names, arrows and X’s.
– Close-up: Notations in tiny, precise handwriting:
 - “JEFF: window side (snoring mitigation)”
 - “KATHY: bathroom proximity (pain management)”
 - “JIM: farthest from minibar (disaster prevention)”
 - “GILLEY: NOT THE BATHTUB. Underlined three times.”
– He stares at the finished matrix, nods—mission accomplished.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
*I am Superman and I know what’s happening.*

Someone had to be the adult. Someone had to make sure Gilley didn’t sleep in the tub again.

---

## **THE PREPARATION (A METICULOUS ROUTINE)**

**INT. HOTEL BATHROOM & BEDROOM – NIGHT**

Bedtime for Cremeans is a ritual—sacred, unbroken, precise. While the city howls, he’s building a fortress of routine.

(VISUAL):
– Time-lapse: Toothbrush scrubs. Face lathers. Floss zigzags. Gargle, spit.
– Socks folded edge to edge, slippers lined up like runway lights under the bed.
– Alarm clock set for 7:00 A.M.—*then* a backup wristwatch alarm, checked and double-checked.
– Eye mask unfurled, pager charger coiled neatly. The itinerary—typed, printed, tucked beneath the glass of water on the nightstand.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
*Trust me when I say I know the pathway to your heart.*

Let them rage and party and puke in stereo.  I’d be up with the sun—and the itinerary.

He slips under the sheets with the exhausted serenity of a monk. While the others chase chaos, Cremeans is *ready*.

---
## **THE PHONE CALL (A BRIEF CHECK-IN)**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – NIGHT**

Cremeans sits upright, feet flat on the carpet, phone cradled between ear and shoulder. He glances at his clipboard, reciting statistics with the calm of a man who’s never lost a receipt.

**CREMEANS** (*cheerful, professional*)
Yes, Mom…Evanston. No, nobody’s been arrested…yet. Yes, I’m keeping the receipts.

(VISUAL):
– The shot is textbook symmetrical—bedspread taut, Mountain Dew bottle centered, Bible and packet of Tums aligned by the phone.
– Quick insert: Spreadsheet columns marching in perfect order on his clipboard—room numbers, check-in times, “Potential Bail Fund: $0.00 (for now).”
– He smiles at the Tums, a talisman against chaos.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
*If you go a million miles away, I'll track you down, girl.*

His mother’s voice crackles in response—comforting, proud, a little worried. He reassures her with facts and figures, the way other sons send flowers.

---

## **THE READING (A QUIET MOMENT)**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – NIGHT**

Order restored, Cremeans slips into pajamas—striped, soft, hospital corners everywhere. He pulls back the covers, nestles in, and opens his battered Bible. The bedside lamp casts a small, perfect sun across the page.

Outside, the city howls. Sirens wail. “*Firestarter*” echoes from some distant frat house, the window a blurry portal to the other universe—the one Cremeans refuses to enter.

(VISUAL):
– Centered, static: His face, eyes soft, mouth moving quietly over underlined scripture.
– Close-up: Neat blue pen marking “<font color="#245bdb">Do not be anxious about anything</font>…”
– Out of focus: Flashes of neon and silhouettes behind the curtain. Inside, peace.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
A little spiritual guidance never hurt anyone.  Especially when the rest of your crew is one tequila shot away from a felony.

He smiles—a gentle, unbreakable calm as chaos rages just out of frame.

---

## **THE SLEEP (A RESTFUL NIGHT)**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – LATER**

The lamp clicks off, plunging the room into a sanctified darkness. Cremeans lies on his back, one hand on his closed Bible, the other resting calmly by his side. His breathing is even, the covers barely rumpled—a monk in his cell, a general before battle.

(VISUAL):
– Wide, static: The room is immaculate, floor spotless, nothing but gentle moonlight and perfect geometry.
– Outside: Chaos howls—distant sirens, the echo of “I’M THE SANDMAN!” ricocheting down the street, a faint flicker of Christmas lights blinking “69” somewhere in the night.
– Inside: Peace, the kingdom of order holding strong.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
Let them have their madness.  I had rest. And a wake-up call set for 6:58 A.M.

*(SLOW MOTION: Cremeans sleeps on, faint smile at the corner of his mouth, untouched by the world’s hangover. The only oasis in a city of entropy.)*

---

## **THE AWAKENING (A REFRESHED START)**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – EARLY MORNING**

At exactly 7:00 A.M., the alarm emits a gentle, civilized buzz—nothing jarring, nothing cruel. Cremeans’ eyes snap open. He sits up at once, alert, rested, hair barely mussed, the kind of discipline that can only be born or built.

*(VISUAL):*
– The sunrise slides in through the curtains, painting the room gold and silent.
– Time-lapse: Sun rising behind the window, the hotel waking up with Cremeans at its center.
– The bed is still half-made beneath him. A glass of water, untouched. The itinerary, perfectly aligned, waiting for its moment.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
I am Superman…and I know that I can do these things…
…like not wake up covered in glitter and regret.

He stands, stretches, surveys his kingdom—a kingdom of order, one last time before the band shambles in, trailing disaster.

---

## **THE BREAKFAST (A NUTRITIOUS MEAL)**

**INT. HOTEL DINING AREA – MORNING**

Cremeans sits alone at a small, square table. Every detail is composed: napkin folded like origami, utensils gleaming. His breakfast is a still-life—whole-wheat toast, apple slices arranged in a perfect fan, a single hard-boiled egg, glass of milk so cold it sweats.

He eats with the calm deliberation of a monk on retreat. One bite, one sip, one check of the itinerary. The only chaos is the occasional clatter of a hungover guest at another table.

(VISUAL):
– Spotless tray, utensils aligned.
– Slow push-in: Cremeans reads the folded, color-coded itinerary, nodding with satisfaction.
– The rest of the room a blur—Cremeans in total focus, totally at peace.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
Fueling up for a big day.  No vomit. No moral hangover.  Just calcium and composure.

---

## **THE PRE-SHOW CHECK (A FINAL PREPARATION)**

**INT. HOTEL ROOM – LATE MORNING**

The band’s rooms are empty or disaster zones. But Cremeans’ space is a cockpit—everything in its place, ready for takeoff.

He stalks the room with clipboard in hand, eyes sharp, movements crisp. He checks and re-checks: Setlist taped to the wall. Cable cases snapped shut. Extra strings in a Ziploc. Portable label maker sits on the desk, still humming, little strips of order marching into battle.

(VISUAL):
– Overhead shot: Clipboard with every item perfectly ticked—Drumsticks? ✓ Spare batteries? ✓ Gaffer tape? ✓
– CLOSE-UP: Cremeans clicking his pen, labeling “BASS CASE” in all-caps, affixing the label with satisfaction.
– Every movement is deliberate, methodical—a metronome of calm as the storm brews outside.)_

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
Order is the opposite of entropy.  Entropy is the enemy of good gigs.  I am the last line of defense against entropy.

He surveys his domain, calm at the center of the storm, ready to wrangle the scattered, hungover herd into one last act of rock and roll heroism.

---

## **THE PATIENT WAIT (A CALM DEMEANOR)**

**INT. HOTEL LOBBY – LATE MORNING**

Cremeans sits with monk-like stillness on a couch that could double as a medieval torture device. A battered paperback rests on his lap, spine uncracked; he sips lobby coffee that tastes like defeat, but he doesn’t mind. He is patience personified.

Behind him, chaos oozes in.  First a limping silhouette—then two, then the whole bedraggled parade: every form of disaster a college town can breed.

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
…and I won’t be afraid…to be the one to save the day.  Especially if that day involves vomit cleanup and motivational speeches.

---

# **CHAPTER THIRTEEN: A GIRL NAMED DESTINY**

---

## **THE ARRIVAL (A DISAPPOINTING SIGHT)**

**INT. HOTEL LOBBY – MIDDAY**

The elevator dings, doors hiss open.
In they come, a living monument to poor decisions and bodily fluids:
– Kathy, shrouded in frat flag, mascara like war paint
– Jeremy, eyes hollow as a condemned house
– Jeff, streaked with grass and mud, dignity MIA
– Bill, one sock, one shoe, all shame
– Jim, party hat askew, still humming the song that nearly killed him
– Rico (Gilley?), glittering with Christmas lights, a fever-dream mascot

Cremeans closes his novel—a soft, deliberate *thwap*.  He stands, straightens, surveys the ruins.

**CREMEANS (V.O.):**
Well, at least someone got a good night’s sleep.  But, who the heck is this Rico?

He sighs—a single, saintly exhale—then sips his cold coffee, mind already running the damage report. Triage begins now.

**SOUND:**
The final, bittersweet twang of “*Superman*” lingers, then vanishes—replaced by the hush before the storm, the moment the adult takes the wheel.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
A perfectly symmetrical, overhead wide: Cremeans at the dead center, clipboard out, checklist ready.  The band sprawled around him like wounded soldiers after the worst battle of their lives.  Order, encircled by entropy.

The day can only go up from here.

---

**TITLE CARD:**
Evanston, Illinois. Late Morning. Dyche Stadium Calls.

**CUT TO BLACK.**

---

## **INT. HOTEL LOBBY – DAY**

The lobby gleams with faux opulence—polished marble, plastic ferns, the antiseptic tang of too much lemon cleaner. Morning sunlight slashes through tall windows like a judgmental spotlight. Muzak drones: a flaccid “*Don’t You Want Me*.”

**CREMEANS** stands dead center, immaculate, sipping Mountain Dew like it’s sacrament. His smile is tight, weaponized.

**(VISUAL):**
The camera pans across the incoming wreckage—**JEFF**, slack-jawed, shoes mismatched; **GILLEY**, still glittered from the scoreboard incident; **JIM**, blinking at daylight like a mole dragged from its burrow; **KATHY**, wrapped proudly in a stolen fraternity flag, strutting like it’s couture.

**CREMEANS** (pleasantly acidic)
Morning, degenerates. I trust you found enlightenment between bong hits and bad decisions?

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
One more sunrise like this and I’ll need both an exorcist and a lawyer.  It’s like managing a zoo—if the animals were drunk, hungover, and possibly armed.

Across the room, **NICK STEWART**—Island Records A&R—leans against a column. Crisp suit, arms folded, eyes sharp. Predator stillness.

**(VISUAL):** A zoom locks on Nick: unreadable face, zero blinking. The smile says *I’ve seen worse.* The eyes say *prove it.*

**JEFF** (slurring, grasping at dignity)
I was…engaged in discourse on post-structuralist theory. Intellectual stimulation.

**NICK (V.O.)**
If that guy owns a book, I’ll eat my Rolex.

**GILLEY** (grinning, brushing crumbs off his shirt)
Took in the sights. Made sparks fly.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
Literally. There was a scoreboard. A socket. And poor judgment.

**CREMEANS** turns to **KATHY**, flag flapping with every sway.

**CREMEANS** (half priest, half parole officer)
Kathy…is that your stage outfit now? Given our—lascivious—lyrics?

**(VISUAL):** Slow dolly-in on her face: smeared makeup, eyes defiant, chin high.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Lascivious? Please. Compared to last night, our lyrics read like the Psalms.

**NICK (V.O.)** (quietly amused)
Now we’re talking.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
The band fidgets under **CREMEANS**’ withering gaze. Behind them, Nick doesn’t move—no gavel, just a contract. The question hangs heavy: can these beautiful disasters pull it together?

---

## **INT. HOTEL HALLWAY – CONTINUOUS**

**CREMEANS** strides down the corridor, each step echoing with managerial frustration. He sips his Mountain Dew like it’s communion.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
This wasn’t just chaos. This was Exodus—if Moses had brought a band instead of tablets.

The Muzak fades as the camera tracks behind him. The carpet pattern ripples like it’s mocking him.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Ephesians said something about the full armor of God. Pretty sure that included underwear.

He reaches a door, swipes the keycard, and steps into hell.

---

## **INT. HOTEL ROOM – DAY**

The double room is a battlefield of youth and poor decisions. Socks drape over lamps. A traffic cone jams the mini-fridge. An unopened Gideon Bible hides under a pizza box.

Faint Muzak leaks through the walls, “Tainted Love” warped by drywall. Groans and coughs echo from every surface. The camera pans the wreckage: empty bottles, used Q-tips, a lone cowboy boot perched on the TV.

**CREMEANS** stands at attention like a weary general.

**CREMEANS** (delivering the verdict)
Helmuth von Moltke once said, “No plan survives contact with the enemy.” Well—guess who’s the enemy?

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Biblical chaos. Revelations with worse lighting.  I wasn’t a band manager. I was FEMA with a clipboard.

He claps once—sharp, commanding.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Everyone—horizontal. Now. I’m back in four hours. Dressed. Tuned. Sober-ish.

His gaze lands on **KATHY**, lounging in the fraternity flag, smug as royalty.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Kathy, that toga’s…bold. But please, for the love of decency—and our sponsors—put on some panties.

She smiles, flicks him a two-finger salute.

He turns to **JIM**, sprawled across a bed already occupied, knotted like a human pretzel.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Jim. You’re in the shower tonight.

**JIM (V.O.)**
It’s tiled. That’s practically a bed.

**CREMEANS** doesn’t answer. He opens the door.

**CREMEANS**
Four hours. Don’t make me call your parents.

The door clicks shut behind him, a period at the end of a threat.  The hallway outside stays behind—empty, quiet, judgmental.

---

## **INT. HOTEL HALLWAY – LATER**

The band shuffles out, groggy and disoriented. Their footsteps drag heavy against the carpet. Muzak from the lobby seeps louder now—a bland pop tune replacing the earlier ’80s hits.

**CREMEANS** waits by the door, holding a six-pack of ice-cold Mountain Dew. He hands each band member a can.

**CREMEANS** (matter-of-fact)
Breakfast of champions.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
It wasn’t balanced. But it was caffeinated. And that was what mattered.
Sometimes I felt like I was running a daycare center for rock-and-roll delinquents.

**JIM**, slightly more alert after the pep talk, gives him a high-five.

**JIM** (sincere)
Thanks, Cremeans. I appreciate you…you know…trying.

**CREMEANS** nods, a faint smile crossing his lips.

**CREMEANS** (reassuring)
It’s what I do.

**KATHY** pauses as she passes, flashing him a quick shot of her ass. He remains utterly unflinching, his face locked in neutrality.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
At least she washed her butt. That’s…something. Progress, maybe. God willing.  Small victories. That’s how you survive a tour. One scrubbed ass at a time.

The hallway empties as the band stumbles toward destiny—or disaster. Cremeans lingers a beat, then slips quietly back inside.

---

## **INT. HOTEL ROOM – CONTINUOUS**

The air still clings to last night’s sins: socks draped like crime scenes, tequila sweat and glitter in the carpet.  **CREMEANS** moves with resolve. Into the bathroom. A toilet flush—his only weapon against the filth.  He returns, opens his wallet like a priest presenting an offering, and counts out two crisp twenties. Places them on the nightstand, precise and visible.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
The room service crew didn’t sign up to clean after a rock-and-roll apocalypse.  But maybe forty bucks makes the vomit and glitter go down easier.

He adjusts the bills. Straightens them with intent. Respect. One last look around the wreckage, a nod, a sigh.

He turns and exits.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
The door clicks shut. Stillness holds. Muzak hums faintly from the hall, background radiation against the silence.  The band has moved on. The wreckage remains. And so does Cremeans—armed with Mountain Dew, a dog-eared Bible, and just enough hope to get them to showtime.

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – DAY**

Backstage is chaos incarnate: clanging cases, snapping cables, roadies barking in staccato rhythms. **CREMEANS** navigates it like a man possessed—one part manager, one part battlefield medic. The dull roar of the crowd bleeds in from the stadium, water bottles crack open like gunshots, gaffer’s tape sticks to skin and steel. It’s organized madness.

The camera trails **CREMEANS** in whip pans and crash zooms—he materializes from frame to frame, a caffeinated phantom slinging hydration and authority.

**THE BAND** (V.O., collectively)
Where the hell is he getting all this water?

**CREMEANS** spins to face the band like a drill instructor who’s read too much Sun Tzu.

**CREMEANS** (brisk, clipped)
Alright. We’re live in one hour. Ten minutes to set up. Forty minutes to burn it down. Ten to disappear. Like ghosts. Efficiency is survival.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
In rock and roll, as in war, timing is everything. Miss a cue, miss a shot.

He holds up his clipboard like sacred scripture.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Setlist: “Not Taken Kindly.” “The Left Hand.” “Payment in Kind.” The holy trinity of smut and sentiment.

**BILL** (circa 1993)
These tracks will be the spine of *69 Reasons*.

Clipboard close-up: bold Sharpie titles, coffee stains, a tiny demon sketched with a tambourine.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Transitions need to be tight. No dead air. You have nine minutes of music and one minute to look like legends.

**KATHY** cocks an eyebrow.

**KATHY** (sardonic)
So, we open with a song about blowjob critiques, move into something about voyeurism, and close on transactional sex. Is there a thesis statement I missed?

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Our lyrics were…emotionally raw. In a "Dear Penthouse" kind of way.  This band was like if Tennessee Williams wrote for Joan Jett.

**CREMEANS** exhales, already defeated.

**CREMEANS**
I don’t write the songs, Kathy. I just keep the wheels from falling off.

Then, quieter—almost sincere:

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
But today—today you need to sell it like it’s truth. Because someone’s watching who can change everything.

His eyes flick to the shadowed corner. There’s **Nick Stewart**—Island Records, immaculate suit, arms crossed, face unreadable. A sphinx with a clipboard.

The band stares at Cremeans—nervous, hungover, wired. Adrenaline rising. This is the last deep breath before the plunge.

One hour to go.

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

Backstage energy hums like a live wire. The band huddles amid a storm of coiled cables, cracked snare heads, scuffed amp cases. Outside, the crowd’s roar swells, shaking the air like thunder.

Sweeping shots: a trembling cymbal, sweat trickling down **BILL**’s neck, Cremeans’ clipboard held like a holy relic.

**BILL** raises a hand, uncertain.

**BILL** (anxious)
So…how are we closing the show?

**BILL (V.O.)**
The closer. The last note. The thing they’d talk about on the ride home—or never forget at all.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
The closer wasn’t just a song. It was the shot that rang out after the credits rolled.

**CREMEANS** steps forward, deadpan and deliberate.

**CREMEANS**
The same way you always do. “*Come Inside Me*.”

**JEREMY** winces at the memory of that sprawling final act.

**JEREMY**
But…it’s long. Like…*long* long.

A stopwatch clicks, red digits blinking. Smash cut to the crowd—a surging sea of anticipation, chanting, vibrating.

**CREMEANS** doesn’t blink.

**CREMEANS** (crisp, precise)
Which is why you modulate it. Build it, break it, rebuild it. Stretch or squeeze it, depending on the clock. Today? You ride that sucker to the buzzer.

He gestures to the wings—where a small light rig waits.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Yellow lamp: two minutes left. Red: you’re out. That’s your cue to end *loud*.

He scans their faces, locking eyes.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Does that work for everyone?

**ALL BUT BILL** (V.O.)
Yeah.

**BILL** shifts, chewing the idea.

**BILL** (soft)
I just…I don’t know if—

**CREMEANS** (cuts him off, voice like steel)
No room for subtlety, Bill. Not today.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Subtlety is for monks and Mennonites. This? This had to hit like a truck.

He claps—sharp, final.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Let’s load in.

The band disperses, heads nodding, hearts pounding. Cremeans turns back toward the shadow where Nick Stewart still stands, arms folded.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Alright, let’s go make some noise.

The band moves toward the stage entrance. The crowd’s roar swells—no longer sound, but pressure, like a storm surge behind a levee.

Just before stepping into the light, **GILLEY** leans toward **KATHY**, mischief in his grin.

**GILLEY** (low, sly)
Hey…about that toga. Any chance I could…borrow your panties?

Close-up: **KATHY**’s face, equal parts amusement and exasperation. She’s heard worse. She’s *said* worse.

The band, Cremeans at the front, assembles just offstage. The crowd’s roar hits like a freight train. Lights dim. A single chord from the previous act hangs in the air like ozone. It’s nearly 2 P.M. Showtime. Chicago, Illinois.

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

Backstage churns with motion—runners hustling, roadies shouting, techs mumbling into headsets. The crowd’s muffled roar is constant, surf crashing miles away.

**CREMEANS** is locked in, clipboard clutched, voice sharp.

The ambient thunder of the crowd, metal clanging, water bottles snapping open and draining fast. The camera tracks Cremeans pacing like a general mid-campaign—no sleep, no coffee, just pure adrenaline.

**CREMEANS** (clipped, focused)
Okay—moving on. Number four:  *“Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar.”*

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
It’s a crowd-pleaser. High tempo. Dirty charm. Perfect and minty after the warm-up act deflates.

**CREMEANS**
And let’s be honest—after last night, you degenerates probably feel *right at home* in a dive bar.

**KATHY** raises an eyebrow, wry, seen-it-all smile locked and loaded.

**KATHY** (bone-dry)
Actually, Cremeans…“*Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar*” is about a bachelorette party in New Orleans. Where the ladies…let’s just say…leaned *hard* into poor decision-making.

Flash cuts:
- Beads flying through humid air.
- Neon sign: BOURBON STREET_.
- Screaming topless woman on a balcony, flinging plastic necklaces like confetti.

**CREMEANS** (deadpan, quoting)
*“Passion’s got a hold of me.”*

Right. Moving on.

He points to the next item on the setlist.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Number five: *“It Has a Wow Finish.”*

**JEFF**, looking marginally less like death, chimes in—thoughtful, even.

**JEFF** (quietly reflective)
That one’s about my girlfriend’s interpretation of Rick and Ilsa from *Casablanca*.

**THE BAND (V.O., collectively)**
Jeff has a girlfriend?

**KATHY (V.O.)**
And she’s pulling her deep emotional insights from Casablanca? *Seriously?*
