The band exchanges looks—part disbelief, part concern.

**GILLEY** (flat-out incredulous)
Since when do *you* have a girlfriend?

**BILL** (half-joking, half-confused)
And Casablanca? That’s a weird-ass place to get romantic inspiration.

**JEFF** shrugs. Unbothered. Zen.

**JEFF** (even)
She has…interesting perspectives.

Cremeans doesn’t have time for this narrative arc. He skips straight to the finale.

**CREMEANS** (snapping back to focus)
Alright—next to last but not least: *“Snap and Sizzle.”*

He raises a hand before anyone can open their mouth.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
I think I can figure that one out just by reading the title.

Close-up: setlist taped to an amp, bold black marker:  *SNAP AND SIZZLE*.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Didn’t need the backstory.  Some titles just tell you everything.  Some truths are best left…unexplored.

He looks up from the clipboard, direct, commanding.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
Look—I don’t care what these songs mean. I care that you *nail* them. And stay hydrated.

He gestures at the dwindling stash of water bottles like a battlefield medic.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Hydration. It was the secret weapon. The difference between vomiting in the wings…and bringing the house down.

The band crowds the water like pilgrims at a sacred well. They drink. Not out of obligation, but out of belief. Hangovers are lifting. Nerves mutating into focus. Showtime is imminent.

Backstage at Dyche Stadium. Chicago, Illinois. Just shy of 2 P.M..

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

Backstage hums with raw, uncontrollable energy. The muffled crowd has become a physical force—constant, pulsing, like the inside of a jet engine.

**CREMEANS** stands at the edge of the stage, just out of the spotlight. Clipboard hanging useless at his side, his face frozen in stunned disbelief.

A wall of noise: crowd roaring, basslines pounding, concrete trembling under a thousand stomping feet. The camera shakes—subtly, as if mounted on a nervous heartbeat. Lighting fractures in bursts of white, purple, and gold slicing through haze.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
I…I didn’t understand it.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
It was like…magic. Uncut. Unfiltered.

First track: *Not Taken Kindly.*
They hit hard. No warm-up. And then—something happened.

He rewinds the Moment in his head: **KATHY** commanding the stage like a hurricane in combat boots, **GILLEY** tearing a solo straight through the fabric of reality.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Maybe it was Kathy’s presence. Maybe Gilley’s fingers caught fire. Or maybe Mars aligned with Saturn and the punk gods smiled down. But *something*…clicked.

The band launches into song two—*The Left Hand.* And the crowd?

Loses its collective mind. The concrete *shudders* beneath the stampede.

The camera swings to the audience—wide-eyed, wild. Sweat, screaming, lights flickering like the Fourth of July in a pressure cooker. Euphoria rendered in fast cuts.

**THE CROWD (V.O., collective)**
This is insane!!

The set rolls forward—
- *Payment in Kind.*
- *Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar.*
- *It Has a Wow Finish.*

Each track hits harder than the last. The crowd's roar swells like a living thing—demanding, primal, loving.

Now **CREMEANS** is beaming. Gone is the tension. Gone is the clipboard. He's vibrating with them, right there—like he's on stage himself.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
This wasn’t a show. This wasn’t a debut. This was a *phenomenon*.

**Nick Stewart**, the A&R scout, stands beside Cremeans, arms folded, posture rigid. His expression: pure, professional detachment. The band tears through the final chorus—Nick doesn’t take his eyes off the band.

**CREMEANS**, electric with adrenaline, offers him a bottle of water like it’s the Holy Grail.

**CREMEANS** (bright, booming)
Want some water? Gotta stay hydrated!

Close-up: the plastic bottle, sweat beading down the label. Quick cut: Nick’s face, still unreadable, watching, measuring.

Nick politely declines with a slight tilt of the head.

**NICK STEWART** (calm, cool)
No, thank you.

But Cremeans isn’t letting go. He all but *forces* the bottle into Nick’s hands, a preacher with a pamphlet.

**CREMEANS** (intense, near-maniacal)
Hydrate! It’s important!

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Hydration wasn’t just health advice. It was a lifestyle. A philosophy. Maybe even the secret to rock and roll superstardom.

Nick, slightly caught off guard, blinks—then cautiously takes a small sip. Cremeans watches like a proud father.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)** (dry, to himself)
This guy…is something else.

Cremeans, riding the wave of crowd energy, is lit up like Times Square. In his mind, he’s no longer a production manager. He’s *Rocky Balboa*.  The camera centers on Cremeans’ face—pure elation. He clenches his fists, eyes shining, practically bouncing on his toes.  The camera pans out across the stage—the band is *on fire*. The crowd? Frenzied. Unified. Glorious.

**CREMEANS** stands at the edge, soaked in sweat, pride, and stage lights.
His heart? Pounding. His belief? Unshakable.

Backstage at Dyche Stadium. Chicago, Illinois. The end of the set draws near.

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

Backstage vibrates—walls trembling, cables shaking, everyone wide-eyed. The crowd’s roar has become a living thing—relentless, primal, filling every crevice of the stadium.

**CREMEANS** stands frozen at stage left, eyes glued to his band.  The crowd screams. The band’s sound swallows the space whole. Then—cutting through it—**BILL’s synth**. The opening drone of *“Come Inside Me”* glimmers to life.  Camera shakes gently with the beat. Strobe lights pulse. The lens catches **CREMEANS** mid-glare—focused, sweaty, possessed by the Moment.  He glances at his watch, does the math in real time.

**CREMEANS** (muttering)
Eleven and a half minutes…standard runtime…So we’re at…let’s see…

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Basic math. Still a critical skill—even when you’re managing chaos with a clipboard.  *Seven* minutes. That’s all they had left. Seven minutes to stick the landing…or crash the plane.

The synth swells. **BILL** is locked in—pure 1980s neon drama. The melody is unmistakable. The crowd goes thermonuclear.

Spotlight on **BILL**, fingers dancing across the keys. Fog rolls around his boots, light flares with every chord shift.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Nailed it. Note for note. Just like on the demo.

Then—**JIM** drops in. His drum line isn’t loose, wild live chaos. It’s tight. Controlled. Studio-level precision.

**CREMEANS**’ eyes widen. Something’s different.

Camera closes on **JIM**—arms moving like pistons, every strike echoing like thunder in a bottle.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Jim. Holy hell. He *actually* did it.

Memory snap—Cremeans flashes back to pre-show chaos: **BILL** and **JIM** huddled at the kit, whispering, tinkering.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
The mic tricks. The setup magic. They pulled it off. In ten minutes flat.

High-speed montage—**BILL** and **JIM** crouched over the drum mics. Gaffer tape. Quick tests. Fingers pointing. Thumbs up. They recreated the gated reverb sound—studio magic, on a stadium stage.

Now **CREMEANS** is beaming—lit up like a Vegas marquee. Anxiety, vaporized. His voice breaks out over the sound.

**CREMEANS** (half-whisper, half-shout)
Yes. YES! They did it!

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
This was it. The Moment. They weren’t just playing—they were *fighting for their lives.* And the crowd? The crowd was devouring every second.

The camera soars across the stage—The band is a machine. A glorious, sweating, screaming miracle.  The crowd is on fire. Jumping. Shouting. Lost in the Moment. And backstage, **CREMEANS**—fists clenched, eyes glassy, heart pounding.

Dyche Stadium. Chicago, Illinois. Seven minutes to curtain.

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

Backstage is a furnace—*all noise, nerves, and raw voltage*. The band rips through *“Come Inside Me”*. **CREMEANS** is glued to the sightlines, joy tightening into something sharper—panic coiling beneath the thrill.  The crowd throbs. Bass booming, stadium shaking. **KATHY**’s vocals—soaring, primal, unstoppable.  *Do you want that, baby?*

The camera rocks hard, as if mounted to a jackhammer. Stage lights flicker like distant lightning. Close-up: **CREMEANS**’ face, smile gone, pure calculation.

His eyes snap to the control panel. Yellow light—glowing like a caution sign at the end of the world.

**CREMEANS** (muttering)
Seven minutes in…Four and a half left…

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
They hadn’t even hit the bridge.  This was a disaster. A beautiful, glorious, full-tilt disaster.

**KATHY** belts the seventh chorus like she’s trying to crack the dome of the stadium. Then—red lamp flashes.

> [!fail]
> Extreme close-up: red lamp pulsing, a warning siren.


Cut to **CREMEANS**—eyes wild, jaw slack.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
They’re ignoring the red light. They’re actually IGNORING the red light.  This was it. They were going to get cut. Live. In front of *fifteen thousand people*.

His brain spins—full calculator mode.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
If they play it all the way through…Four minutes. Minimum.

He shoots a desperate look at the show producer.

Close-up: **CREMEANS**—sweat, pleading eyes. Quick cut—producer, cool and unbothered.

Meanwhile, Nick Stewart is tapping his foot, smiling faintly. Living his best scouting life.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**
This…this is *something*.

To Cremeans’ shock, the producer gives a subtle nod to the sound engineer.

The music keeps going.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
He’s letting them play! He’s actually letting them *play*.

Cremeans could fly. He could punch a hole in the moon.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
I’ve achieved cold fusion.

The band shifts into the third bridge. A full-blown instrumental detonation. Every member flexing like it’s their last performance on Earth.

Rapid cuts: **JIM**, arms blurring. **BILL**, coaxing thunder from the synth. **GILLEY**, guitar neck snapping under his grip. **KATHY**, hair wild, body in motion.

Nick Stewart leans in toward Cremeans, yelling over the sound.

**NICK STEWART** (amused)
Bit self-indulgent, isn’t it?

**CREMEANS** just stares, eyes wide, pulse in his throat.

**CREMEANS** (disbelieving)
“Bit”?

Camera sweeps the stage—the band giving it everything, crowd a sea of raised fists and pure hysteria.

Backstage, **CREMEANS**—frozen, breathless, radiant. *Unbelieving. Overjoyed.*

*Still Dyche Stadium. Chicago, Illinois. Well past their time slot. And nobody wants it to end.*

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

Backstage is trembling—walls, rails, even breath. The roar is otherworldly. **CREMEANS** stands rooted, no longer managing, no longer calculating—just *experiencing*.  The crowd is unhinged. The music booms. The floor rumbles. **JEREMY’s** guitar shimmers like heat on asphalt.  Camera rattles with the rhythm of the stadium. Stage lights flicker—blue, white, crimson. Tight close-up: **CREMEANS**’ face, eyes wide, mouth slightly agape.

His gaze snaps to **JEREMY’s** guitar. He recognizes it—the *shimmer*. He knows what it means.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
The shimmer. That goddamn shimmer.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
It meant one thing. They were going full monty. Every. Single. Goddamn. Second.

They weren’t winding down. They were *stretching* it. Pushing *“Come Inside Me”* to its farthest edge.

**JEREMY’s** fingers glide across the strings, shimmer cascading through the amps. Cut to the crowd—mouths open, eyes locked, drenched in sweat and stage light.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
And then…it happened.

The music *shifts*. Another bridge—unexpected, hypnotic. A simple lyric begins to loop:

*“Let it go.”*

**JEFF (V.O.)**
It was filler. Just a line to stretch the track. Nothing more.

**KATHY** on stage—spotlighted, hair wild, voice like velvet steel. She sings: *“Let it go.”*

The camera sweeps—the crowd begins to echo it back.

**THE CROWD (V.O., joining in)**
*_Let it go!*
*_Let it go!*
*_Let it go!*

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Then they started singing.

All of them.

Camera pans wide—fifteen thousand voices joining in. Mouths moving in sync. Harmony by instinct.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Fifteen thousand people…singing a song they’d *never heard* before.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
It was…surreal.

Camera on **CREMEANS**—completely undone. No clipboard. No control. Just disbelief and reverence.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
How…how are they doing that?

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
This wasn’t fusion. This was…some kind of miracle.

Wide aerial pullback—stage glowing, band in full flow, crowd chanting like a hymn.

*Let it go!  Let it go!  Let it go!*

Their voices soar into the Chicago afternoon.  **CREMEANS**—silent. Staring. Mind blown.

Dyche Stadium. Chicago, Illinois. The end is nigh. But nobody wants it to stop.

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The band takes their final bow. The crowd erupts—a *roar* that rattles concrete and eardrums. Confetti explodes overhead. Lights strobe, a finale at the end of the world.

The crowd screams, applause crashing like waves. Final echoes of *“Come Inside Me”* ring out, confetti raining like metallic snow.

Camera follows **CREMEANS**—shoulders tense, eyes alight—as he navigates through chaos. His face: a volatile mix of relief, euphoria, and disbelief.

He barrels up to the show producer near the soundboard. Nick Stewart drifts in behind him, curiosity now fully engaged.

**CREMEANS** (breathless, overwhelmed)
Thank you! Thank you *so* much! For letting them finish. They *killed* out there!

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
They did it. They *actually* did it.  A miracle. A pure rock and roll miracle.

Nick Stewart, arms crossed, eyebrow raised, *finally* impressed.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**
Intriguing. Very intriguing.

**NICK STEWART** (cool, impressed)
That was…something. Especially considering they were a complete non-entity from some cornfield in Ohio…*forty-five minutes ago*.

The producer yawns, still watching the stage, then shoots a knowing glance at **CREMEANS**.

**PRODUCER** (mock-serious, dry)
Hey. We had to let them finish.  We couldn’t cut ’em off. Not with *that kind* of…entertainment happening on stage.

**CREMEANS** pauses, frowning.

**CREMEANS** (puzzled)
Entertainment?

The producer leans in, voice low, conspiratorial.

**PRODUCER** (half-whisper)
Let’s just say for the last third of that song, we had a fantastic view of **KATHY**’s assets.

Quick cuts:
- **KATHY** mid-performance, spinning.
- The producer winking, smug.

**CREMEANS** stares, mouth slightly open.

**CREMEANS** (incredulous)
Are you…serious?

The producer breaks into laughter.

**PRODUCER** (laughing)
Relax. I’m kidding!

*Beat.*

**PRODUCER (CONT’D)** (now sincere)
Well…mostly kidding. She did accidentally moon the camera a few times at the end there.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Oh, for the love of…

Nick Stewart turns toward **CREMEANS**, amused and now *fully dialed in*.

**NICK STEWART** (genuinely curious)
So…the fraternity flag? That part of the act?

**CREMEANS** sighs, rubs his temples.

**CREMEANS** (resigned)
It’s a long story. Involves an IUD, some ibuprofen, and a very bad decision at a fraternity party.

Camera locks on **CREMEANS**. His face: *exhaustion*, disbelief, and dawning horror. The crowd still roars behind him—but now it’s blended with the reality crash of what just happened.

Still backstage. Dyche Stadium. Chicago, Illinois. The Moment after the miracle.

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The roar is fading. House lights start rising, casting a pale wash over the sea of confetti. Stagehands are already unbolting, unplugging, hauling. **CREMEANS** stands still amid the motion—shell-shocked, exhilarated, *processing*.

Echoes of the crowd dissolve. Metal-on-metal clanging, scattered applause, low murmurs. The footsteps of the band approach from stage left.

Camera on **CREMEANS**’ face—drenched in sweat, blinking against the light. Exhaustion. Disbelief. And underneath it…*hope*. Real hope.

Nick Stewart stands nearby—no clipboard, no sunglasses, no swagger. Just a man who’s *seen something*.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**
This business is full of phonies. Guys with big words and no follow-through. But this guy…Cremeans…he was cut from something else.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**
He’s Toledo steel. Sharp. Honest. Cuts through bullshit like it’s butter.

He turns to **CREMEANS**—expression open, engaged.

**NICK STEWART** (decisive)
I think I can do business with a man like you.

Close-up on Nick’s face—*no smile, no pretense*. Just clarity.

**CREMEANS** blinks, still processing, still sweaty.

**CREMEANS** (half-laugh, half-dazed)
Business?

**NICK STEWART** (firm, certain)
I want to meet the band. When they come off.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
This was it. This was *the* Moment. Or…at least one of them.  Still had to deal with the whole…mooning incident.

Cremeans glances toward the stage entrance—gears kicking in again.

**CREMEANS** (practical)
Sure. Just…give me a second.

He gestures at a nearby stack of empty water bottles.

**CREMEANS (CONT’D)**
They’re coming in hot, sweaty, and stupidly thirsty.

Quick cut—water bottles, dented and half-empty. Cut to the stage entrance, where the band emerges like survivors from battle.

Nick Stewart grins—*amused, approving*.

**NICK STEWART** (chuckling)
Of *course*.

The band stumbles in—*flushed, dripping, elated*.

**V.O. (Collective Thought)**
Water!

**KATHY (V.O.)**
I need a shower. And a stiff drink.

Camera tracks the band as they cross the backstage floor. **CREMEANS** stands waiting—arms full of water. Nick Stewart beside him, already imagining contracts and studio dates. The band—tired, loud, half-laughing—heads toward the men who might change everything.

Still backstage. Still Dyche Stadium. Chicago, Illinois. The end of one performance. The start of something else entirely.

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The band staggers in—sweaty, flushed, buzzing with adrenaline. The final echoes of the crowd ripple through the steel bones of the stadium.

Crowd noise still fading. Gear slammed into cases. Heavy breathing, excited half-laughs, footsteps—the *aftermath*.

The camera captures them up close—faces glowing, hair stuck to foreheads, clothes wrinkled and sweat-streaked. They look wrecked. They look victorious.

Suddenly—**KATHY** freezes. Eyes wide, mouth slightly open. She’s staring at **GILLEY’s** guitar. Hanging from one of the tuning pegs—like a banner of divine comedy—are **her panties**.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Oh. My. God.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Of all the gin joints, in all the towns, in all the world…my panties had to end up *on* his guitar.

Extreme close-up: fabric fluttering from the tuning peg. Smash cut to **KATHY**’s face—pure, unfiltered mortification. With ninja-speed embarrassment reflexes, she snatches them away and shoves them beneath the toga, face burning.

**GILLEY (V.O.)**
Whoops. Collateral damage.

As **KATHY** recovers, **JIM** and **BILL** lock eyes on Nick Stewart—and freeze.

Quick punch-ins: **JIM**’s pupils dilate, **BILL**’s mouth drops open. Cut to **Nick**—stoic, collected, hands in pockets.

**JIM** (low, urgent)
*Holy* shit…It’s Nick Stewart!

**BILL** (barely breathing)
From *Island Records?*

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Nick Stewart? Island Records? Are they talking about what I think they are?

**JEFF**, **JEREMY**, and **KATHY** blink in confusion.

**JEFF** (deadpan)
I didn't hear you.

**JIM** and **BILL** exchange reverent, almost religious looks.

**JIM** (whispering)
He’s a *legend.* Signed half the British invasion.

**BILL** (whispering harder)
Jeff, he’s the guy who discovered…*U2!*

Rapid cuts: **JIM** and **BILL** staring like disciples. **Nick Stewart** coolly watching them all. Unbothered. Slightly amused.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
Island Records…that rang a bell. MTV. 3 A.M.. Fuzzy reception. Something with a lion.

**KATHY**, now composed and internally recalibrating, eyes Nick Stewart with sudden intrigue.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Okay. *Now* things were getting interesting.

Camera centers on the band—their fatigue giving way to something else: hope, urgency, *holy shit, this might be real*.  **Nick Stewart** stands still, watching. An offer is coming. Everything’s about to change.

Still backstage. Still Dyche Stadium. Chicago, Illinois. Moments after the miracle._

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The band stands in a *nervous semicircle*—like students before a surprise oral exam—staring at Nick Stewart, the A&R demigod who’s just emerged from myth and metaphor into their very real, very sweaty orbit.

**CREMEANS**, still clutching his sacramental armload of water bottles, stays off to the side—hovering somewhere between *proud dad* and *project manager with PTSD*.

The tail end of the crowd’s roar drifts up into the rafters. Equipment clanks in the background like industrial punctuation. The soft panting of people trying to play it cool. A quiet but unmistakable hum of *tension thick enough to cut with a Ginsu*.

Camera on Nick Stewart—tight, steady. His face is calm. His gaze? Not. He’s *reading* them. Each one. And they *know* it.

Nick breaks the silence.

**NICK STEWART** (even, measured)
Well…That was certainly…meaty.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**
I’ve seen every kind of band. Over-rehearsed. Over-hyped. Shiny but hollow. These kids? Raw. Messy. Electric. Like a broken lamp still throwing off sparks.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**
They’ve got raw energy. Untamed. Unpolished. And a manager who seems to juggle a clipboard, a hangover, and a nuclear-level panty crisis without dropping the ball.

Nick glances at **CREMEANS**, grins slightly, then returns to scanning the band like a field surgeon deciding which parts are worth saving.

**NICK STEWART**
Let’s talk about the performance.

*Pause.*

**NICK STEWART (CONT’D)**
You grabbed that crowd by the collar in under thirty seconds. That’s not *luck.* That’s instinct. You made them believe they were watching *something great.*

Flashbacks—snaps from the performance:  **KATHY** spinning. **JEREMY**'s shimmer. **JIM**’s snare snap. The crowd’s faces turned to *rapture*.

**NICK STEWART (CONT’D)**
That kind of *connection*—you can’t teach that. It either *lives in your bones*…or it doesn’t.

**JEFF (V.O.)**
He was talking about us. *Us.*

**BILL (V.O.)**
This is it. This is the speech that ends with a contract in someone’s hand and a plane ticket in someone’s shoe.

Nick’s eyes move methodically—locking onto each band member. Measuring. Calculating. He’s a lion in a button-down shirt.

**NICK STEWART (CONT’D)**
You’re rough. Frayed. But that’s not a weakness. It’s *texture.* It’s *honest.* Most of what I see is sterile, produced within an inch of its life. But *you*? You kill on stage.

Close-ups—**KATHY**’s cautious smile. **JEREMY** blinking hard, jaw clenched. **JIM** holding back a grin. **JEFF**…trying not to faint.

**KATHY (V.O.)**
Rough around the edges? Please. We were *splinters held together with duct tape and tequila.*

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
They were a mess. A symphonic, toe-tapping, ass-shaking mess. And somehow…that *worked.*

Then, without preamble, Nick’s focus sharpens. He turns to **CREMEANS**.

**NICK STEWART** (clipped, direct)
*Mr. Cremeans*…I’d like a word. Privately.

The camera shifts to **CREMEANS**—clipboard finally gone, face suddenly unreadable. He nods once—*serious mode engaged.*  The camera slowly pulls back. The band holds still—watching, hoping, barely breathing. The air around them is charged—like lightning’s about to strike, or already has.  Nick and **CREMEANS** step aside.  And just like that…everything’s in motion.

*Still Dyche Stadium. Still backstage. Still glowing with the afterburn of something impossible.*

---

## **INT. DYCHE STADIUM – BACKSTAGE AREA – CONTINUOUS**

The air is *radioactive* with tension. Everyone holds their breath. Even the sound of roadies packing up seems muted by the *gravity* of what’s about to happen. **CREMEANS** stands completely still—clipboard gone, anxiety filed away like a tax return from another lifetime.

The tail-end hum of the crowd. Metal gear ratcheting into place. Silence from the band. Then, soft and surgical—the *hiss* of a Mountain Dew can being cracked open.

Camera cuts in *tight* on **CREMEANS’ face**. Blank. Calm. A man in the middle of chaos, holding a can of cold sugar water and an unshakable belief in himself. Without missing a beat, **CREMEANS** pulls a business card from his pocket—not flashy, not oversized, just *intentional*. He hands it to **Nick Stewart**, whose eyebrow lifts half a centimeter.

**CREMEANS** (even, level)
I only talk to principals.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
It was a line I’d been saving. A silver bullet in a world of blanks. And this? This was the monster I built it for.

**CREMEANS (V.O.)**
Play hardball. Even if your bat’s made of plastic. Swing like it’s maple.

Without another syllable, **CREMEANS** turns—a smooth, surgical 180—and walks out the nearest door. No strut. No smile. Just presence.

Slow-motion tracking shot: his retreating silhouette, the corridor light framing him like a saint walking into the unknown.

The band stands frozen. Jaws slack. Eyes wide. Hearts pounding.

**V.O. – COLLECTIVELY**
What…the actual hell…just happened?

**BILL (V.O.)**
Did he just…Did he just imply he only talks to Chris *fucking* Blackwell?

**JEFF (V.O.)**
Is he insane?

**KATHY (V.O.)**
No. That was the most baller move I’ve ever witnessed.

**JIM (V.O.)**
I think we just saw history rewritten.

**JEREMY (V.O.)**
I need a goddamn drink.

There’s a long, loaded beat. Then—**Nick Stewart** starts to laugh. Not a polite chuckle. Not industry laughter. Real, cathartic, shaking-the-dust-off-his-soul kind of laughter.

Close-up on **Nick’s face**, cracked open in unfiltered joy.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**
I’ve seen agents fake it. Labels push it. Bands die trying to fake what that man just pulled off.

**NICK STEWART (V.O.)**
He *checkmated* me. With a can of soda and a goddamn laminated card.

(beat)
That’s when I knew.

(beat)
I had to work with this band. Because any band with *that guy* behind them…That’s not a gamble. That’s destiny.

---

**(OBSERVATION – JEFF – YEARS LATER):**
We didn’t know what was happening. But we knew one thing: **CREMEANS** had just kicked open a door we didn’t even know existed.

**(OBSERVATION – BILL – YEARS LATER):**
I still think he was bluffing. But damn…what a bluff.

**(OBSERVATION – KATHY – YEARS LATER):**
He made it look like this was all part of the plan. Even when the plan was made on the back of a napkin in a stolen dorm room microwave.

**(OBSERVATION – JIM – YEARS LATER):**
That was our manager. Our chaos conductor. The only man alive who thought a *Mountain Dew* was a negotiation tool.

**(OBSERVATION – JEREMY – YEARS LATER):**
All I remember is thinking: We’re either going to be famous…or arrested.

---

Back in the moment—Nick’s laughter fades. He straightens his jacket. Then addresses the band with the gravity of a State Department diplomat.

**NICK STEWART** (cool again, deadly serious)
Right.

(beat)
Well…I believe Mr. Cremeans mentioned something about hydration?

He picks up a water bottle and holds it out—not like a drink, but like a *torch*.

The band stares at Nick. Then the water bottle. Then each other. Their world has just shifted—by a line, a laugh, and the quiet exit of a man who’d just played the biggest hand of his life…and *won*.

*Still backstage. Still Dyche Stadium. Still Chicago. But nothing is the same.*

---

# **CHAPTER FOURTEEN : DON'T BUY PLAYERS.  BUY WINS**

---

**(SOUND):**
A relentless, rhythmic instrumental. Drums and bass, a low synth undercurrent. No lyrics, no gloss—just momentum.

**(VISUAL)—clean, observational):**
Shots move slow, deliberate. Focus on hands: pens scribbling, ticket stubs traded, sweat sliding down a glass. Bar lights bouncing off old wood.

---

## **W.O. WRIGHT’S, BEAVERCREEK, OH – INITIAL ASSESSMENT**

Nick Stewart edges through the doorway—sport coat soft at the seams, boots broken in, pen already out. No flash, just focus. He’s not here to be noticed; he’s here to *notice*.

**WIDE—BAR INTERIOR:**
W.O. Wright’s at capacity, thick with anticipation and domestic beer. The air is humid with pre-show nerves. Every surface is taken: elbows, pint glasses, scuffed Nikes. Stage lights haze the front row in red and blue.

**(SOUND):**
Crowd talk—hyped, impatient. Drums thumping through the floor during soundcheck, an accidental pulse in everyone’s shoes.

**AT THE SOUNDBOARD:**
Cremeans is a one-man mission control—clipboard in hand, lips tight with calculation. Kathy tests her mic with a practiced flick. Bill fine-tunes a synth patch, not looking up. Jeremy bends to his pedalboard, precise and private.

Nick checks his watch—analog, naturally.  Jots: “7:04 p.m.—band nearly set.”  He scans the crowd, notes the shape of anticipation:

- Heads craned toward the stage
- Laughter at the bar, dying off as amps warm
- That particular hush right before something begins

**IN THE CROWD:**
A college kid, beer sloshed on his sleeves, elbows a friend:
“Dude, if they do ‘Wow Finish’ second again, I’m done for.”

A girl in a cut-up jacket, hair in her eyes:
“Heard there’s a new song. Gilley’s supposed to shred tonight.”

Nick, barely blinking, writes:
“Repeat faces. Anticipation: feverish. Word-of-mouth: everywhere.”

**NICK (V.O.):**
Not just fans. Believers. There’s an edge to it—something I haven’t seen outside of the city, not this far from the coasts.

**ON STAGE:**
The band shares a quick laugh—no nerves showing, just the ritual. Cremeans whispers something that makes Kathy smirk. Gilley shakes out his hands, rolling his shoulders like a prizefighter.

Nick logs it: 
“Chemistry: unforced. Leadership: visible.”

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Lights drop a shade. The temperature in the room changes—everybody closer, everything louder. The air pulls tight.

Nick leans in, not out. The notebook never leaves his hand.

**NICK (V.O.):**
This isn’t just a set. It’s ignition. I’m here to see if it burns.

---

## **W.O. WRIGHT’S: PERFORMANCE DATA**

Commuted takes the stage. Nick Stewart’s attention sharpens, pen and stopwatch in hand, every detail a number waiting to be logged.

**(SOUND):**
Commuted launches—guitars jagged, drums sharp, crowd roar cresting over the band. For a bar, it’s a stadium’s worth of noise.

**(VISUAL):**
Every motion tracked—Nick’s eyes flick from the stage to the room to the clock. A documentarian’s gaze: dispassionate, hungry.

**CLOSE-UP – NICK’S NOTEBOOK:**
Setlist recorded with precision:

1. “Not Taken Kindly” – 4:18
2. “The Left Hand” – 3:46
3. “Payment in Kind” – 4:05
4. “Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar” – 4:41
5. “It Has a Wow Finish” – 3:33
6. “Come Inside Me” – 11:02

Transitions noted: “Clean segues. No dead air. Tight.”

**WIDE—THE CROWD:**
It’s kinetic—bodies pressed tight, fists in the air, two couples spinning slow in the back. One guy up on a chair, arms wide, singing along, already lost his voice.

**NICK (V.O.):**
This is where the real numbers live—not on the soundboard, but in the crowd. Applause per square foot. Sweat per ounce. You don’t measure heat by the thermostat—you measure it by the fever in the room.

**Nick logs:**
“Dance floor packed by song two. Applause peaks at 2:03—‘Wow Finish.’ Zero early exits before encore.”

**AT THE BAR:**
Nick slips sideways, unobtrusive. Counts glasses—bartender pulling drafts with the urgency of a pit crew. He times a round: watches the order, the pour, the delivery. Chalkboard scrawled:  “$3 cover. $1.50 PBR. $2.50 house whiskey. Miller Lite sold out by song three.”

Scribbles: “Revenue potential: high. Engagement = consumption.”

**NICK (V.O.):**
Forget the guys in the glass offices. This is the market, right here—noisier, messier, more honest. It drinks cheap beer and sings back every line.

**POST-SHOW:**
House lights up. The crowd, sweat-stained and elated, floods the front of the stage. Kathy’s surrounded, signing arms, setlists, and a torn concert flyer. Jeremy’s got three new friends and a Sharpie. Bill autographs a synth key. Gilley’s mobbed by three girls with banana bras and too much lip gloss. Cremeans—already rolling cables, one eye on the exit.

**Nick tallies:**
“Fan interactions: 37. Age range: 18–34. High lyric recall. Gear pack-out: 27 minutes.”

**NICK (V.O.):**
Liked is good. Remembered is everything. And tonight, nobody’s forgetting.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Nick watches as the crowd thins but the energy lingers. Kathy’s at the bar, water bottle in one hand, someone’s phone number scrawled up her arm. Cremeans hauls the last amp. Nick closes his notebook. Clicks his stopwatch. Allows himself a thin, satisfied smile.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Data never lies. And tonight, the numbers sang.

---

## **BOGART’S, CINCINNATI, OH: SCALING UP**

*Scaling* up. That’s the test. No more safety net. If Commuted’s just a bar band, tonight’s the night the cracks show.

**(SOUND):**
A deep, relentless groove. Bottles, voices, footsteps on old concrete. The crowd is heavier—older, sharper, more deliberate.

**(VISUAL):**
Camera glides along the perimeter—Bogart’s: 1,500 capacity, all brick and balcony, stained history in every light rig. A real stage. You feel the money in the air.

**NICK (V.O.):**
W.O. Wright’s was a pressure cooker. Bogart’s is a proving ground. Different scale. Different gravity.

**NOTES:**
Venue Capacity: 1,500
Acoustics: natural, little slapback
Demographics: skewing older, city crowd, less small-town sweat

Nick’s thumb flicks the mechanical clicker. Each head through the door, another point on the graph. Click. Click. Click.

*“Expanded* crowd. College, late-30s, hipsters. Leather. Piercings. More city than county. No dead air in the lobby.”

**TICKET WINDOW (EXT. BOGART’S):**
Nick leans on the glass, voice low.

**NICK** (quiet, easy)
How’s it looking?

**ATTENDANT**
Sold out. Three days. Balcony too. Not a single walk-up.

Nick nods, notes it:  *“Advance sell-out, full prepay. Market anticipation: real.”*

**INSIDE—SOUND CHECK:**
Nick crouched behind the sound booth, decibel meter out—old-school needle, no flash.  Reading: 107 dB, full spectrum. Vocals ride the top, synths punch through. It’s clean. Cleaner than expected.

**SHOWTIME—STAGE:**
Lights snap on—real white, hard and surgical. Kathy steps in, center frame, owns it with a look.  Gilley cuts through the haze with lead lines that don’t meander.  Jeff’s bass is subsonic, rattling the floor.  Bill’s synth is a *wall.*
Jim’s snare doesn’t crack—it pronounces.

**NICK (V.O.):**
No distortion. No mistakes. Too tight for a band this young.  “Adaptation: confirmed. Fear: not observed.”

Lighting—notes:  “Pro rig, quick response. Band using full stage, not hiding.”

**AFTER THE SHOW—LOBBY:**
No one leaves. The lobby’s a queue—shirts, setlists, records, bodies pressed close just to linger in the afterglow.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Pull isn’t taught. It’s gravity. This band’s got it.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Nick against a column, notebook shut, watching the last of the line. There’s no smile. Just calculation—the sense that the next stop won’t be a bar, or even a city this size.

**NICK (V.O.):**
They didn’t just fill the room. They filled the space. This might be the last time it’s easy to get a ticket.

---
## **BOGART’S: REVENUE ANALYSIS**

Second night. Same room. Same fire. *The question isn’t whether Commuted can fill Bogart’s. It’s how much they wring out of every ticket, every body, every second onstage.*

**(SOUND):**
Crowd at fever pitch. Cash drawers snapping. Bottles clinking in time with “It Has a Wow Finish.”  The room isn’t just full—it’s restless, greedy, *primed*.

**(VISUAL):**
Fast, data-hungry intercuts:  Nick in constant motion, timing bar lines, counting heads at merch, jotting in his battered notebook. His focus: predatory, clinical, unwavering.

**BAR REVENUE TRACKING:**
He lingers near the bar, blending in with the noise.

- Four bartenders, hands blurred.
- Orders: Coors, gin, Jack.
- Nine-minute wait at the peak, during “Sweet Memories in a Dive Bar.”

**NICK (V.O.):**
Forget the setlist. Watch the pour speed. That’s your ticker. That’s *real-time market sentiment.*

**MERCHANDISE SALES:**
The merch table is a feeding frenzy.

- Shirts: mediums and larges, sold out.
- Cassettes: gone before encore.
- Hand-numbered lyric zines: line eighteen deep, two bucks a pop.

Nick’s tally: “Merch Estimate: $4,100. Time: 9:32 P.M..”

**NICK (V.O.):**
This isn’t a crowd, it’s a market. They aren’t just watching—they’re buying. They want a piece.

**POST-SHOW—REVENUE ANALYSIS:**
Nick corners the manager, quiet but direct.

**MANAGER (low, half-amazed):**
Bar’s up forty percent. Never seen a merch line like that—ever.

Nick’s only answer: a checkmark in the notebook. *Viable.* Very.

**NICK (V.O.):**
This isn’t just music. It’s conversion.  Fans to dollars. Noise to margin.

He flips to his Beavercreek notes—checks a box, draws a line.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Scaling’s not hope. It’s math. Tonight, it adds up.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Nick posts up at a steel column, running his totals.  Behind him, the band’s gear slides out the door—methodical, machine-tight, nobody lingering.  The room smells like sweat, money, and the start of something big.

**NICK (V.O.):**
*Now* we’re in business.

---

## **THE SMOKY DIVE: ATMOSPHERE AND AMBIENCE**

**INT. STILLWRIGHTS BAR – COLUMBUS, OH – NIGHT**

*If* ambiance could puke, it would do it here.

Stillwrights is a shoebox of bad decisions—plasterboard and plywood, everything lacquered with cigarette tar and regret. The band’s stage is barely a step up from the floor, haloed in red from a busted bulb.

**(SOUND):**
Thick guitar buzz, glasses clinking, low mutter of the crowd, the occasional sharp crack of pool balls. Somewhere, a fryer sizzles.

**(VISUAL):**
The lens loses the battle with smoke—faces smear into color fields, everything with a cheap noir blur.  Neon throws bar code over sweat-stained faces. Every inch is friction.

**NICK’S TABLE:**
Nick hunched over a sticky two-top, wedged next to a jukebox wheezing out “Turn the Page.”  Legal pad open, corner stained dark, pen moving with grim intent.

**INSERT—LEGAL PAD NOTES:**
- Ambient noise: “ludicrous.”
- Visibility: “smoke index high, light index low.”
- Floor spill: “3:17—record.”
- Food orders: “Pickles 8, Nachos 3, Mozzarella 1 (regret).”

**NICK (V.O.):**
Atmosphere. Everyone calls it “vibe.” Really it’s just math—particles per million, grease per cubic foot.

He counts food baskets: one, two, three…makes a note.

**NICK (V.O.):**
If they’re eating, they’re planning to stay. Or at least not bolt before the set’s done. That’s staying power.

**CAMERA POV:**
A pint goes over at table 7—spreads like an oil slick.  A girl chain-smokes with two lighters going.  Guy in Megadeth sleeveless yells, “Play the bridge!” Nobody listens.

Nick checks his watch. Sighs. Writes:  “Crowd density: low. Enthusiasm: stubborn. Acoustics: disastrous.”

He sips bourbon, tastes futility. Makes a face.

**NICK (V.O.):**
It’s ugly, but ugly’s honest. These places teach you what matters. No room for fake.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
The pad, corners curling.  The band in the red light, wringing every ounce out of cheap gear and shit sound.  A mozzarella stick dying a slow, sticky death on the linoleum.

**NICK (V.O.):**
They don’t flinch. That’s the tell. That’s what makes them worth betting on.

---

## **THE EMPTY BAR: MINIMAL VIABILITY**

**INT. IDORU MUSIC BAR – SPRINGFIELD, OH – NIGHT**

It’s a weeknight that barely deserves the name. Even the jukebox would rather stay quiet.

**(SOUND):**
Guitar and snare echo off too much empty brick. The relentless buzz of the lights.  The hollow thunk of a single bottle, set down with nothing to toast.

**(VISUAL):**
Tracking across the bar’s void—eight patrons, four alive, two lost, one asleep, one debatable.  The bartender’s polish is eternal.  Light: too white, too honest.

**NICK’S TABLE:**
Nick alone, slumped but still upright. Notebook looks abused, dog-eared, half-mashed.  He accepts the house draft. He didn’t ask for it. He doesn’t mind.

**INSERT – NOTES:**
- *Occupancy: 8%*
- *Revenue: “theoretical at best”*
- *Existential dread: palpable*
- *Band: full set. No shortcuts. No grumbling.*

**NICK (V.O.):**
Nobody puts this test in the brochure. Not the festival. Not the sold-out night.  This is the graveyard shift of the music business. Where you learn who’s bluffing, and who’s addicted.

He watches—Kathy giving it everything, Gilley soloing like the walls are full, Bill sweating through his shirt.  Nobody phones it in. Nobody looks for the door.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Here’s the truth: Weekend warriors bail when it rains. Lifers play through the drought.  Minimal viability isn’t about the crowd. It’s about never giving up the setlist.

He checks his notes. Three songs extra.  No complaints, no shortcuts.

**(CAMERA POV):**
One man at the bar flicks a peanut shell, unimpressed.  Nick clicks his stopwatch. For the first time tonight, he grins.

**NICK (V.O.):**
They passed. God help me, that’s all it takes.

---

## **THE ROWDY CROWD: BEHAVIORAL ANALYSIS**

**INT. THE PIT – TOLEDO, OH – NIGHT**

There’s a line out front. There’s carnage inside.  Between them: the full moon, the sweat, the charge in the air—ready to turn the stage into kindling.

**(SOUND):**
Bass slamming off cinderblock.  Glass shattering, metal chairs doubling as percussion.  Laughter, jeers, a bottle ricochets and explodes.

**(VISUAL):**
The camera swims in strobe and sweat, catching a shirt in flight, bodies colliding.  Nick sits at the eye of the storm, calm as a bookie, notes flying.

**INSERT – NICK’S NOTEBOOK:**
- Intoxication index: 9.3/10
- Volatility: “fluid, potentially explosive”
- Fight clock: running
- Viral potential: “disturbingly high”

**STAGE LEFT:**
Kathy’s vocals spike, riding the room’s madness.  Jim’s hitting like he wants to break something—cymbal blows out, nobody misses a beat.  The crowd howls.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Crowd dynamics: herding cats, if the cats were half-naked, hammered, and maybe missing parole.

**11 MINUTES, 42 SECONDS:**
Push, spill, shove—fight erupts right on time.
Nick marks it, almost bored. Took longer than expected.

**STAGE CENTER:**
Gilley clocks the fight—doesn’t blink.  Leans into the mic, dry as dust:

**GILLEY** (deadpan):
Let’s all take a breath and remember—we’re here to *love* each other. Or at least keep it above the belt.

Room laughs, some groans, energy pivots.  He hammers into the next riff—crowd follows.

**NICK (V.O.):**
That’s command. Not by yelling, but by daring the room to follow his tempo instead of their fists.

**CAMERA SWEEP:**
The brawl fizzles. The pulse returns.  Bodies move—not to fight, but to music.

**INSERT—NOTEBOOK:**
*Command* (underlined).

**NICK (V.O.):**
You don’t just survive a crowd like this.  You own it.

---

## **THE IMPROMPTU JAM SESSION: UNEXPECTED DATA**

**INT. CANAL STREET TAVERN – DAYTON, OH – VERY LATE NIGHT**

The show’s long over. What’s left isn’t a crowd—it’s the afterglow.  Nick hunches in the corner, half-lit, notebook resting easy, as if the night might take notes on him, too.

**(SOUND):**
Acoustic strings stretching into tune.  Pint glasses clinking, voices blending with last-call hush.  A tambourine keeping time for nobody in particular.

**(VISUAL):**
Soft gold and tobacco haze.  Kathy barefoot, Gilley strapping on a battered Strat, Jim tapping out jazz-funk on a pint glass.  Jeremy rides a bassline thick as river fog.  Locals join—one in a battered Stooges shirt, another in steel-toed boots and hope.

**NICK (V.O.):**
This isn’t data you can schedule. This is jazz in the machine—joy as method, the mess as the metric.

**INSERT—NICK’S NOTES:**

- Improvisation: “innate, playful”
- Style blending: “fearless, not precious”
- Social cohesion: “unforced”
- Jam start: 1:17 A.M.
- Time now: 2:43 A.M.
- Audience retention: “83% (Red’s dog doesn’t count)”

They roll from blues into something psychedelic and messy, Kathy harmonizing with a local folkie in a Bauhaus tee, Gilley grinning like he’s home.  Jeff’s trading licks with a dude who probably did acid at Monterey Pop.

**NICK (V.O.):**
You don’t plan for this. It’s not on any checklist.  You just have to see it, and know it’s the thing.

Nick’s posture changes: notebook still open, but now forgotten.  He’s not analyzing, just—witnessing.  Remembering why he does this job, and who he’d be if he ever forgot.

**SLOW PAN:**
The last notes ring.  Room exhales.  Kathy raises her glass. Gilley bows, grinning.  Someone cheers. Someone else just sighs, content.

Nick underlines one phrase, almost sheepish, almost grateful.

**INSERT—NOTEBOOK:**
This is why we sign bands.

Just offscreen, a flash of a newcomer’s face—watching from the bar, a red spiral notebook under her arm. Sarah, but not named yet. Not Nick’s problem…until it is.

---

## **CROSSCHECKING: COMPARING NOTES**

**INT. INDIE MUSIC CLUB – INDIANAPOLIS, IN – NIGHT**

A tight, low-ceiling box with more attitude than wattage.  Exposed brick, condensation on the ductwork, stage barely a foot off the sticky dance floor.  A room built for making—or breaking—reputations.

**(SOUND):**
Muted bass, glasses clinking, crowd chatter.  Commuted on stage—looser, louder, hungry.

**(VISUAL):**
Camera glides over a crowd dense with hope and skepticism:  bands with crossed arms, college radio nerds, curious scene kids.  Then lands on *two* note-takers, one at each side of the house.

**NICK STEWART:**
Jacket off, sleeves up, pen tapping a beat—old-school confidence, no wasted movement.

**[[5.3 Sarah Malcolm|SARAH]]:**
Straight from NYU, but hiding the nerves.  Leather notebook, red pen, sharp blazer over jeans—watching everything, *especially* what Nick ignores.

**NICK (V.O.):**
She catches what I miss.  I see what she doesn’t know to value—yet.  Double coverage, same game.

Gilley launches into a solo that sounds like he’s playing three guitars at once—possibly by accident.

**SARAH** (dry, notebook open, not looking up):
“He’s either brilliant…or stoned.”

**NICK** (without missing a beat):
“Not mutually exclusive.”

**INSERT – NICK’S NOTES:**
- Crowd: 82
- Song lengths: inconsistent
- Set pacing: loose, pulls you in
- Acoustics: middling, but energy covers the gaps

**INSERT – SARAH’S NOTES:**
- Kathy: frontwoman, needs polish
- Gilley: “chaos, but watch him”
- Fashion: “Grunge before grunge, plus thrift-store rhinestones”

During break, they migrate to a corner by the faded merch table.  Red wine in cheap plastic.  Whispers just above the hum.

**SARAH (V.O.):**
He plays by feel.  I run the numbers.  But even a spreadsheet knows the story isn’t always in the stats.

**SARAH** (raising an eyebrow, pen as pointer):
“Kathy’s the one. Give her a stylist and a little vocal coaching? Whole damn package.”

**NICK** (nods):
“She keeps them in orbit. Can’t buy that.”

They swap notebooks, scan, nod.

**SARAH** (smiling):
“We might just agree.”

**NICK** (toasting, almost surprised):
“Miracles happen.”

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Back to the stage—second set.  Commuted, suddenly tighter, sharper.  Nick and Sarah, both pens at the ready.  Two scouts, one target, the band in their crosshairs.

---

## **THE DIFFERENT PERSPECTIVES: CONFLICTING DATA**

**INT. UPSCALE BAR & VENUE – COLUMBUS, OH – NIGHT**

This is not a dive.  House lights soft as butter. Cocktails with names and garnish.  A stage so polished you could check your eyeliner in it.

**(SOUND):**
Crystal-clear mix, glassware clinks, a sax solo slips under idle bar chatter.  Even the applause is polite—measured, never rowdy.

**(VISUAL):**
Nick and Sarah at a small round table, backs almost touching but looking at the stage from angles as different as their philosophies.

Cut between their notebooks:

**INSERT – NICK’S NOTES:**
- “Timing on ‘It Has a Wow Finish’: off by five seconds. Kathy covers—solid pivot.”
- “Jeremy pedal fix mid-verse—professional.”
- “Bridge/chorus structure: tighter than Dayton.”

**INSERT – SARAH’S NOTES:**
- “Gilley’s hair: ‘haunted prom date’—needs stylist.”
- “Kathy: star quality. Wardrobe? Thrift store, heavy on the rebellion.”
- “Audience connection: weak. No eye contact. Introspective.”

**NICK (V.O.):**
They’re musicians, not mannequins.  Nobody ever asked The Clash to color-coordinate.

**SARAH (V.O.):**
You don’t sell records to musicians. You sell them to dreamers.  No one buys a poster of a band that looks like Wednesday morning.

**DURING SET BREAK:**
Sarah angles her notebook toward Nick, a half-grin daring him to challenge her.

**SARAH:**
“They sound like pros. But they look like they got dressed in the dark—twice.”

**NICK:**
“Would you prefer eyeliner and dance moves? This isn’t New Kids on the Block.”

**SARAH:**
“I’d prefer polish. Presence. Something that says they belong on a magazine cover, not just a playlist.”

**NICK:**
“That tight turnaround between chorus and bridge? That’s the real presence.”

They exchange a look—not quite irritation, more like respect with a dash of “we’re not there yet.”

**(VISUAL):**
After the show:  Sarah  the bar, stopwatch in her hand, tracking how long Kathy lingers with fans.  Nick at a distance, arms folded, watching the band crack up over a gear mishap.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Subjectivity. Like static on a clean feed.  You learn to work around it—or learn from it.

**SARAH (V.O.):**
Tight sets are great, but no one hums a bassline in their sleep.  They remember the feeling. The look. The presence.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
The band pushes their battered gear out to the van under the soft neon “CRAFT BEER & KARAOKE” sign.  Nick and Sarah each close their notebooks—satisfied, unresolved.  Two scouts, two visions, one target.

Tonight?  The music’s tight.  The brand is still a question mark.

---

## **ON TOP OF THE JOB**

**INT. CLUB – GREEN ROOM – NIGHT**

**GILLEY** leans against the faux-brick, beer in hand, grin at half-mast—the kind of confidence that only comes from a total lack of self-doubt. Across from him, **Sarah Malcolm**—newly-minted analyst, professional, unflappable—meets his banter with an arched eyebrow and an actual laugh.

**(VISUAL):**
Extreme close-up: Sarah’s lips parting in a slow, genuine smile.  Gilley’s finger tracing the rim of his bottle.  Their conversation is a low hum, just under the static of the after-show room.

**(SOUND):**
Muted thump of a closing amp case. Glasses clinking. Sarah’s laugh—quick, bright, just slightly surprised.

### **CUT TO:**

**INT. HOTEL – HALLWAY – EARLY MORNING**

Harsh yellow light. Silence, except for the whir of the vending machine.

**GILLEY** emerges from a room, hair a disaster, t-shirt one size too small (not his), shoes in hand. He closes the door with the care of a man sneaking past a sleeping dragon.

**(VISUAL):**
A single, manicured hand waves lazily from under crisp sheets.  Sarah’s silhouette barely visible, a tangle of hair and satisfied anonymity.

### **CUT TO: ACROSS THE HALL – NICK’S HOTEL ROOM – DOOR AJAR**

**Nick Stewart**, fully dressed, coffee in hand, leans in his doorway. He watches the parade, sighs like a man who’s seen it all and still can’t believe it.

He writes, deadpan:

**INSERT – NICK’S NOTES:**
- *“Extracurricular activity: observed.*
- *Duration: 7h12m.*
- *Potential effect on cohesion: unknown. Possible scenario: drama.*
- *Plan B: poach a rhythm guitarist from the openers?”*

**NICK (V.O.):**
There’s no spreadsheet formula for what happens when libido meets logistics.  But maybe there should be.

**NICK** (dry, muttering):
“Day one, Gilley. Of course.”

**GILLEY (V.O.):**
Hey, I was just being friendly.  She asked about alternate tunings. One thing led to…Well, here we are.

**(VISUAL):**
Slo-mo: Gilley finger-guns at the vending machine.  A can of Mountain Dew drops into his hand—perfect aim, perfect timing.  His hair? Pure chaos. His walk? Pure strut.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Nick sips his coffee, taps his notepad, then looks down the hallway as the sun edges up outside.  Sarah’s door closes quietly. Gilley disappears toward the elevator.

**NICK (V.O.):**
*This* wasn’t in the A&R manual. But maybe it should be.

---

## **THE SYNTHESIS**

**INT. INDEPENDENT COFFEE SHOP – DOWNTOWN COLUMBUS – LATE MORNING**

A corner booth. Strewn with battered notebooks, legal pads, two empty cups, and a pair of mid-level A&R types running on espresso and adrenaline.

**Nick Stewart:** button-down crisp, sleeves rolled, pen like a scalpel.  **Sarah Malcolm:** slouched, relaxed, stylishly messy, her notepad full of looping arrows, lipstick marks, and a page reading:

- KATHY = magnetic.
- GILLEY = dangerous.
- JEREMY’s hair = future liability?

**(VISUAL):**
Wide shot: indie coffee shop—brick walls, Edison bulbs, vinyl on the turntable.
Quick cuts: Sarah’s notepad next to Nick’s graph paper.  A Venn diagram of taste and risk tolerance.

**(SOUND):**
Espresso machine hissing. Spoons clinking. The tick of a quartz watch.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Numbers tell you what happened. But the intangibles? They tell you *why* it matters.

Sarah scans her notes, circles “audience buy-in,” taps her pen.

**SARAH (V.O.):**
They don’t just play shows. They convert people. It’s not clean, but it’s real.

**SARAH** (half-laughing, dry):
I still think “Come Inside Me” needs a new title.

**NICK** (stone-faced):
Eighty percent crowd retention in Cincinnati. That’s better than Pearl Jam in ’91.

**SARAH** (grinning):
Maybe. But try explaining it to a Midwest Walmart buyer.

**NICK** (shrugs):
You don’t explain. You let them hear the hook.

**(Beat. Shared respect. This is the fun part.)**

**NICK (CONT’D):**
Look, we’re not selling polish. We’re selling impact.

**SARAH** (pensively):
So what’s the logline? “Grit with a pulse”? “Smutty but sincere”?

**NICK:**
"Untapped energy. Midwest resonance. Proof of concept at scale. Immediate upside."

**SARAH** (pretending to faint):
That’s the most A&R thing I’ve ever heard.

**NICK:**
It’s what gets you in the door.

**NICK (V.O.):**
They’re rough, yes. But rough is memorable. And memorable pays bills.

**SARAH (V.O.):**
Island doesn’t need more safe bets. They need *risk*. They need a story.

**CUT TO:**

**INT. COFFEE SHOP – PRINTER (SLOW PUSH IN)**

Nick taps “PRINT.”  Pages slide out, crisp and warm.

**Top of the page:**

> **TO: CHRIS BLACKWELL
> RE: POTENTIAL ACQUISITION – COMMUTED**

---

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Nick and Sarah shoulder their bags and walk out.  The morning sun is too bright. The city is waking up.  On the table, two empty cups and a legal pad with “<font color="#ff0000">YES</font>” scrawled in red ink.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Some bets, you just have to make.

---

## **QUANTIFIABLE RESULTS**

**MONTAGE – NIGHT INTO DAY – VARIOUS LOCATIONS**

**Nick Stewart:** In his one-bedroom, a cave of paper, old *Billboard* issues, dog-eared *Bill James Baseball Abstracts*, and a flickering IBM PS/2.

**Sarah Malcolm:** In her Columbus loft, all velvet, posters, thrifted lamps, three coffee mugs, and a wall-sized mood board.

**(VISUALS):**
- **Nick** hammers at his TI-85. Mechanical stopwatch clacks. A bar graph creeps across the screen—*attendance, revenue, applause length*.
- **Sarah** trims a *Spin* magazine, pins a Polaroid of Kathy in full riot-grrl mode next to a lipstick note: “*Sex, noise, and sincerity*.”
- Dot-matrix printer sputters. Old-school spreadsheets crawl onto green-and-white striped paper.
- Nick’s post-its: “**Bogart’s: 31% net revenue jump.**” Circled, starred.
- Sarah’s mood board: *Boots, ripped flag, Kathy’s silhouette, “Nostalgia punk, Midwest sex appeal.”* Early BBS printout: “*Commuted is fire, see them now.*”

---

**(SOUND):**
Dot-matrix whir. Cassette ejects. Pencil taps, calculator beeps, the sigh of exhausted inspiration.

---

**NICK (V.O.):**
Numbers. Pure. Pitiless. They don’t lie—unless you want them to. And I don’t.

**SARAH (V.O.):**
Look is everything. It’s what gets the next set of eyes. Sound makes you stay; image makes you show up.

---

**INT. SHARED MEETING TABLE – AFTERNOON**

A battered table, battered folders. Nick’s tabbed graphs meet Sarah’s collage. No laptops. Just proof.  **Nick** slides a spreadsheet forward—revenue spikes in Columbus.

**NICK**
Thirty-seven percent more spent at the bar after “Wow Finish.” That’s not noise.

**Sarah** holds up a Polaroid—shirtless, bloody-nosed fan, ecstatic.

**SARAH**
And this is why. Brand loyalty, sure. Brand *liability*, definitely. You want chaos, you’ll get it.

**NICK**
Profitable chaos.

**SARAH**
With casualties.

A moment—tension melts into tired grins. It’s real partnership now, not rivalry.

---

**NICK (V.O.):**
We never did speak the same language. But by the end, we wrote the same story.

**SARAH (V.O.):**
His numbers. My myth. That’s how movements start.

---

**(FINAL SHOT):**

A beige laser printer sputters out the summary page:

> **ISLAND RECORDS INTERNAL SCOUTING BRIEF**
> SUBJECT: COMMUTED
> RECOMMENDATION: HIGH PRIORITY — DEVELOPMENT POTENTIAL

Underneath: Two signatures. *Stewart. Malcolm.*

**CUT TO BLACK.**

---

## **THE PITCH REHEARSAL**

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – CONFERENCE ROOM – NYC – DAY**

Glass walls. Too much white. An echo of fluorescent light over everything—no shadows, no secrets. A pitcher of water, untouched. The soundtrack: the nervous hum of Midtown, markers squeaking, the distant thump of car horns below.

**NICK STEWART** stands at the whiteboard, sleeves rolled, hair wild from running hands through it. He scrawls a line graph—**“Regional Attendance”**—and underlines **“Retention > Norm.”**

**NICK** (Pointing to the graph)
They don’t just fill rooms. They convert crowds. Liquor sales up 32% after the opener. Merch line tripled at Bogart’s. That’s sustained interest.

**SARAH MALCOLM** sits, unfazed, sorting acetate slides like tarot cards. She swaps out Nick’s graph for a Polaroid of the crowd—fists up, faces lit by lighter flames.

**SARAH**
Numbers are fine. But this? (tapping the photo) This is what the market buys. They’re not just a sound—they’re an aesthetic. A movement.

Nick wipes his hand on his tie, leaving a faint smear of red marker.

**NICK**
I can’t put “aesthetic” in a spreadsheet, Sarah.

**SARAH**
But you can sell it. Especially if the spreadsheet says it’s scalable.

**(TENSION):**
They circle—Nick on data, Sarah on myth. Two strategies, one target. The clock ticks. The projector hums.

**SARAH (V.O.):**
You have to sell the dream. You have to make them believe.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Best data in the world’s nothing if you can’t make them care.

A beat.

**NICK**
Let’s lead with the numbers. Then I’ll set you up for the closer.

**SARAH** (Grinning)
Deal. But I want the last word.

**NICK**
Wouldn’t dream of it any other way.

Sarah lays out her closing slide: a freeze-frame of fifteen thousand fists raised to the “Let It Go” chant. She jots a sticky note:  *This is what a movement looks like.*

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Camera slowly backs out as Nick paces, rehearsing financials, while Sarah cues up a boombox with a live cassette—**“Come Inside Me”** blaring, their voices layered over the music, sharpening the pitch with each pass. Their outlines blur against the glass—two minds, one argument, one chance.

---

## **TITLE CARD:**

***THE PITCH IS READY.***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – EXECUTIVE BOARDROOM – NYC – DAY**

A cathedral of commerce—chrome, leather, and ten million dollars’ worth of skyline. The table is long enough to land a jet. The execs look bored, until Nick starts talking.

**(SOUND):**
Just the hiss of HVAC, the hum of Manhattan traffic outside, and the quiet drama of pages turning.

**NICK** (clicking remote, projecting a spike on a chart)
This is the audience curve. Five cities. Seventy-one percent net gain in six weeks. Every time they play “*Come Inside Me*,” bar sales spike. Every. Time.

He lets that linger. A few execs exchange glances. The numbers are real.

**NICK (V.O.):**
Not a slam dunk. But the rim is rattling.

Sarah slides in, flipping the easel to her collage—photos, flyers, the tactile evidence of underground hype.

**SARAH**
They’re not just a band. They’re an *idea*, caught right before it goes supernova. They sell out rooms on word-of-mouth alone.

She pins a Polaroid: fans chanting, fists raised.

**SARAH (V.O.):**
We planted the seed. Now we watch who gets out of the way.

A white-haired exec scribbles on a legal pad. A young one, half-joking, mouths “Seventy-one?” again. Someone checks the time—but doesn’t leave.

**CUT TO: PIE CHART ON SCREEN**
Revenue per capita—Commuted vs. median. Nick stands tall.

**NICK**
We tracked them in bars, clubs, dives. In one week, they played to six and sixteen hundred—and played both like they were Wembley.

**EXECUTIVE #1** (cool, direct)
So they’re rough. No track record. Why risk scale?

Beat. Nick leans in—low, steady.

**NICK**
Because when the house is empty, they *play harder*. You don’t teach that. You sign it before someone else does.

Sarah, poised, closes:

**SARAH**
They’re not a problem to fix. They’re a story to tell. Just turn up the volume.

**(VISUAL):**
Wide shot—the whole table leans forward. A suit lowers his glasses. Another flips to the final page. Someone smiles, barely.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Nick and Sarah exchange a quiet nod—battle-worn, but knowing they stuck the landing.

---

## **TITLE CARD:**

***Decision Pending…***

---

**INT. ISLAND RECORDS – BOARDROOM – DAY**

No frills. No wasted movement. Just sunlight on polished glass and the hum of a room where history gets made. **Chris Blackwell** sits at the head of the table. Executives flank him—each one a gatekeeper.

**(VISUAL):**

- Sharp cuts: Nick and Sarah moving in sync, each slide, each graph, each photo of Commuted landing like a well-thrown dart.
- Blackwell, inscrutable behind his yellow legal pad, makes notes with a Montblanc. He’s watching. Really watching.

**(SOUND):**
The hum of the projector, the tap of pen on paper, the soft swell of instrumental music underscoring the moment.

**NICK (V.O.)**
This was the moment. The real one. Not the stage, not the bar, not the road. The room where futures get decided.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL** (leaning forward, voice even but iron-edged)
So…why haven’t we signed them already? Sounds like we’re missing the train.

**NICK** (quiet, measured)
Their manager…refused to talk to me.

**(FLASHBACK):**
Cremeans, face shadowed, handing over a battered business card.

**CREMEANS** (firm, unblinking)
I only talk to principals.

Back to the boardroom.

**NICK** (with new confidence)
That’s what he said. “I only talk to principals.”

**(VISUAL):**
Blackwell’s eyebrows lift—an executive’s poker tell.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL** (almost amused, almost impressed)
Is he mad? Stupid? Or just…absolutely sure of his hand?

**(CUTAWAY):**
Nick and Sarah exchange a micro-glance—one heartbeat of total agreement.

**NICK** (with a small smile)
Absolutely sure, sir.

**SARAH** (without a blink)
He’s running the table.

Blackwell pivots to Sarah—his gaze, the final test.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL**
Sarah. Honest opinion. Leave out the hotel story.

**(CUTAWAY):**
A micro-flash—Sarah’s silhouette in the hotel room, a ghost of a grin, then back to her composed, professional posture.

**SARAH** (steady, direct)
With respect, sir, I think we’d be making a mistake not to go after them. They’ve got the material, the hunger, the right kind of crazy. And their manager? He knows exactly how to play this game.

**CHRIS BLACKWELL** (last turn, to Nick)
Nick. Final word.

**NICK** (no hesitation, all conviction)
This is the most important band since U2. And the first one that feels inevitable.

**(VISUAL):**
Extreme close-up on Blackwell. Still, silent, then a long, low whistle. It hangs in the air.

**(SOUND):**
That whistle, as the music rises behind it.

**(WIDE SHOT):**
Every exec in the room is suddenly awake—leaning forward, reevaluating. The balance has shifted.

**NICK (V.O.):**
It wasn’t a “yes.” But it wasn’t a “no.” It was the sound of the door opening.

**(FINAL SHOT):**
Blackwell, notepad closed, eyes sharp and hungry.

---

## **INT. ISLAND RECORDS BOARDROOM - CONTINUOUS**

The air has a weight to it now. The buzz of fluorescent lights. The distant throb of Manhattan traffic. At the head of the polished boardroom table, CHRIS BLACKWELL leans back in his chair, fingers steepled, eyes locked in a thousand-yard stare that cuts through time and markets.

**(SOUND):** The low, electronic *beep* of a speakerphone being activated. The faint hum of a powerful machine waiting for instruction.

**(VISUAL):** Extreme close-up on Blackwell’s hand—weathered, decisive—as it presses the smooth black button of the speakerphone. Power as choreography.

**DISBODIED VOICE (V.O.)** 
Yes, Mr. Blackwell?

**BLACKWELL** (V.O.):
*In this business, hesitation is death. You move fast. Or you miss everything.*

**BLACKWELL (into speakerphone)**
I need three first-class tickets to Dayton. Friday morning.

**(VISUAL):**
Cut to Sarah. Her pen freezes mid-note. Nick blinks once. No sound. No movement. Just the shift of history underfoot.

**DISBODIED VOICE (V.O.):**
Confirming…three first-class tickets to Dayton…departing Friday morning.

**NICK** (V.O.):
Friday morning. That was fast. Then again—so’s lightning.

**SARAH** (V.O.):
We just set something in motion. Something really big.

Blackwell leans forward, his elbows on the table. For the first time, he actually *smiles*.

**BLACKWELL**
We’re going to see a show.

**(VISUAL):** Close-up on Blackwell’s face. The skin around his eyes creases. This is a man who *knows*. Knows when to strike. Knows what it looks like when lightning hits a garage band.

The camera pulls back. The table. The executives. Nick and Sarah. The skyline visible beyond the glass. They’re all tiny players now, dwarfed by the decision that just got made.

**(FINAL SHOT):** The frame pulls even farther back. The boardroom fades into a stylized map of the United States. A glowing red line traces a route from New York City to Dayton, Ohio. The words scrawl across the screen:

**FRIDAY.**

**(SOUND):**
One final, thunderous chord of music. Then dead silence.

---

# **FIN.**
